# Past Actions Bearing on the 90 Overtures to the 53rd PCA General Assembly (2026)

For each of the 90 overtures before the 53rd General Assembly, this document lists the **past actions
that bear on it**: SJC/CJB **judicial cases**, **constitutional inquiries** and CCB **overture/amendment
advice**, **prior overtures**, and **RPR exceptions of substance**. Each entry also captures what the
overture does and any prior action it cites in its own grounds.

**Basis.** Every citation is drawn either from the overture's own PDF (pcaga.org) or from a searchable
corpus of all PCA General Assembly minutes, **1973–2025 (GA1–GA52)** — the judicial-case index (647
SJC/CJB cases), the constitutional-inquiry catalogue, the CCB overture-advice catalogue, the overture
catalogue (~2,028 proposals with dispositions and ratification status), and the RPR exceptions catalogue
(5,941 threaded exceptions of substance, GA18–52). Each finding was cross-searched by **both** the
provision number and the underlying topic; ⭐ marks recent (GA48–52 / 2021–2025) overtures.

**How to read a citation.** Judicial cases are by docket number + parties (e.g. *2024-18 Harris v.
Wisconsin*); inquiries/CCB advice by GA + CCB section; overtures as **GA<N> O<n>** with outcome.
Outcomes for constitutional (BCO) amendments distinguish *Approved & ratified* (final) from *Approved
but not ratified* and *Answered in the negative* (defeated), because a BCO change is only final once
two-thirds of presbyteries ratify and the next GA affirms.

**Coverage of this report:** judicial cases found for 61/90 overtures · inquiries/CCB advice for 82/90 ·
prior overtures for 88/90 · RPR exceptions for 67/90. "None found" is stated honestly where a category
turned up nothing; it does not always mean nothing exists, only that nothing surfaced in this corpus.

**Caveats.** (1) The corpus ends at GA52 (2025); GA53 itself is the present Assembly. (2) BCO sections
were renumbered over the decades — older actions may cite an old number; topic searches mitigate this but
a few deep cuts may be missed. (3) Inquiry/overture *subject titles* are partly machine-generated (~97%
accurate). (4) One user-anticipated item — a constitutional inquiry holding the BCO "silent on who may
serve as clerk" (re O58) — was **not located** in the corpus despite targeted searching; O58 rests on
that asserted silence rather than on a citable ruling.

---

## Thematic clusters (overtures that share a subject and therefore much of their past-action history)

Many of the 90 overtures travel in families. Reading them together is useful because they draw on the
same cases, inquiries, and prior overtures:

- **Judicial process & discipline (BCO 31–46):** O3, O15, O16, O28, O29, O35, O54, O56, O65, O67, O69,
  O75, O85, O86 — appeals vs. complaints, dismissals, the record of the case, indictment timing, counsel.
- **The diaconate (deacons / women deacons / diaconal ministry):** O34, O36, O37, O38, O71 — the PCA's
  most-overtured topic, anchored on the women-in-office history and SJC *2009-25/26 (Brown/Grace v.
  N. Calif.)*.
- **Offices/titles for the unordained & commissioning:** O14, O48, O52, O74 (new BCO 17A) — closely tied
  to the diaconate cluster and to GA50 O26 (BCO 7-3, ratified 2024).
- **BCO 5 — church planting / mission churches:** O2, O17, O18, O19, O20, O51.
- **Consent of the congregation / who exercises authority:** O1, O13, O24, O39, O49, O55, O57, O72, O82, O84.
- **Ordination requirements (BCO 21):** O12, O25 (plus O42 on the 29-1 Standards reference).
- **RAO 4-9 — Stated Clerk / Coordinator terms & election thresholds:** O40, O41, O43, O73, O77.
- **RAO 8-4.i — floor nominations:** O8, O9, O45, O47.
- **RAO 4-21 — electronic meetings:** O78, O79 (and O11 on MNA data).
- **RPR rules & procedure:** O7, O33, O53.
- **AC / committee & agency structure:** O5, O6, O32, O68.
- **Presbytery boundaries:** O10 ⇄ O87 (the same Pittsburgh/Ohio change from both sides), O44, O62, O70.
- **Declarations / thanksgiving / prayer:** O4, O50, O61 (Danvers), O66 / O76 / O89 (250th anniversary).
- **Ad interim committees on cultural issues:** O80 (CRT) and O90 (Christian Nationalism).
- **The Lord's Supper:** O31 ⇄ O60 (who distributes the elements), O81 (wine + grape juice at GA).

---

## O1 — Amend BCO 23-1 on Associate/Assistant Pastors Succeeding Senior Pastor
**Targets:** BCO 23-1 (title/file also says 23-2, but the operative text amends only 23-1; rationale also cites 16-1, 16-2, 21-1) · **Source:** Potomac · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/Overture-1_Potomac_23-2.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/Overture-1_Potomac_23-2.pdf)

**What it does:** Lowers the bar for an associate/assistant pastor to succeed the senior pastor without an intervening term in a different field of labor: replaces the current 4/5 congregational secret-ballot petition + 3/4 presbytery vote with a simpler congregational petition that the presbytery may grant by a 2/3 vote, on a finding that the prior dissolution "was brought about in Christian love and good order."

**Cites in its own grounds:** No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by number. Cites WCF 1:6, BCO 16-1/16-2 and 21-1, and refers generally to "an earlier form of this provision [that] made the restriction absolute" and "the current form [that] was an improvement" — i.e., the GA12 (1984/85) succession-by-exception amendment listed below.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-5 — Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-05.md)** (GA52/2025, granted) — only spine case construing BOTH 23-1 and 23-2; most on-point judicial treatment of the associate-relations provisions O1 touches. [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p983)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.S** (GA52/2025, in conflict & ambiguous) — CCB found proposed amendments to BCO 8-4, 20-1, 21-1, 21-12, **23-1** (TE relationships for needful work) in conflict; most recent CCB read on amending 23-1's relations framework. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci19.md)
- **II.Y** (GA51/2024, not in conflict, 8-0) — CCB cleared a proposed 23-1 amendment (presbytery exit interview before dissolution); directly on point as the CCB's standard for amending this very section. [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci25.md)
- **II.D** (GA47/2019, not in conflict; adopted) — CCB cleared Central Indiana's 23-1 dissolution-procedure amendment; shows the CCB passing prior 23-1 edits. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci04.md)
- **CI #13** (GA14/1986, advice given) — early advice on the associate/assistant-relations side of the chapter (calling an assistant pastor; presbyterial examination required). [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci16.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA12 O4](../overtures/ga12_1984__o4.md)** (1985, Approved & ratified) — "Amend BCO 23-1 to Allow Associate Pastor to Succeed Senior Pastor by Presbytery Exception" (Southern Florida). THE direct predecessor: created the current exception O1 now seeks to loosen; the rationale's "current form was an improvement" refers to this. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p49)
- **[GA12 O29](../overtures/ga12_1984__o29.md)** (1984/85) — "Amend BCO 23-1 Regarding Associate Pastors Succeeding Senior Pastors" (Delmarva). Companion attempt at the same GA on the identical question. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p54)
- **[GA12 O49](../overtures/ga12_1984__o49.md)** (1984/85) — "Amend BCO 23-1 to Allow Associate Pastors to Succeed Senior Pastors by Petition" (West Hopewell session). Another companion succession-by-petition proposal. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p62)
- **[GA10 O16](../overtures/ga10_1982__o16.md)** (1983, Approved & ratified) — "Require Presbytery Approval Before Minister Leaves Pastoral Field" (Ascension). Same chapter, adjacent question (leaving the field); context for the succession rule's origin. [page](../markdown/ga10_1982.md#ga10-p47)
- **[GA51 O30](../overtures/ga51_2024__o30.md)** (2024, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 23-1 to Require Presbytery Exit Interview Before Dissolution of Call" (Lowcountry). ⭐ Recent 23-1 amendment attempt (different question — dissolution, not succession); shows current GA caution on amending 23-1. [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1183)
- **[GA47 O5](../overtures/ga47_2019__o5.md)** (2019, Approved → sent to presbyteries) — "Amend BCO 23-1 on Procedures for Dissolving Various Pastoral Relations" (Central Indiana). Recent successful-at-GA 23-1 amendment; precedent for amending the section. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p593)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 23-1** — 308 spine citations across presbyteries (e.g., [Southwest Florida](../rpr/southwest-florida.md) 30th/2002: "No record of 4/5 congregational vote for change in call from associate to senior pastor. BCO 23-1"; [Potomac](../rpr/potomac.md) 52nd/2025). The vast majority are dissolution-procedure (missing congregational concurrence) findings — incidental to succession — but they document heavy, ongoing real-world friction under 23-1, and a few (e.g., the Southwest Florida 4/5-vote item) bear directly on the succession supermajority O1 would change. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 23-2** — 3 citations ([Eastern Pennsylvania](../rpr/eastern-pennsylvania.md) 48th/2021 retired-vs-associate status; [Missouri](../rpr/exc/missouri__055.md) 50th/2023 & 51st/2024). Incidental: O1 does not in fact amend 23-2. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Pruned as incidental: **2023-11 Psiaki v. Pacific Northwest** cites 23-1 in passing but concerns *voting eligibility in officer elections* (BCO 6-4 territory), not pastoral-relations succession — not bearing. **2022-20 Wilson v. Pacific Northwest** was dismissed as judicially out of order (BCO 43-1) because the complaint targeted actions of a congregational meeting, not a court; 23-1 appears only as background (the congregation was voting whether to accept an associate pastor's resignation), but the case construes no aspect of the succession rule O1 targets. **2015-12 Wills v. Metro Atlanta** (GA44/2016, dismissed) was about complaint procedure under BCO 43-2 and does not cite BCO 23-1 in its text at all; the spine hit reflected minutes context, not a substantive 23-1 holding. The title/filename reference 23-2 but the operative amendment touches **only 23-1**, so the 23-2 spine cases (Bigelow excepted, since it also cites 23-1) and the 3 23-2 RPR rows are not bearing. The bulk of the ~308 23-1 RPR rows and the older spine cases — Wuckovich/McLeod (GA12), CI #1 (GA16), Nickoley (GA20), 92-5 / 31-3 / Roberts (GA21), 2001-34 / Nichols & Couch (GA33), Evans 2023-7, Moehn 2024-1, Gleason 2024-2 — all construe **dissolution procedure / congregational concurrence**, not the associate→senior **succession** rule O1 targets. Likewise pruned inquiries/CCB items on dissolution or TE voting (16-77 GA16, 23-15 GA23, 26-68 GA26; 17-82 GA17, 31-56 GA31, 32-40 GA32). No renumbering: BCO 23 has carried this number throughout (no chapter-23 entry in bco_renumberings.jsonl), so there is no "old number" to search. Companion GA53 overtures on assistant/associate pastors (note cross-links, not duplicated here): O39 (BCO 22 consent for assistant pastors), O55 (22-3/23-1 tenure of assistant pastors), O64 (23-2 associate membership for retired TEs). O1's true predecessors are the GA12 succession overtures; the GA47/GA51 items set the modern bar for amending 23-1.

---

## O2 — Amend BCO 5-4 for Consent of Mission Church Members in Calling a Pastor
**Targets:** BCO 5-4 · **Source:** Wisconsin · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/Overture-2_Wisconsin_5-4.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/Overture-2_Wisconsin_5-4.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a proviso to BCO 5-4: when members have already been received into a mission church (per BCO 5-5) at the time Presbytery calls a minister to serve as pastor under 5-4.a, those members must consent to the pastor by a majority vote at a BCO-25 congregational meeting, and that consent must be reported to Presbytery before it calls the pastor.

**Cites in its own grounds:** Preliminary Principle 6 (BCO Preface); M38GA (2010) Overture 15, footnote i (pp. 401f) — the chapter-5 rewrite establishing that a mission church should mirror a particular church's practices.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-5 — Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-05.md)** (GA52/2025, granted) — Squarely on point. The SJC reviewed the dissolution of a planting/assistant pastor's call to a mission church and held, construing BCO 5-4 and 5-5, that **no congregational vote of the mission church was constitutionally required** in the pastoral relationship. That holding is the exact gap O2 seeks to close by requiring existing members' consent. [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p983)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found.

### Prior overtures
- **[GA38 O15](../overtures/ga38_2010__o15.md)** (2010, Approved & ratified 2011) — Potomac's "Revise BCO 5-2 Through 5-11 and Add New BCO 5-5 Regarding Church Organization" created the current 5-4 / 5-5 framework O2 now amends; O2 cites its footnote i in its own grounds. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p368)
- **[GA38 O11](../overtures/ga38_2010__o11.md)** (2010, Approved & ratified 2011) — Blue Ridge's "Amend BCO 5-3 to Allow Latitude in Oversight of Mission Churches" addressed the same chapter-5 temporary-government scheme O2's whereas-clauses invoke. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p356)
- **[GA08 O15](../overtures/ga08_1980__o15.md)** (1980, Approved & ratified 1981) — Mid-Atlantic's "Add BCO 5-4 on calling pastors in new congregations" originally created the very section O2 amends. [page](../markdown/ga08_1980.md#ga08-p40)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 5-4** — 3 citations on this provision. Decisively, **Wisconsin Presbytery (O2's own sponsor)** was cited for exception at GA49 (2022, unsatisfactory/outstanding) and again at GA51 (2024, raised/open) because "the nature of provision for pastoral ministry for a mission church not clearly defined" — the precise real-world friction prompting this overture. (The third row, [Siouxlands](../rpr/exc/siouxlands__040.md) 28th/2000 on organization procedure citing BCO 5-4..5-8, is incidental and pruned.) [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
The exact-provision spine returned only Bigelow 2024-5; no inquiries, no CCB advice, and an empty prior_overtures list (no past overture cited "5-4" verbatim). The three prior overtures above come from the topical chapter-5 supplement (the index OVERTURES.md). The first pass cited cases 2022-7 and 2020-6 and a GA44 CCB-advice item that do NOT appear in the join's hit-list and lacked real deep-links — those are dropped. The Siouxlands RPR row is pruned as incidental. No renumbering of BCO chapter 5 since the 2011 ratification of the GA38 O15 rewrite (which is the live numbering), so no old-number search was warranted; the only caveat is that pre-2011 "5-5" citations predate the inserted member-reception section. GA53 companion: **O18** (Westminster) also amends BCO 5-4 — to let a mother church call a church planter — so O2 (consent of existing members) and O18 are companion 5-4 overtures the Assembly will weigh together. Both O2 and O18 were referred to CCB, OC, and MNA. The Bigelow minutes link is used because the join supplied no case_page.

---

## O3 — Amend BCO 32-20 and 32-21 Regarding Dismissing Charges
**Targets:** BCO 32-20, new BCO 32-21 · **Source:** NY State · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/Overture-3_NY-State_32.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/Overture-3_NY-State_32.pdf)

**What it does:** Changes 32-20 from permissive ("the court **should** consider...") to mandatory ("the court **shall** consider the gravity of the alleged offense as well as what degradations of evidence and memory may have occurred"), and inserts a new 32-21 barring dismissal of any charge without a hearing where both parties argue dismissal, requiring that memory-based dismissals interview each witness with a ruling on recall, and that the court record its reasons for any dismissal — so that neglecting these steps becomes "clear error."

**Cites in its own grounds:** **SJC Case 2024-18** (GA52/2025) — the rationale states the SJC "could not overturn a presbytery decision to dismiss in the absence of clear error on this point," but "both concurring and dissenting opinions noted the deficiency of the procedure the presbytery used." O3 is the direct legislative response.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-18 — Harris v. Wisconsin Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-18.md)** (GA52/2025, denied) ⭐ — THE case O3 cites in its grounds. SJC denied a prosecutor's complaint against a presbytery JC's 8-0 dismissal of both indictments; the dissent argued the presbytery *clearly erred*. O3 hard-codes the considerations whose neglect the dissent flagged. [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1037)
- **[2022-4 — Sheppard v. Highlands Presbytery](../cases/ga50_2023__2022-04.md)** (GA50/2023, sustained) ⭐ — construes 32-20 in the pretrial dismissal/process posture O3 regulates. [minutes](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p833)
- **[1993-10 — Clark v. Southwest Presbytery](../cases/ga23_1995__1993-10.md)** (GA23/1995, not sustained) — early SJC construction of 32-20 on objecting to consideration of a charge. [minutes](../markdown/ga23_1995.md#ga23-p102)
- **[1995-10 — Merriam v. Tennessee Valley Presbytery](../cases/ga25_1997__1995-10.md)** (GA25/1997, remanded) — 32-20 in the charge-consideration/dismissal frame; remanded for further process. [minutes](../markdown/ga25_1997.md#ga25-p76)
- **[2007-16 — Grady v. Southwest Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga37_2009__2007-16.md)** (GA37/2009, sustained in part) — 32-20 construed on handling of charges; bears on the court's duty before dismissal. [minutes](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p166)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.O** (GA48/2021, not in conflict; Adopted) ⭐ — CCB cleared Overture 22 (Pacific NW) amending 32-20 to govern the *time* considerations for prosecuting offenses — the very rewrite that produced today's 32-20 language O3 now makes mandatory. [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci15.md)
- **App. O II.D** (GA41/2013, not in conflict) — CCB on Suncoast Florida's proposed (different) "32-21" defining supporting reasons for a complaint/appeal; not in conflict only "if BCO 32-18 is read as addressing cases in process." Same 32-21 slot O3 now proposes to fill. [page](../inquiries/ga41_2013__ci01.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA48 O22](../overtures/ga48_2021__o22.md)** (2021, Approved & ratified 2022) ⭐ — "Amend BCO 32-20 to Replace One-Year Statute of Limitations for Offenses" (Pacific Northwest). Wrote the current 32-20 ("should consider gravity... degradations of evidence and memory") that O3 converts from permissive to mandatory. [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p999)
- **[GA52 O1](../overtures/ga52_2025__o1.md)** (2025, Answered in the negative) ⭐ — "Review Wisconsin Presbytery Dismissal of Indictment Against Teaching Elder" (Northern New England). Same fact pattern as Case 2024-18; the GA declined review. O3 is the structural-rule response to that episode. [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1050)
- **[GA41 O4](../overtures/ga41_2013__o4.md)** (2013, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 32 by Adding Section 32-21 on Supporting Reasons for Appeal" (Suncoast FL). A prior, defeated attempt to add a 32-21 (different content). [page](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p90)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (The deterministic join returned no Records-of-the-Proceedings-Review exceptions tagged to BCO 32-20 or 32-21.)

### Note
The chain is tight: **GA48 O22 (2021)** wrote current 32-20 → **Case 2024-18 (Harris v. Wisconsin)** applied it permissively and was affirmed despite a criticized procedure → **GA52 O1 (2025)** tried and failed to review that dismissal → **O3** now makes the considerations mandatory and adds 32-21's hearing/witness-interview/record-of-reasons requirements so future neglect is "clear error." The three prior overtures (GA48 O22, GA52 O1, GA41 O4) were found via topical supplement — the provision-exact spine returned prior_overtures=[]. **Pruning:** the spine's 32-20 hit-list is high-recall and heavily incidental — ~22 of the 27 cases (e.g., 1982-2, 1990-8/9, 2007-14, 2010-16/26, 2011-11, 2012-4/8, 2013-1, 2016-5, 2019-7/8, 2020-7/8/9, 2020-14, 2021-11, 2022-5, the 2009-16 administrative item) cite 32-20 in passing within larger disciplinary fights; only the five above squarely construe the charge-consideration/dismissal question O3 amends. Sheppard 2022-4 has no standalone case page in the join, so it is cited via minutes only. No renumbering caveat — chapter 32 is stable across this range (bco_renumberings.jsonl shows no ch.32 entry). Companion GA53 discipline overtures touch adjacent discipline provisions (e.g., 31-2 investigation, 32-18 record of the case); cross-link if those pages exist.

---

## O4 — Docket a Prayer of Thanksgiving for Adult Professions of Faith
**Targets:** (prayer — non-provision overture) · **Source:** Pacific Northwest Presbytery (to OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/10/Overture-4_PNW_Thanksgiving.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/10/Overture-4_PNW_Thanksgiving.pdf)

**What it does:** Asks the 53rd GA to offer a prayer of thanksgiving to God during the Assembly in Louisville for the 5,656 adult professions of faith reported in the PCA Statistical Report; appends a per-presbytery table of churches reporting the most adult professions in 2024.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (Scripture — Luke 15:6-7 — plus the PCA Statistical Report and the 52nd GA Commissioner Handbook pp. 307, 331 for the statistics; no prior GA cases, overtures, inquiries, or BCO provisions).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (A docketed corporate prayer of thanksgiving raises no constitutional/judicial question; the deterministic spine returns no provision and there is no judicial action on point.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CCB II.C** (GA47/2019, not in conflict; adopted by the CCB) — CCB advice on Overture 3 (Northern New England) amending RAO 10-3 to "encourage godly prudence in planning corporate prayer and worship at the General Assembly"; bears as the nearest constitutional treatment of corporate prayer/worship on the Assembly's own docket, though it concerns an RAO amendment rather than a one-time prayer resolution. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci03.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA19 O41](../overtures/ga19_1991__o41.md)** (1991, Adopted (final)) — "Call a Day of Thanksgiving for War Victory" (Heritage Pby, substitute for O16); closest precedent — a GA-adopted corporate prayer/thanksgiving resolution offered by the Assembly itself. [page](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p59)
- **[GA15 O32](../overtures/ga15_1987__o32.md)** (1987) — "Set Aside the First Day of General Assembly for Worship and Prayer" (Southeast Alabama); a prior attempt to commit Assembly docket time to corporate prayer/worship. [page](../markdown/ga15_1987.md#ga15-p40)
- **[GA8 O24](../overtures/ga08_1980__o24.md)** (1980) — "Devote GA time daily to prayer and Bible study" (Louisiana); same genre — using Assembly docket time for corporate prayer. [page](../markdown/ga08_1980.md#ga08-p33)
- **[GA44 O32](../overtures/ga44_2016__o32.md)** (2016, Referred) — "Call Member Churches to a Day of Prayer and Fasting" (James River, to OC); most recent comparable OC-assigned "call to prayer" docket request. [page](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p632)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (No BCO provision is amended, so there is no Record-of-the-Presbyteries exception thread.)

### Note
Non-provision (prayer) overture — the exact-provision spine returns provisions=[], so all bearing actions come from topical search of /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md and CCB-OVERTURE-ADVICE.md. The overture cites nothing in its own grounds. The single on-point precedent is GA19 O41 (a GA-adopted thanksgiving); GA15 O32 and GA8 O24 bear on dedicating Assembly time to corporate prayer/worship. Pruned the "day of prayer for an external cause" overtures (GA2 O1 missions; GA3 O20 fasting; GA14 O49 & GA15 O49 farm crisis; GA22 O25/O34 Korea; GA24 O39 elections) down to one representative (GA44 O32) — those direct prayer *outward by the churches* rather than offering thanksgiving *during the Assembly*, so they bear only on genre, not substance. No ⭐ recent (GA48–52) overtures exist on this topic; the most recent comparable is GA44 (2016). CCB II.C is the nearest constitutional touchpoint but is tangential (an RAO amendment, not a prayer resolution). Cross-link: O4 sits among the GA53 "prayer/thanksgiving" overtures — O50 (Day of Fasting and Prayer) and O66/O76/O89 (Declarations of Thanksgiving for the 250th anniversary) — none of which addresses adult professions of faith.

## O5 — Amend RAO 5-1.a to Stipulate that AC Members Elected by GA Must Be from Different Presbyteries
**Targets:** RAO 5-1.a · **Source:** Pacific Northwest Presbytery · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-5_PNW_RAO5_rev.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-5_PNW_RAO5_rev.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends RAO 5-1.a so that none of the 11 GA-elected Administrative Committee members (nor an alternate) may be elected if there is already a member from the same Presbytery, while allowing a member who later changes Presbyteries to finish his term.

**Cites in its own grounds:** No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries. It cites constitutional/RAO provisions as analogies/support: BCO 15-4 (parallel "different presbyteries" rule for the SJC), BCO 14-1.9 (proportionate representation of all presbyteries "wherever possible"), and RAO 5-4 / RAO 10-1 / RAO 10-8 (AC's unique funding and GA-site authority).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **GA49 CI08 (II.H)** (GA49/2022, not in conflict; adopted by CCB) — CCB found no constitutional conflict in a Westminster overture changing the *membership composition* of the SJC (BCO 15-4, RAO 17-1). Bears as the closest analogue: PNW O5 leans on BCO 15-4's "different presbyteries" rule, and this shows GA may constitutionally restructure a committee's membership composition. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci08.md)
- **GA47 CI07 (II.G)** (GA47/2019, in conflict; adopted by CCB) — CCB held an overture amending BCO 14-1 (membership rules for GA committees/boards, incl. RAO 5-2) was in conflict. Bears as a caution that BCO 14-1 / RAO 5 membership amendments are reviewed for constitutional conflict. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci07.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA52 O9](../overtures/ga52_2025__o9.md)** (2025, Answered in the negative) — James River sought to amend BCO 14-1 to make AC members appointed by committees non-voting; recent attempt to reshape AC membership/voting composition. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p120)
- **[GA32 O10](../overtures/ga32_2004__o10.md)** (2004, Answered in the negative) — Nashville sought to amend BCO 15-4 to *allow* one TE and one RE from the same Presbytery on the SJC — the converse of PNW O5's analogy; the same "same-Presbytery" question for a GA committee. [page](../markdown/ga32_2004.md#ga32-p171)
- **[GA24 O30](../overtures/ga24_1996__o30.md)** (1996, Answered in the negative) — New River's overture to "Remember Proportionate Representation In Nominations and Elections" — the very BCO 14-1.9 proportionality concern O5 raises, previously declined. [page](../markdown/ga24_1996.md#ga24-p54)
- **[GA19 O29](../overtures/ga19_1991__o29.md)** (1991, Answered by reference) — Louisiana's overture to amend RAO/BCO 14-1 to *limit Administrative Committee membership* (spine hit; same subject — capping AC composition). ### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
Companion at this same Assembly: **GA53 O9** (Amend RAO 8-4.i to Highlight Proportionate Representation of Presbyteries by Floor Nominations) directly addresses O5's core grievance — that BCO 14-1.9 proportionality "can easily be overlooked when floor nominations are considered at GA"; the two overtures attack the same problem from different rules. Renumbering caveat: RAO 5 was modified in 2011 (39th GA, new 5-5 inserted with downstream shift), but RAO 5-1 itself is unaffected, so older "RAO V" citations (GA18/GA19) still refer to the AC chapter. Pruning: the spine's lone RPR row (Iowa, 47th GA) construes **BCO 5-1** (composition of *Presbytery*), an incidental chapter-number collision with RAO 5-1 and unrelated to AC membership — pruned. The provision-exact spine returned only GA19 O29; the BCO 15-4 / BCO 14-1.9 analogy overtures and the GA52 AC-composition attempt were recovered by concept search and are the most bearing prior actions.

## O6 — Amend RAO 14-9, 15-8, and add 16-7.h to Require 150 Commissioners to Remove from an Omnibus
**Targets:** RAO 14-9 (14-9.d), RAO 15-8 (15-8.b), new RAO 16-7.h · **Source:** PNW · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/Overture-6_PNW_Omnibus_rev.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/Overture-6_PNW_Omnibus_rev.pdf)

**What it does:** Flips the omnibus ("in gross") procedure across all three reporting tracks (Committees of Commissioners, Overtures Committee, and RPR). Instead of any one commissioner being able to pull an item from the in-gross package for separate vote, the Moderator may put recommendations in gross and an item is removed only if 150 commissioners vote (without debate) in favor of removal. Aim: stop a lone commissioner out of 2,000+ from forcing floor debate on near-unanimous committee recommendations.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — cites only RONR (12th ed.) 12:14 & 51:48.b and, internally, RAO 14-9-h.3 (the 60-minute debate already afforded CoC amendments). No prior case, overture, or inquiry is cited.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (RAO floor procedure for omnibus/in-gross handling is not a subject of SJC adjudication; the provision-exact join returned no case construing RAO 14-9, 15-8, or 16-7.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CCB Advice II.A** (GA50/2023, not in conflict; Adopted 8-0-0) ⭐ — CCB unanimously found James River Presbytery's Overture 3 to limit GA debate via **RAO 14-9.h and 15-8.g** not in conflict with the Constitution. On point: closest precedent that amending the RAO 14-9 / 15-8 floor-debate machinery is constitutionally permissible — the very machinery O6 amends. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci01.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA50 O3](../overtures/ga50_2023__o3.md)** (2023, → CCB found not in conflict; see CCB Adv. II.A above) ⭐ — "Amend RAO 14-9.h and 15-8.g to Limit General Assembly Debate" (James River). Same two RAO sections, same goal of constraining floor debate; the immediate predecessor to O6. [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p969)
- **[GA37 O2](../overtures/ga37_2009__o2.md)** (2009, Adopted final) — "Amend RAO 19-4.d, 14-9.h, and 15-8.g Governing Debate on Minority Reports" (Potomac). Prior adopted amendment to the same 14-9/15-8 debate machinery. [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p57)
- **[GA36 O13](../overtures/ga36_2008__o13.md)** (2008, Adopted final) — "Revise RAO 14-6k; 14-9g; 15-8e; 14-9e; and 15-8c" (Potomac). Earlier adopted structural amendment to the same reporting/debate subsections. [page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p56)
- **[GA40 O9](../overtures/ga40_2012__o9.md)** (2012, Answered in the negative) — "Amend RAO 14-9e to Allow GA to Consider Amendments by Two-Thirds Vote" (Rocky Mountain). Prior (defeated) supermajority-threshold idea in the same RAO 14-9 family. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p87)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (These are GA floor-procedure rules, not presbytery-records provisions; RPR exception scope does not reach RAO 14-9/15-8/16-7. Note O6 *adds* the omnibus mechanism to the RPR report's own presentation via new 16-7.h.)

### Note
RAO-procedure target, so SJC adjudication and RPR exceptions are structurally absent. The deterministic provision-exact spine returned only the GA50 CCB item (nothing incidental to prune). The four prior overtures above are a **topical supplement** (STEP 3c): the spine missed them because it matches at chapter level while these overtures are catalogued by subsection (14-9.h, 15-8.g, etc.) in OVERTURES.md — each is a genuine prior attempt to amend the same RAO 14-9/15-8 debate machinery and carries a verbatim corpus deep-link. This O6 PDF is a PNW Overtures-Commission **revision** (approved Apr 9, 2026) of the Oct 10, 2025 stated-meeting overture. Companion GA53 overtures on the same omnibus/RPR machinery (cross-links, not bearing past actions): **O33** (Westminster — new RAO 16-7.h on minority reports from RPR, overlapping the very subsection O6 adds), **O53** (Great Lakes — RAO 16, bar RPR members from debating the report), **O7** (restructure RPR reporting to keep most items off the floor), and especially **O63** (RAO 19-4 preference in recognition for an objector to an in-gross motion) — the conceptual counterpoint, protecting the lone objector O6 would override. Read O6 together with O33 (same 16-7.h text) and O63.

## O7 — Amend RAO 16 Regarding RPR's Reporting on Presbytery Records
**Targets:** RAO 16-7 (with conforming changes to 16-3.e.(8/9) and 16-4.c.(3)) · **Source:** Pacific Northwest (to CCB, OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/Overture-7_PNW_RPR_rev.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/Overture-7_PNW_RPR_rev.pdf)

**What it does:** Restructures the RPR Committee's reporting so that exceptions of substance and most recommendations are approved by the *Committee* itself (and merely recorded in the report) rather than coming to the GA floor as omnibus recommendations; only a recommendation that a presbytery's *second* response be judged Unsatisfactory (and OMSJC-15 / BCO 40-5 matters) would still come to the Assembly. Purpose: a 2,000-commissioner Assembly cannot meaningfully act on ~500 recommendations in a 215-page report posted 12 days before GA.

**Cites in its own grounds:** RAO 16-8 ("Neither the report of the committee nor the General Assembly's approval or disapproval of this report establishes doctrinal precedent"); RAO 16-10.c; OMSJC 15; BCO 40-5; BCO 13-11, 14-6.c, 40-1 (in the 16-3.e provision). No prior overtures, cases, or CCB rulings are cited by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2010-18/2010-19/2010-20/2010-21/2010-22/2010-23 — Gulfstream Presbytery, Citation re: Review of Presbytery Records / Korean Central Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2010-18_2010-19_2010-20_2010-21_2010-22_2010-23.md)** (GA39/2011, administrative) — The terminal BCO 40-5 escalation when presbyteries fail to respond to RPR; bears because O7 expressly preserves this floor-bound path (second-response-Unsatisfactory / OMSJC 15) while moving routine RPR actions to committee finality. [full text](../cases/ga39_2011__2010-18_2010-19_2010-20_2010-21_2010-22_2010-23.md)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **29-28 III.7 — New River Presbytery** (GA29/2001, advice given) — CCB lacks authority to give unsolicited advice to other committees, but the CRPR "may make any recommendation within its RAO 16 purview to the GA." Construes the scope of what RPR may bring/decide — the very allocation O7 shifts toward committee finality. [page](../inquiries/ga29_2001__ci07.md)
- **32-36 II.2** (GA32/2004, advice given) — A presbytery's BCO 21-4 exception-granting is reviewable by RPR, which "must report apparent violations." Bears on what RPR is obligated to surface vs. dispose of internally. [page](../inquiries/ga32_2004__ci02.md)
- **49 Supplemental II.B** (GA49/2022, not in conflict; adopted by CCB) — CCB found the RPR Committee's own proposed change to RAO 16-4c not in conflict with the Constitution. ⭐ Directly bears: O7 also amends 16-4.c.(3). [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci28.md)
- **51 II.W / O28** (GA51/2024, not in conflict) — CCB found the amendment to RAO 16-6.c.1 eliminating conflict with BCO 40-5 not itself in conflict; touches the same 40-5/RPR escalation interface O7 leaves intact. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci23.md)
- **52 II.W / O34** (GA52/2025, in conflict) — CCB found an overture amending RAO 16 (session/diaconate statistical reporting) in conflict with the BCO; nearest recent precedent for CCB review of an RAO 16 reporting-scope amendment (O7 is referred to CCB). ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci23.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA9 O18](../overtures/ga09_1981__o18.md)** (1981, Adopted final) — Ascension, "Investigate Referring Review of Presbytery Records to a Standing Committee." Original structural debate over whether RPR is a committee vs. commission — exactly O7's framing ("RPR does not need to be a commission of the Assembly"). [page](../markdown/ga09_1981.md#ga09-p47)
- **GA10 — Administration report follow-up on GA9 Overture 18** (1982) — the Committee on Administration's report to the Tenth Assembly on GA9's affirmed Ascension overture (reproducing the Ascension "refer review of presbytery records to a standing committee" text), the GA-level follow-on to the same structural change. (Note: GA10's own numbered Overture 18 is a separate Central Carolina overture on BCO 24-9; this RPR matter is the carried-forward GA9 Overture 18, not a new GA10 overture.) [page](../markdown/ga10_1982.md#ga10-p135)
- **[GA21 O28](../overtures/ga21_1993__o28.md)** (1993, Answered in the negative — RPR had already handled it) — Rocky Mountain, "Unwarranted Requirements on Presbytery Clerks" (asking GA to direct RPR to stop requiring clerks to spell out "M/S/C" and underline books of the Bible). Prior GA pushback on RPR reporting/notation practice. [page](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p56)
- **[GA26 O24](../overtures/ga26_1998__o24.md)** (1998, Answered in the negative) — New Life PC, "Amend RAO 14-7c3 to Require BCO Citations for CRPR Exceptions of Substance." Construes the content of exception-of-substance reporting (O7 retains the scriptural/constitutional-citation requirement at 16-7.2.c.3). [page](../markdown/ga26_1998.md#ga26-p51)
- **[GA34 O3](../overtures/ga34_2006__o3.md)** (2006) — Susquehanna Valley, "Amend RAO 16-1 to Remove Minutes from Assembly Registration Fee." Minor prior RAO 16 amendment. [page](../markdown/ga34_2006.md#ga34-p160)
- **[GA51 O28](../overtures/ga51_2024__o28.md)** (2024, to CCB/OC) — New Jersey, "Amend RAO 16-6.c.1 to Eliminate Conflict with BCO 40-5." ⭐ Recent RAO 16 reform touching the 40-5/RPR escalation O7 preserves. [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1180)
- **[GA52 O34](../overtures/ga52_2025__o34.md)** (2025, Adopted final) — Savannah River, "Amend RAO 16 to Require Reporting on Session and Diaconate Membership and Duties." ⭐ Most recent RAO 16 reporting amendment; GA52 *added* duties where O7 now seeks to *reduce* floor handling. [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1270)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (RPR-BY-PROVISION.md is keyed to substantive BCO/RAO/WCF provisions cited *in* exceptions of substance, not to RAO 16-7 itself — the procedural reporting rule this overture amends. No exception of substance is taken under RAO 16-7. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md))

### Note
Closely related to two companion GA53 overtures on the same RPR/RAO 16 machinery: **O33** (Westminster, RAO 16-7.h minority reports from RPR) and **O53** (Great Lakes, RAO 16, barring RPR members from floor debate on the RPR report). All three respond to the same friction — an unwieldy omnibus RPR report consuming ~105 minutes of GA floor time — and should be read together; O7 itself carries forward the 16-7.h minority-report language O33 targets. Pruning: the deterministic spine returned provisions=[] (RAO 16 is a non-BCO procedural rule), so all bearing actions above come from topical search; the generic GA4–GA9 CJB judicial-commission entries in cases.jsonl are incidental presbytery-complaint cases unrelated to RPR reporting structure and are pruned, as are the substantive provision-keyed RPR exception rows. Renumbering caveat: RAO Article XVI has carried number 16 throughout the relevant period, but an earlier parallel numbering ran as RAO 14 — hence GA26 O24 reads "RAO 14-7c3" and several older inquiries cite RAO 14-x alongside the RAO 16-x equivalent; both were searched.

## O8 — Amend RAO 8-4.i to Set the Deadline for Floor Nominations 24 Hours Earlier
**Targets:** RAO 8-4.i · **Source:** Pacific Northwest · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/Overture-8_PNW_Nominations_rev.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/04/Overture-8_PNW_Nominations_rev.pdf)

**What it does:** Moves the floor-nomination deadline up roughly 24 hours — from the close of the first full day's afternoon session to 4:30 pm on the day the Assembly convenes — and eliminates the hard-copy filing option (electronic-only), so the Nominating Committee Supplemental Report can post earlier and Commissioners get more review time before Thursday-morning elections. Effective 2027.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None. (Cites only operational data — 2025 floor-nomination counts and NC Manual deadlines; no prior overture/case/CCB ruling by number.)

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **GA47 II.I** (2019, not in conflict; Adopted by CCB) — CCB found Northern New England's Overture 12 amending RAO 8-4 floor-nomination procedure "not in conflict"; closest CCB precedent on amending this exact rule. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci09.md)
- **GA49 III** ⭐ (2022, in order / not in conflict; Adopted by CCB) — CCB cleared Tennessee Valley's proposed RAO 8-4 amendment as in order and not in conflict with BCO/RAO; bears as precedent on amending this rule. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci26.md)
- **GA49 Supplemental III.2** ⭐ (2022, Adopted by CCB) — floor nominations for Stated Clerk follow the same RAO 8-4 procedure as other contested offices; construes the floor-nomination mechanics O8 modifies. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci30.md)
- **GA50 II.O** ⭐ (2023, not in conflict; Adopted 8-0-0) — CCB found amending RAO 8-4.h (with 17-1, 19-2) on minority reports not in conflict; bears on the adjacent subsection of the same Nominating Committee rule. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci15.md)
- **GA52 Supplemental II.2** ⭐ (2025, Adopted 8-0-0) — floor nominations permitted under RAO 3-4 even if the AC brings no Stated Clerk nominee; expressly construes **RAO 8-4.i**, the very subsection O8 amends; most recent bearing action. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci35.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA47 O12](../overtures/ga47_2019__o12.md)** (2019, Answered in the negative) — Northern New England, "Amend RAO 8-4 to Restrict Floor Nominations for GA Committees and Agencies"; the most directly comparable recent attempt to amend the same RAO 8-4 floor-nomination rule (defeated on the floor though CCB cleared it). [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p616)
- **[GA50 O22](../overtures/ga50_2023__o22.md)** ⭐ (2023, Answered in the negative) — Session of First PC Montgomery, "Amend RAO 8-4.h, 17-1 & 19-2 to Specify When Minority Reports Are Permitted"; amends the adjacent subsection (8-4.h) of the same Nominating Committee rule. [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1019)
- **[GA49 O32](../overtures/ga49_2022__o32.md)** ⭐ (2022, Answered in the negative) — Tennessee Valley, "Amend RAO 8.4 to Add Board-Recommended Nominees to GA Nominating Committee Report"; the most recent prior attempt to amend the same RAO 8-4 Nominating Committee rule (this is the overture behind the GA49 III CCB advice above). [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1352)
- **[GA31 O4](../overtures/ga31_2003__o4.md)** (2003, Adopted) — James River, "Amend Floor Nomination and Election Process"; the prior successful overhaul that produced much of the floor-nomination machinery O8 now adjusts. [page](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p63)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
The provision-exact spine returned **no prior overtures** and an RPR list of 21 rows — but every RPR row is for **BCO 8-4** (teaching elders laboring out of bounds), a different provision sharing the bare string "8-4"; all 21 RPR rows are pruned as incidental false positives, and RAO (assembly-operations) rules generate no RPR exceptions anyway. The bearing prior overtures (GA47 O12, GA49 O32, GA50 O22, GA31 O4) were recovered by topical search of /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md, since the spine matched RAO 8-4 inquiries but no overtures by number. GA49 O32 (Tennessee Valley, "Amend RAO 8.4 to Add Board-Recommended Nominees") is the overture behind the GA49 III CCB advice above and is indexed as a discrete overture in OVERTURES.md, so it is listed both as a prior-overture bullet and reflected in that CCB-advice bullet. Older "limit/eliminate floor nominations" overtures (GA21 O7/O19/O43, GA22 O36, GA30 O17) were reviewed and pruned: they target BCO 14-1 / RAO 13-2 eligibility restrictions, not the RAO 8-4.i deadline/filing mechanics O8 addresses. No RAO renumbering affects this provision; the lone NC-related case hit (GA15 p.112, geographic NC selection) is incidental and pruned. **Companion GA53 overtures** all amend RAO 8-4.i and will likely be perfected together: **O9** (Highlight Proportionate Representation), **O45** and **O47** (Require Floor Nominations Come from Previously Submitted Presbytery Nominees) — their edits to the same subsection must be reconciled.

## O9 — Amend RAO 8-4.i to Highlight Proportionate Representation of Presbyteries by Floor Nominations
**Targets:** RAO 8-4.i (invoking BCO 14-1.9) · **Source:** Hills and Plains Presbytery (to CCB, OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/10/Overture-9_HP_Nominations.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/10/Overture-9_HP_Nominations.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends RAO 8-4.i so every floor nomination for a GA Permanent Committee/Agency must include the nominee's Presbytery and an explanation of how the nomination contributes to the goal of proportionate representation of all Presbyteries set forth in BCO 14-1.9.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None by number — cites only BCO 14-1.9 (proportionate representation of presbyteries on GA committees) as the governing principle; no prior case, overture, or inquiry is cited.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.I** (GA47/2019, not in conflict; Adopted by CCB) — CCB cleared Northern New England Presbytery's Overture 12 to amend RAO 8-4 on floor nominations; construes the same provision O9 amends. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci09.md)
- **III** (GA49/2022, in order and not in conflict; Adopted by CCB) — CCB advised that Tennessee Valley Presbytery's proposed RAO 8-4 amendment was in order and not in conflict with BCO/RAO; same provision and same in-order/conformity question O9 raises. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci26.md)
- **Supplemental III.2** (GA49/2022, Adopted by CCB) — CCB construed floor-nomination procedure under RAO 8-4 (with RAO 3-4); bears on how the RAO 8-4 floor-nomination mechanism operates. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci30.md)
- **Supplemental II.2** (GA52/2025, Adopted 8-0-0) — CCB ruled floor nominations are permitted under RAO 3-4 / RAO 8-4.i; construes the exact subsection (8-4.i) O9 edits. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci35.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA47 O12](../overtures/ga47_2019__o12.md)** (2019, Answered in the negative) — Northern New England Presbytery, "Amend RAO 8-4 to Restrict Floor Nominations for GA Committees and Agencies"; the closest prior attempt to alter the same floor-nomination provision (defeated). [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p616)
- **[GA49 O32](../overtures/ga49_2022__o32.md)** (2022, Answered in the negative) — Tennessee Valley Presbytery, "Amend RAO 8.4 to Add Board-Recommended Nominees to GA Nominating Committee Report"; recent RAO 8-4 nomination amendment (the overture behind CCB advice III above). ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1352)
- **[GA31 O4](../overtures/ga31_2003__o4.md)** (2003, Answered in the negative) — James River Presbytery, "Amend Floor Nomination and Election Process"; a prior attempt to alter the floor-nomination mechanism (defeated). [page](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p63)
- **[GA30 O17](../overtures/ga30_2002__o17.md)** (2002, Answered in the negative) — Eastern Canada Presbytery, "Eliminate Floor Nominations & Change to Random Contests"; prior attempt to reshape floor nominations. [page](../markdown/ga30_2002.md#ga30-p76)
- **[GA24 O30](../overtures/ga24_1996__o30.md)** (1996, Answered in the negative) — New River Presbytery, "Ensure Proportionate Representation in Nominations & Elections"; direct prior attempt to build proportionate-representation into the nomination/election process — O9's animating idea, previously defeated. [page](../markdown/ga24_1996.md#ga24-p54)
- **[GA21 O19](../overtures/ga21_1993__o19.md)** (1993, Answered in the negative) — Covenant Presbytery, "Amend BCO 14-1 to Limit Floor Nominations to Presbytery-Nominated Candidates"; same subject, related provision (BCO 14-1). [page](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p55)
- **[GA18 O22](../overtures/ga18_1990__o22.md)** (1990, Answered in the negative) — Ascension Presbytery, "Study How to Achieve Better Ruling Elder Representation at GA"; related representation-balance concern. [page](../markdown/ga18_1990.md#ga18-p72)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
**Spine pruning.** The exact-provision spine returned 0 cases, 0 prior overtures (no overture rows are tagged "RAO 8-4"), and 21 RPR rows. All 21 RPR rows were pruned — they match **BCO 8-4** (out-of-bounds TE annual reports), a false hit against the unrelated **RAO 8-4**, and have no bearing on floor nominations. One spine CCB hit was also pruned: **GA50 II.O** (RAO 8-4.h, 17-1, 19-2 minority reports) construes a different subsection on an unrelated question.

**Topical supplement.** Because the provision-exact spine found no prior overtures, the seven above were recovered by concept search of /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md (floor nominations + proportionate representation). The strongest bearing actions are **[GA47 O12](../overtures/ga47_2019__o12.md)** (same provision) and **[GA24 O30](../overtures/ga24_1996__o30.md)** (same proportionate-representation rationale) — both answered in the negative, signaling repeated Assembly reluctance to constrain floor nominations. The retained CCB inquiries confirm the Assembly's consistent posture that RAO 8-4 floor nominations are a protected right; O9 does not restrict that right but adds a disclosure/justification requirement, a novel approach distinct from prior restriction attempts.

**Companion overture.** GA53 O9 amends the same paragraph (RAO 8-4.i) as other GA53 floor-nomination overtures; if any companion in the GA53 batch also edits 8-4.i, the texts must be reconciled by the committee.

## O10 — Change the Boundaries of Pittsburgh Presbytery and The Ohio Presbytery
**Targets:** (boundaries) · **Source:** Ohio · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Overture-10_Ohio_Boundaries-5.15.26.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Overture-10_Ohio_Boundaries-5.15.26.pdf)

**What it does:** Transfers all Ohio counties currently within Pittsburgh Presbytery's bounds (the region "east and south of and including the counties of Columbiana, Carroll, and Monroe") to Ohio Presbytery, since Ohio Presbytery has since been formed and in 2025 the only PCA church in those Ohio counties of Pittsburgh closed.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None by number — the grounds quote Pittsburgh's existing official boundary description, note Ohio Presbytery's formation, and recite the 2025 closure of the lone affected church.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (Presbytery boundary changes are routine MNA business, not justiciable; the provision-exact spine returned no provisions and no cases.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **10-77** (GA10/1982) — Constitutionality of a non-geographical presbytery; the CCB found BCO 11-4 implies geographical bounds while BCO 13-1 does not limit "bounds" geographically. The only constitutional treatment of what a presbytery's "bounds" means — the framework under which a county-by-county transfer between two geographic presbyteries operates. [page](../inquiries/ga10_1982__ci04.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA44 O24](../overtures/ga44_2016__o24.md)** (2016, Adopted (final)) — Ohio Presbytery, "Form Columbus Metropolitan Presbytery"; most recent reshaping of Ohio Presbytery's own bounds, showing the territory has been actively redrawn. ⭐ no (pre-GA48) [page](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p259)
- **[GA37 O19](../overtures/ga37_2009__o19.md)** (2009, Adopted (final)) — Great Lakes, "Form Ohio Presbytery"; the overture that created Ohio Presbytery itself and set the original Ohio/Pittsburgh interface this overture now cleans up. [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p233)
- **[GA37 O21](../overtures/ga37_2009__o21.md)** (2009, Answered by reference) — Ascension, "Concur with Formation of New Ohio Presbytery"; the concurring companion to the Ohio formation, modeling the two-presbytery concurrence pattern. [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p240)
- **[GA37 O12](../overtures/ga37_2009__o12.md)** (2009, Adopted (final)) — Ohio Valley, "Form Central Indiana Presbytery"; same 2009 Midwest reorganization wave that produced Ohio Presbytery. [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p230)
- **[GA30 O14](../overtures/ga30_2002__o14.md)** (2002, Answered in the negative) — Rocky Mountain, "Transfer Northern West Virginia Counties to Pittsburgh Presbytery"; prior boundary overture directly touching Pittsburgh Presbytery's bounds (denied — note it was filed by a non-affected presbytery without the affected presbyteries' concurrence). [page](../markdown/ga30_2002.md#ga30-p75)
- **[GA29 O22](../overtures/ga29_2001__o22.md)** (2001, Adopted (final)) — Great Lakes, "Divide Great Lakes Presbytery & Form Ohio Valley Presbytery"; the earlier division that produced the Ohio-region presbyteries (cf. companion GA29 O23 from Mississippi Valley, answered in the negative). [page](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p57)
- **[GA33 O15](../overtures/ga33_2005__o15.md)** (2005, Answered in the negative) — Great Lakes, "Adjust the Boundaries of Great Lakes and Ascension Presbyteries"; a two-presbytery boundary adjustment in the same region that was denied. [page](../markdown/ga33_2005.md#ga33-p168)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (The provision-exact spine's BCO 5-3 RPR hits — Northern Illinois, Calvary, South Texas, etc. — all concern "Temporary Government" of mission churches, an unrelated subject, and are pruned.)

### Note
Non-provision (boundaries) overture: the deterministic join returned provisions=[], so this page is built from a topical search of /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md and INQUIRIES.md rather than a provision spine. The governing BCO text is the geographic "bounds" language of BCO 11-4 / 13-1 (see inquiry 10-77); no provision number is cited in the overture. Boundary changes are referred to MNA and routinely adopted as final when the affected presbyteries concur — the bearing here is institutional precedent and standard procedure, not contested precedent. **Companion to GA53 O87** (Pittsburgh Presbytery, identically titled, dated 5.15.26): O10 (Ohio) and O87 (Pittsburgh) are the two affected presbyteries each overturing the same transfer — the mutual concurrence MNA looks for, which historically yields adoption; treat O87 as the concurring overture. Pruned: BCO 5-3 RPR exceptions (temporary government of mission churches — off-topic). The first pass cited GA37 O19/O21/O12, GA44 O24, GA30 O14, GA29 O22 — all verified real and retained here with verbatim deep-links; its bare "[OVERTURES.md](../index/OVERTURES.md)" placeholders without anchors have been replaced with real corpus links, and a generic boundary-precedent catch-all was dropped in favor of the region-specific Ohio/Pittsburgh line.

## O11 — Amend RAO 4-21.d to Require Assessment Data from MNA
**Targets:** RAO 4-21.d · **Source:** Ohio · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/10/Overture-11_Ohio_MNA.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/10/Overture-11_Ohio_MNA.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a new subsection RAO 4-21.d.6 requiring MNA's annual report to GA to include specified Assessment Center data (number of assessments, final ratings by category, and mission churches started/particularized/dissolved with an MNA-assessed planter and that planter's rating), with the data reviewed by the MNA Committee and that review noted in its minutes.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (grounds rest only on Scripture — Matt 16:19, 1 Pet 5:2 — and WCF 30; no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries are cited by number).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.D** (GA50/2023, not in conflict; Adopted 8-0-0) — Southern New England Presbytery's Overture 7 expanding RAO 4-21.d (to let Committees of Commissioners review compliance policies) was found not in conflict. Bears directly: a prior amendment to the very subsection O11 amends, cleared by the CCB. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci04.md)
- **II.I** (GA51/2024, not in conflict; Adopted 8-0-0) — Northwest Georgia's Overture 14 amending RAO 4-21.d to require enrollment data from PCA-affiliated higher-education institutions was found not in conflict. Closest precedent: a prior overture adding a mandatory data-reporting requirement to RAO 4-21.d, structurally identical to O11. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci09.md)

### Prior overtures
- ⭐ **[GA50 O7](../overtures/ga50_2023__o7.md)** (2023, Adopted) — Amend RAO 4-21.d to Require Committees to Record GA Instruction Compliance in Minutes. Directly on point: a prior amendment to RAO 4-21.d. Its CCB vetting is CI II.D above. [p.987](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p979), [p.1083](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1075)
- ⭐ **[GA51 O14](../overtures/ga51_2024__o14.md)** (2024, Adopted) — Amend RAO 4-21.d to Require Enrollment Data from Higher Education Institutions. Closest precedent: a prior overture adding a mandatory data-reporting requirement to RAO 4-21.d, structurally identical to O11. Its CCB vetting is CI II.I above. [p.1277](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1270)
- ⭐ **[GA51 O32](../overtures/ga51_2024__o32.md)** (2024, Carried over) — Pruned as incidental: empty subject in the spine and carried over without action; matched only by body text, not on the report-content question.

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
This is a provision-exact spine on RAO 4-21. The two GA47/2019 clusters in the spine are PRUNED as incidental: CI II.G/II.J/II.O/II.P/II.R (overtures 8/14/19/21/32 on non-ordained persons serving on GA committees and boards) cite RAO 4-21.c.6 only in passing and concern BCO 14-1, not the report-content question; CI III.A (SJC member eligibility for concurrent agency-board service) lists RAO 4-21 in a long string of RAO sections without construing reporting requirements. The bearing actions are the two prior RAO 4-21.d data-reporting amendments (II.D, II.I), both adopted not-in-conflict — direct precedent that the CCB has twice approved adding mandatory data to agency-type GA reports under this subsection, a favorable posture for O11. No RAO renumbering affects 4-21.d. (This redo corrects a looser first pass that used non-deep-link placeholders and cited GA12 overtures absent from the spine; it also adds GA51 O14 / CI II.I, which the first pass missed.)

## O12 — Amend BCO 21-4.a to Allow Alternatives to a Bachelor's Degree for Ordination
**Targets:** BCO 21-4.a (refs BCO 8-2, BCO 21-4) · **Source:** Chesapeake (to CCB, OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-12_Chesapeake_21-4.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-12_Chesapeake_21-4.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 21-4.a.1 so an ordination candidate may present, in lieu of a Bachelor/Master college degree, **either** an Associate degree plus ≥3 years full-time vocational work experience **or** a GED plus ≥10 years such experience (each demonstrating maturity, leadership, and communication skills); also broadens 21-4.a.2 to accept a GA-approved theological study program certificate. Stated rationale: rising college costs and changing educational pathways create financial barriers for otherwise-qualified candidates, without lowering the theological-exam requirements.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None. The grounds invoke current BCO 21-4.a, BCO 8-2 ("competency of human learning"), and BCO 21-4's exam standards, plus secular education statistics (NCES, IPEDS, Barna, Faith & Leadership). No prior overture, judicial case, or CCB/inquiry ruling is cited by name or number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. — All 15 provision-exact spine cases cite BCO 21-4 only for matters unrelated to the educational/degree requirement O12 amends: the *extraordinary clause for examination trial parts* and *transfer/ordination irregularities* (e.g. 1980-4 Bogue v. Ascension, [minutes](../markdown/ga08_1980.md#ga08-p52); 2007-8 Jones v. Louisiana / the Wilkins line, [minutes](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p117); 2009-24 Phelps v. Pacific, [case](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-24.md); 2015-12 Wills v. Metro Atlanta, [case](../cases/ga44_2016__2015-12.md); 2015-13 Barnes v. Heartland, [case](../cases/ga45_2017__2015-13.md); 2016-17 Webster & Fowler v. Heritage, [case](../cases/ga46_2018__2016-17.md); 2019-2 Schrock v. Philadelphia, [minutes](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p685); 2022-3 Klett v. Philadelphia, [minutes](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p820); 2022-21 Senters v. Savannah River, [case](../cases/ga51_2024__2022-21.md)). None construes the college-degree prerequisite, so all are pruned as incidental provision-exact hits.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **16-77 III,9 (CI #5)** (GA16/1988, advice given) — Holds BCO 21-4's extraordinary clause "applies only to listed trial parts for ordination, **not** to prerequisite requirements such as college diploma, seminary diploma, and internship completion." Most on-point action: it establishes the **college-diploma prerequisite is not waivable** via the extraordinary clause — exactly the constraint O12 must amend the text to overcome. [page](../inquiries/ga16_1988__ci05.md)
- **16-77 III,9 (CI #2)** (GA16/1988, advice given) — Companion ruling: the extraordinary clause excuses only the six-month membership period, not the session endorsement, filing deadline, or internship sequence — confirming the same "prerequisites are firm" reading. [page](../inquiries/ga16_1988__ci02.md)
- **13-45 III,61** (GA13/1985, advice given) — Use of BCO 21-4's extraordinary clause must be limited to "truly extraordinary circumstances or proven extraordinary gifts," warning against laxity. Bears on the 3/4-vote omission mechanism O12 leaves intact. [page](../inquiries/ga13_1985__ci04.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA16 O22](../overtures/ga16_1988__o22.md)** (1988, Answered by reference) — "Amend BCO 21-4 to Allow Ordination Without Undergraduate Degree by Supermajority Vote." Near-identical prior attempt: ordain candidates lacking an undergraduate degree by supermajority. O12 is the modern successor, routing relief through codified Associate/GED-plus-experience pathways rather than a bare supermajority waiver. [page](../markdown/ga16_1988.md#ga16-p73)
- **[GA12 O12](../overtures/ga12_1984__o12.md)** (1984, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 19-2 and 21-4 to Add Church History to Ordination Examinations." Prior attempt to alter the 21-4 qualification list; shows Assembly caution about re-tooling the 21-4 educational/exam requirements. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p50)
- **[GA15 O43](../overtures/ga15_1987__o43.md)** (1987, Referred) — "Amend BCO 21-4 to Clarify Extraordinary Provisions for Ordained Ministers." Bears on the extraordinary-clause mechanism O12 retains. [page](../markdown/ga15_1987.md#ga15-p68)
- **[GA14 O43](../overtures/ga14_1986__o43.md)** (1986, Referred) — "Amend BCO 21-4 to Clarify Extraordinary Reception of Ministers from Other Denominations." Related 21-4 extraordinary-clause amendment (transfer context); a prior 21-4 amendment attempt. [page](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p55)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 21-4** — 805 RPR rows cite this provision (high-volume). The bearing cluster is the recurring exception that records show **"no record of fulfillment of BCO 21-4, par. 1, Educational requirements"** ([Philadelphia](../rpr/philadelphia.md), 18th/1990) and waivers of educational/language exams without the recorded 3/4 vote and reasons ([Western Carolina](../rpr/western-carolina.md), 18th/1990; [Heritage](../rpr/heritage.md), 19th/1991). These confirm real-world friction with the educational-requirement and record-of-omission machinery O12 amends. The large majority of the 805 rows concern transfer-exam and trial-part recordkeeping and are incidental to the degree question. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Pruning: the provision-exact spine returned 15 cases, 15 inquiries, 17 CCB items, 38 prior overtures, and 805 RPR rows — all keyed to *all of BCO 21-4*, which bundles the educational prerequisite (O12's target) with the extraordinary clause for trial parts, confessional-exception handling, transfer examinations, dividing presbytery, background checks, and moral qualifications. O12 touches **only 21-4.a's degree/education requirement**, so I pruned everything not construing that subject: all 15 judicial cases (extraordinary-clause / transfer / discipline matters, none about the college degree); the confessional-exception CCB line (30-29 III; 31-56 VI; 32-36 III; 32-40 II.G; 33-29 II.D; 34-34 II.F; 35-30 II.I); the male-only-ordination, same-sex-attraction, background-check, re-examination, and translation/exam-discretion inquiries (45 App.O II.B; 48 II.I/II.P/II.U/II.Z; 49 II.X; 50 II.C; 51 II.K/II.L/II.S; 24-23 ref.#2; 32-36 II.2; 34-34 IV.B; 38-18 II.1; 42 App.O IV.B); the "dividing presbytery into sections" inquiries (14-52 48; CI #19; 16-67 V,6); and the off-topic prior overtures (GA12 O5 mercy ministries; GA13 O20 / GA15 O22 parity & delegated-GA; GA20 O23 exam-rejection grounds; GA21 O5/O20; GA25 O1/O14; GA30 O4/O24/O29; GA31 O6; GA34 O17; GA48 O37; GA49 O31; GA51 O2 — confessional-exception, transfer, moral-qualification, and procedural amendments). Renumbering: BCO 21-4 is a stable, non-renumbered provision (confirmed against bco_renumberings.jsonl), so no old-number search was needed. Companion: no other GA53 overture targets 21-4.a; O12 stands alone on the education question. The four surfaced prior overtures (GA12/14/15/16) all predate GA48, so no recent-overture stars apply; the GA48–51 spine items (cases 2019-2, 2022-3, 2022-21; the moral-qualification/background-check CCB line; prior overtures GA48 O37, GA49 O31, GA51 O2) are all pruned as off-topic to the degree requirement. Strongest bearing action: **CI 16-77 III,9 (CI #5)** holding the college-diploma prerequisite is *not* waivable under the extraordinary clause, paired with the near-identical prior attempt **[GA16 O22](../overtures/ga16_1988__o22.md)**.

---

## O13 — Amend BCO 15-2 Regarding Session Commissions
**Targets:** BCO 15-2 · **Source:** Great Lakes · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-13_GreatLakes_15.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-13_GreatLakes_15.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a third paragraph to BCO 15-2 governing commissions appointed by a **Session** (distinct from Presbytery commissions): each shall consist of at least two elders "with any combination of teaching or ruling elders," and the quorum shall be the greater of two elders or one-half of the membership. Resolves a disputed practice — some argue Session commissions should mirror the Presbytery rule (2 TE + 2 RE), which would leave many Sessions (e.g., all-RE Sessions) unable to form one.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (the grounds cite only BCO 15-1; no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2021-3 — DeJong v. Session of Village Seven Presbyterian Church](../cases/ga49_2022__2021-03.md)** (GA49/2022, sustained) — directly construes BCO 15-2 as applied to a **Session** governance commission: holds the list of matters commissions may execute under 15-2 is not exhaustive, but a commission's scope must be specifically defined by the referring court (BCO 15-1); two provisions of the Village Seven governance commission were held to extend unconstitutionally beyond those limits. This is the only spine case construing BCO 15-2 on a Session commission's constitutional scope — precisely O13's target. [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p881)
- **[2009-10 — Woodward v. Western Carolina Presbytery](../cases/ga38_2010__2009-05_2009-08_2009-09_2009-10.md)** (GA38/2010, sustained in part) — Presbytery appointed a commission under BCO 15-1 & 2; the Woodward sub-complaint (2009-10) was dismissed on standing (BCO 43-1/11-4) rather than on commission-composition grounds, but the case documents how BCO 15-2 commissions are constituted and deployed in practice. [minutes](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p197)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI #15** (GA13/1985, advice given) — Scope of presbytery commissions under BCO 15-2: the list of assignable matters is typical but not exhaustive. Construes the breadth of a 15-2 commission, the provision O13 amends. [page](../inquiries/ga13_1985__ci11.md)
- **14-44** (GA14/1986, advice given) — A judicial commission requires appointment under BCO 15-2 (plus BCO 32-3 approval of charges). Construes how a 15-2 commission is constituted. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci02.md)
- **CI #14** (GA14/1986, advice given) — A presbytery visitation commission may not be granted judicial power absent charges/a pending case (BCO 15-2, 31-2). Construes the limits of 15-2 commission authority. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci17.md)
- **II.M** (GA49/2022, not in conflict; Adopted by the CCB) — A proposed amendment to **BCO 15-2** clarifying presbytery commission **membership and quorum** (Overture 19, Northwest Georgia) was found not in conflict with the BCO. Most directly bearing: the prior, recent, CCB-cleared attempt to amend the very text and subject (commission membership/quorum) O13 now extends to Session commissions. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci13.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA6 O19](../overtures/ga06_1978__o19.md)** (1978, Answered in the negative) — Covenant Presbytery, "Amend BCO 15-2 to Remove Cap on Commissioners from a Single Congregation": an early attempt to amend 15-2's commission-composition rule. [page](../markdown/ga06_1978.md#ga06-p38)
- **[GA18 O11](../overtures/ga18_1990__o11.md)** (1990) — Eastern Canada, "Amend BCO 15-2 Regarding Quorum of Commission as Session": directly on point — a prior attempt to set the **quorum** for a commission acting as a Session, the same subject O13 addresses. [page](../markdown/ga18_1990.md#ga18-p71)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 15-2** — 105 citations across GA18 (1990) through GA52 (2025); overwhelmingly presbyteries forming commissions without the required 2 TE / 2 RE or without recording a quorum (e.g., [Pacific](../rpr/pacific.md) 33rd/2005 outstanding; [Korean Eastern](../rpr/korean-eastern.md) 34th/2006; [Palmetto](../rpr/palmetto.md) 49th/2022; [Rocky Mountain](../rpr/rocky-mountain.md) & [Platte Valley](../rpr/platte-valley.md) 52nd/2025 "commission of one person"). Heavy, persistent real-world friction over commission composition and quorum — exactly the gap O13 fixes for Session commissions. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
O13 concerns **Session** commissions; almost the entire exact-provision spine for BCO 15-2 concerns **Presbytery** commissions (the 2-TE/2-RE quorum rule O13 explicitly declines to impose on Sessions). The spine hits therefore bear as context — establishing the existing presbytery rule and its enforcement record against which O13 carves out a distinct, lighter Session-commission rule — not as prior litigation of the precise question. **Pruned as incidental** (cite 15-2 only in passing on unrelated judicial-procedure grounds): Mays v. New River (GA8), Marshall v. Eastern Carolina (GA19), both Fitzsimmons v. Evangel entries (GA26), Kim v. Korean Eastern (GA34), the GA36 p.101 SJC decision, the Lee v. Korean Eastern cluster (2007-09/2007-10/2009-16, GA37), Dunn v. Phila Metro West (GA41/GA42), and Speck v. Missouri (GA49) — Speck does not cite 15-2 in its case text at all. **Restored: DeJong v. Village Seven (2021-3)** — prior note incorrectly characterized this as incidental; DeJong directly construes BCO 15-2/15-1 on the constitutional scope of a Session governance commission, the only spine case on point for a Session (not Presbytery) commission. **Woodward (2009-10)** is retained as background context only: its 2009-10 sub-complaint was dismissed on standing (BCO 43-1/11-4), not commission-composition grounds. Also pruned: GA22 O6 (Amend BCO 13 re dissolving churches — only an incidental 15-2 cross-reference) and the lone RAO 15-2 RPR row (Overtures Committee tenure — unrelated provision). **Renumbering caveat:** the 1989 (17th GA) amendment inserted new 15-1..15-5; "BCO 15-2" has denoted the commissions section since then, so the GA13/GA14 inquiries and later actions citing "15-2" are on-point. No companion GA53 overture targets Session-commission composition.
Pruned as incidental: 2016-14 Wills v. Metro Atlanta Presbytery — BCO 15-2 appears only once as a parenthetical citation ("BCO 15-2") identifying the authority for appointing a commission; the case is about church dissolution under BCO 13-9(f) and bears no analysis of commission composition or quorum.

---

## O14 — Amend BCO 7-3, 7-4, 9-2, and 9-7 Regarding Titles and Offices for Unordained People
**Targets:** BCO 7-3, 7-4, 9-2, 9-7 · **Source:** SWFL · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-14_SWFL_Titles-1.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-14_SWFL_Titles-1.pdf)

**What it does:** Expands BCO 7-3 to forbid any synonymous title for unordained persons (e.g. shepherdess, eldress, pastoress, minister, deaconess) and adds new BCO 7-4 barring congregations from inventing offices or conferring authority titles besides pastor/elder and deacon; amends 9-2 and 9-7 so that where deacons cannot be ordained the elders must directly execute diaconal duties (not delegate them to unordained staff), assistants to deacons may not be called "deaconess" or "members of the diaconate," and assistants may not be appointed where no ordained deacons serve.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (the rationale cites only savethepca.com research documenting ~5–10% of churches using such titles, and the PCAAC BCO text — no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries by name).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2007-13 — Kniseley v. Rocky Mountain](../cases/ga37_2009__2007-13.md)** (GA39/2011, denied) — construes whether the title "minister" may be used for unordained church staff; the SJC denied the complaint holding the BCO does not proscribe such generic use, reasoning from BCO 7-2 and BCO 40-2(3); bears directly on O14's 7-3 expansion forbidding synonymous titles for unordained persons. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p557)
- **[2009-25 — Brown v. Northern California Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-25_2009-26.md)** (GA39/2011, sustained) — applies BCO 9-2/9-7 to a diaconate/property dispute; same provisions O14 amends. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p550)
- **[2009-26 — Session of Grace PC v. Northern California Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-25_2009-26.md)** (GA39/2011, sustained) — companion to 2009-25 on BCO 9-2/9-7. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p550)
- **[2011-14 — Reese and Bech v. Philadelphia Presbytery](../cases/ga42_2014__2011-14.md)** (GA42/2014, sustained) — construes BCO 9-2's "impossible for any reason to secure deacons" clause: City Church Philadelphia invoked it to justify not forming a diaconate on grounds of conscience regarding women deacons; the SJC sustained the complaint that Presbytery erred in not acting on TE Hsu's violation of his ordination commitments; bears on O14's 9-2 duty-execution and diaconate-formation provisions. [minutes](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p530)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.S** (GA50/2023) — CCB found NO constitutional conflict in amending BCO 7-3 to regulate titling of unordained individuals; the direct CCB ruling on the immediate predecessor (O26) of O14's 7-3 expansion. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci19.md)
- **38-34 II.A** (GA38/2010) — CCB found an overture *prohibiting* deaconesses in conflict, reasoning "deaconess" need not denote an ordained office; directly contrary to O14's premise that "deaconess" is barred. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci02.md)
- **38-34 II.D** (GA38/2010) — CCB found an overture prohibiting commissioned/installed assistants to deacons in conflict on the same grounds; bears on O14's restriction of 9-7 assistants. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci03.md)
- **38-34 II.E** (GA38/2010) — CCB found an overture appointing unordained persons to diaconal ministry in conflict (implied unordained office contra BCO 17-1); construes BCO 9-2/9-7/7-2 together as O14 does. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci04.md)
- **App. O II.H** (GA46/2018) — CCB found Grace Presbytery's deaconess/women-officer overture in conflict, noting the session (not congregation) appoints and vows are required; bears on O14's 7-4/9-7 appointment limits. [page](../inquiries/ga46_2018__ci04.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA50 O26](../overtures/ga50_2023__o26.md)** (2023, Approved & ratified 2024) — Amend BCO 7-3 to Prohibit Ecclesiastical Titles for Unordained People; the ratified predecessor O14 directly builds on and extends. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1028)
- **[GA47 O40](../overtures/ga47_2019__o40.md)** (2019) — Urge Sessions to Acknowledge and Support Women Leaders Under BCO 9-7; the counter-current on the same provision. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p692)
