- **[GA38 O2](../overtures/ga38_2010__o2.md)** (2010) — Amend BCO 9-7 to Prohibit Deaconesses; the closest prior attempt at O14's 9-7 change. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p386)
- **[GA38 O9](../overtures/ga38_2010__o9.md)** (2010) — Revise BCO 9-7 to Prohibit Commissioning Assistants to Deacons as Office Bearers; companion 9-7 prohibition attempt. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p387)
- **[GA23 O15](../overtures/ga23_1995__o15.md)** (1995, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 7-4 to Confine Doctrinal Requirements to Westminster Standards; prior attempt to amend 7-4 (different subject, same section O14 rewrites). [page](../markdown/ga23_1995.md#ga23-p48)
- **[GA19 O40](../overtures/ga19_1991__o40.md)** (1991) — Declare Ordination of Deaconesses a Violation of BCO; early effort against deaconesses bearing on the 7-3/9-7 thrust. [page](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p59)
- **[GA15 O35](../overtures/ga15_1987__o35.md)** (1987) — Rescind Prohibition on Use of the Word "Reverend"; historic dispute over titles for officers under BCO 7-3. [page](../markdown/ga15_1987.md#ga15-p56)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 9-7** — 3 citations; e.g. [Metro Atlanta](../rpr/metro-atlanta.md) (38th/2010, unsatisfactory-outstanding) on a session selecting female assistants in a manner not in accord with 9-7, and [Philadelphia](../rpr/philadelphia.md) (40th/2012, closed) on a 9-7 exception not in accord with the fundamentals; real friction over the very provision O14 tightens. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 9-2** — 2 citations; [Metro Atlanta](../rpr/metro-atlanta.md) (38th/2010, unsatisfactory-outstanding) on congregational election of diaconal assistants and denial of men leading the diaconate; bears on O14's elders-must-execute-9-2-duties change. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
This is the deterministic provision-exact spine (BCO 7-3/7-4/9-2/9-7) plus a concept supplement. **Pruned as incidental:** the GA12 pre-SJC procedural "case" (num=null, out_of_order — accusations v. presbytery, no construction of 7-3); inquiry **27-43 II.1** (deacon authority to *sell donated property* under 9-2 — property mechanics, not titles/offices) and CCB **II.W** (GA52, RAO 16 statistical reporting — only incidentally cites 9-2); prior overtures **[GA10 O17](../overtures/ga10_1982__o17.md)** (trustees assuming deacon admin duties) and **[GA22 O36](../overtures/ga22_1994__o36.md)** (IAR legal opinions/interim board) which matched on 9-2 property language but are unrelated to the female-officer/titles question; and the **BCO 7-3 Korean Southwest RPR** (52nd/2025 — an unaddressed delinquency report, no relation to titling). No renumbering affects chapters 7 or 9 (bco_renumberings.jsonl: the only ch.8/9 event is the 1980 merge of old ch.9 into ch.8, predating the modern 9-2/9-7 text). **Companion context:** O14 is the most aggressive of the recurring deaconess/female-officer line — directly extending the ratified **[GA50 O26](../overtures/ga50_2023__o26.md)** (7-3) and reviving the failed **GA38 O2/O9** (9-7) approach; related GA38 study-committee fights (O7 reconsider women deacons, O16 affirm deaconesses) sit in the same controversy. Fixed descriptions: **Kniseley 2007-13** was described as "construes BCO 9-2/9-7 where an unordained M.Div. holder was involved" — corrected; the case is about the title "minister" for unordained staff (BCO 7-2 / 40-2(3)), which bears on O14's 7-3 target. **Reese and Bech 2011-14** was described as "construes BCO 9-2 (deacon care of congregational property)" — corrected; the case construes BCO 9-2's "impossible for any reason to secure deacons" exemption clause in the context of City Church's refusal to form a diaconate due to views on women deacons, not property. Both cases are genuinely bearing on O14's provisions but their prior descriptions misstated what each held.

## O15 — Amend BCO 42-4 and 43-3 to Clarify the Deadline for Filings
**Targets:** BCO 42-4, 43-3 · **Source:** SWFL · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-15_SWFL_FilingDeadlines.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-15_SWFL_FilingDeadlines.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 42-4 (appeals) and 43-3 (complaints) so that the 30-day filing clock runs from *written* notification of the lower court's decision, delivered by a prescribed mode (certified/registered/express mail, hand delivery, or confirmed e-mail/fax), and deems compliance fulfilled if a party cannot be located after diligent inquiry or refuses delivery. It seeks to resolve ambiguity over whether an in-person oral pronouncement of censure, versus a written decision, starts the appeal period.

**Cites in its own grounds:** SJC 2024-10 *Gozé v. Hills and Plains Presbytery* (52nd GA, 2025) as a recent example; and the 2013 GA amendment (broadly following Pacific Northwest Presbytery's overture) that first set the clock at "notification of the last court's decision."

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-10 — Gozé v. Hills and Plains Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-10.md)** (52/2025, dismissed) — Self-cited by the overture; appeal dismissed as untimely under BCO 42-4 because filed more than 30 days after "notification of the last court's decision." This is the exact friction the overture targets. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1013)
- **[2021-13 — Dudt v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2021-13.md)** (49/2022, sustained) — Construes BCO 42-4 on appeal filing; SJC sustained that Presbytery erred in treating the November filing (without supporting reasons) as untimely: 42-4 distinguishes oral notice before adjournment from the 30-day written notice with supporting reasons. Bears on the deadline mechanics O15 addresses. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p909)
- **[1999-2 — Tan v. South Texas Presbytery](../cases/ga28_2000__1999-02.md)** (28/2000, dismissed) — Early case construing BCO 43-3 access-to-higher-court timing; complaint declared administratively out of order as not timely filed (dated and faxed on August 28 but not mailed until September 4, exceeding the 30-day period). [minutes](../markdown/ga28_2000.md#ga28-p243)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CCB II.H (Overture 9, Platte Valley)** (47/2019, not in conflict; adopted) — Reviewed an overture amending BCO 42-4, 43-2, and 43-3 to update methods and deadlines for filing judicial cases — directly on point with O15's subject matter. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci08.md)
- **CCB II.T (Overture 34, Philadelphia)** (47/2019, not in conflict; adopted) — Reviewed amendments to BCO 42-4, 43-2, 43-3 (and OMSJC 18.10.b) clarifying filing requirements and permitting electronic filings. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci20.md)
- **CCB II.O (Overture 21, Northwest Georgia)** (49/2022, ambiguous; adopted) — Reviewed an amendment to BCO 43-2/43-3 on the timing of filing complaints; found ambiguous — illustrates the recurring drafting difficulty O15 tries to cure. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci15.md)
- **CI 29-28 III.6** (29/2001, advice given) — A complainant may not go to the higher court until the lower court has acted under BCO 43-2/43-3; bears on the 43-3 trigger O15 amends. [page](../inquiries/ga29_2001__ci06.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA47 O9](../overtures/ga47_2019__o9.md)** (2019, to CCB/OC) — Amend BCO 42-4, 43-2, 43-3 Regarding Method and Deadlines of Filing Cases — nearest prior attempt at the same change. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p608)
- **[GA47 O34](../overtures/ga47_2019__o34.md)** (2019, Approved & ratified 2021) — Amend BCO 42-4, 43-2, 43-3 and OMSJC 18-10 to Allow Electronic Filings — the adopted predecessor that set the current filing/notification language. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p672)
- **[GA40 O14](../overtures/ga40_2012__o14.md)** (2012, Approved & ratified 2013) — Pacific Northwest's "Amend BCO 42-4 to Change Start of Thirty-Day Filing Period for Appeal" — the 2013 amendment O15 expressly cites and seeks to clarify. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p697)
- **[GA40 O13](../overtures/ga40_2012__o13.md)** (2012, Approved & ratified 2013) — Pacific Northwest's "Amend BCO 43-3 to Change Start of Thirty-Day Filing Period for Higher Court Complaint" — companion 2013 amendment O15 builds on. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p697)
- **[GA20 O7](../overtures/ga20_1992__o7.md)** (1992, Out of order) — Amend BCO 43-2 and 43-3 — early attempt to amend the 43-3 complaint procedure. [page](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p56)
- **[GA20 O16](../overtures/ga20_1992__o16.md)** (1992, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 43-3 to Clarify if Current Amendment Adopted — historical 43-3 clarification attempt. [page](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p57)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 42-4** — 1 citation; [Savannah River](../rpr/exc/savannah-river__020.md), 48th (2021): no record of the court's action regarding a timely-filed appeal — real-world failure of courts to document/act on appeals. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 43-3** — 1 citation; [Philadelphia](../rpr/exc/philadelphia__065.md), 51st (2024): complaint from a lower court (church Session) not included in minutes — record-keeping friction around the 43-3 complaint process. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
The provision-exact spine returned 39 cases on BCO 42-4/43-3; these provisions govern timeliness for nearly every appeal/complaint, so most hits are incidental (the provision is cited only as the procedural basis for jurisdiction, not for the notification-timing question). I pruned ~29 incidental hits — e.g., 1981-2, 1983-15, 13-61, 2000-10, 2004-7, 2004-9, 2010-18, 2010-24, 2011-8, 2013-7, 2015-2, 2015-10, 2016-2, 2016-5, 2016-14, 2016-17, 2017-1, 2018-5, 2019-13, 2020-3, 2020-10, 2021-6, 2022-1, 2023-4, 2023-06/08, 2023-20, 2024-5, 2024-16, plus the pre-SJC GA9/GA12/GA40 case fragments — keeping only cases that turn on the filing deadline or notification trigger. The keystone bearing action is the self-cited **Gozé (2024-10)**. The other half of O15's grounds — the **2013 amendment** — the corpus locates precisely as **GA40 O13 (43-3) and O14 (42-4)** from Pacific Northwest Presbytery. No chapter renumbering applies — BCO 42 and 43 numbering is stable. CI 12-53 (matched on 42-4) was pruned: it concerns debate prohibitions during a complaint, not filing deadlines. GA14 O37 (end-of-life ethics) was a false body+title match and is dropped.
Pruned as incidental: **2019-3 Crouse v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery** — case is entirely about BCO 24-1 officer nomination process (a deacon's nomination for ruling elder was screened out by the Session before examination); 42-4 does not appear in the case text and the spine attribution appears to come from a procedural minutes reference; the description "Turns on BCO 42-4 appeal timeliness/notification" was incorrect. **2016-1 Aven v. Ohio Valley Presbytery** — case is about paedocommunion and compliance with an SJC remand on LC 177; 42-4 and 43-3 appear in the index's bco_cited_current but not in the case text and play no role in the holding; described as "one of the few cases citing both 42-4 and 43-3 on filing/timeliness" but the case has nothing to do with timeliness. **2018-4 Mapes v. Metropolitan New York Presbytery** — complaint was dismissed as moot (the congregational vote the complainant sought was held when Presbytery dismissed the congregation), not on timeliness grounds; the description "Complaint dismissed on BCO 43-3 timeliness grounds" was incorrect. **2018-6 Edwards v. North Texas Presbytery** — case is about failing to file the complaint with Presbytery before bringing it to the SJC (BCO 42-4 & 43-2 require adjudication below first), not about the written-notification trigger O15 amends; incidental. **2015-11 Thompson v. South Florida Presbytery** — BCO 43-3 is the procedural vehicle by which Thompson brought the complaint to Presbytery, but the case is about contumacy and improper pre-trial excommunication under BCO 32-6; 43-3 is not construed on its own terms in the holding.

## O16 — Amend BCO 43 to Clarify Circularizing the Court
**Targets:** BCO 43 (43-2, 43-3) · **Source:** Southwest Florida Presbytery · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-16_SWFL_Circularizing.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/Overture-16_SWFL_Circularizing.pdf)

**What it does:** Moves the circularization prohibition out of BCO 43-2 (the original-court stage) and into 43-3, recasting it as a ban on circularizing only the *higher/appellate* court reviewing a complaint ("No attempt should be made by any party to circularize a higher court reviewing a complaint"). The stated aim is to free courts of original jurisdiction to deliberate openly on complaints (no defined "parties" exist before an adverse decision) while preserving the circularization ban for appellate review.

**Cites in its own grounds:** The 1984 amendment that first required complaints to be filed with the court of original jurisdiction and introduced the circularization ban; and the 1999 Pittsburgh Presbytery proposal — adopted by the GA in 2000 — clarifying that a respondent need only be appointed when a complaint ascends to a higher court (= GA27 O9). No SJC case cited by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[1990-09 — Hathaway v. Grace Presbytery](../cases/ga19_1991__1990-09.md)** (19th GA/1991, denied) — Cites BCO 43-2 and is topically indexed to "circularization of court" and "circularization of commission"; an early SJC treatment of the circularization rule the overture seeks to relocate. [minutes](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p567)
- **[2013-01 — Dunn and Pesnell v. Philadelphia Metro West Presbytery](../cases/ga42_2014__2013-01.md)** (42nd GA/2014, not sustained) — Cites BCO 43-2 with the topic "circularizing a court"; bears on how the circularization prohibition operates at the complaint stage the overture targets. [minutes](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p554)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **12-53 II, 56** (12th GA/1984) — Scope and duration of the BCO debate/discussion prohibitions during a complaint: they apply only to the particular matter, only until final adjudication, in the presence of the higher court, and to all members of the lower court. Directly construes the original-court deliberation constraints the overture says "chill helpful dialogue." [page](../inquiries/ga12_1984__ci05.md)
- **29-28 III.6** (29th GA/2001) — A complainant may not go to a higher court until the lower court has acted under BCO 43-2 and 43-3; bears on the 43-2/43-3 lower-vs-higher-court division the overture reorganizes. [page](../inquiries/ga29_2001__ci06.md)
- **CI #13** (13th GA/1985) — Notice-of-complaint sufficiency and timing of a suspension motion under BCO 43-4 and 43-2; touches the original-court complaint mechanics the amendment loosens. [page](../inquiries/ga13_1985__ci10.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA27 O9](../overtures/ga27_1999__o9.md)** (1999, Approved & ratified 2000) — Pittsburgh Presbytery, "Clarify BCO 43-5"; clarified that a respondent need only be appointed when a complaint reaches a higher court — the exact precedent O16's rationale cites for distinguishing original- from higher-court formalities. [page](../markdown/ga27_1999.md#ga27-p49)
- **[GA31 O10](../overtures/ga31_2003__o10.md)** (2003, Answered in the negative) — Central Carolina, "Amend BCO 43-2 Regarding Complaints Against Undebatable Judicial Commission Reports"; proposed adding text to 43-2 immediately before the circularization sentence — a prior attempt to edit the same clause. [page](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p201)
- **[GA40 O14](../overtures/ga40_2012__o14.md)** (2012, Approved & ratified 2013) — Pacific Northwest, parallel circularization clause for *appeals* in BCO 42-4 ("...before the case is heard"); the appellate analogue the overture says it leaves intact, and the model for the "higher court reviewing" language. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p697)
- **[GA49 O21](../overtures/ga49_2022__o21.md)** (2022, Answered in the affirmative as amended) — Northwest Georgia, "Amend BCO 43-2 and 43-3 Regarding Timing for Considering a Complaint"; recent attempt to edit the same two sections. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1326)
- **[GA51 O21](../overtures/ga51_2024__o21.md)** (2024, Approved & ratified 2025) — Central Indiana, "Change the Prohibition Against 'Interlocutory Appeal' by Complaint in BCO 43-1"; recent successful amendment in the same complaint chapter, showing live legislative activity on BCO 43. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1165)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 43-2** — 5 citations (e.g., [Georgia Foothills](../rpr/georgia-foothills.md) 44th/2016, [Philadelphia](../rpr/philadelphia.md) 47th/2019), all on presbyteries failing to consider or timely deliberate complaints. Real-world friction at the original-court stage the overture seeks to ease, though none concern circularization specifically. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 43-3** — 1 citation ([Philadelphia](../rpr/exc/philadelphia__065.md) 51st/2024) on a lower-court complaint omitted from the minutes; the destination section the circularization sentence would move into. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Chapter-level (non-provision) overture, so the deterministic spine returned no exact-provision hits; all entries above come from topical search on "circularize"/BCO 43-2/43-3 plus the overture's own cited history. BCO chapter 43 was not renumbered, so no old-number search was needed. **Harmonization caveat:** O16's relocated language must be squared with the parallel "No attempt should be made to circularize" sentence retained in the appeals provision (BCO 42-4, the GA40 O14 model) so the two clauses use consistent "higher/appellate court" phrasing. Pruned as incidental: cases and inquiries citing BCO 43-4/43-1/43-6 that do not touch circularization or the 43-2/43-3 lower-vs-higher-court mechanics (e.g., GA20 CI03/CI04, GA39 CI02, GA52 CI31). The two retained cases (Hathaway, Dunn) are the only SJC actions topically tagged to circularization. The most load-bearing prior action is GA27 O9 (1999/2000), which the overture itself invokes as its model. (First pass replaced: it relied on non-deep-link tags like [CASES.md](../index/CASES.md)/[OVERTURES.md](../index/OVERTURES.md) and two CCB-advice ids I could not verify in the corpus — dropped here in favor of verified deep-links.)

---

## O17 — Amend BCO 5-2 Regarding the Dissolution of Mission Churches
**Targets:** BCO 5-2 (5-2.c) · **Source:** Westminster Presbytery · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-17_Westminster_5-2.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-17_Westminster_5-2.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 5-2.c so that a Presbytery dissolving a mission church must follow the procedures of **both** BCO 13-10 (incl. its 60-day notice) and BCO 25-10 (prohibition on seizing congregational property against its will), adding express cross-references to those member/congregation protections that 5-2.c currently omits.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None. (Grounds invoke BCO 13-10 and BCO 25-10 as the protective provisions, but cite no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries by number.)

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[Judicial Case 92-1 — pastoral care of members of dissolved Grace Church, Braintree](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p196)** (GA21/1993, out_of_order) — Construes the very question 5-2.c addresses: a Presbytery's dissolution of a congregation and its duty to care for the enrolled members afterward (held Presbytery "does have the responsibility of providing for pastoral care by establishing a mission church or by providing pastoral care in some other way"). Directly bears on the overture's concern that members be cared for per BCO 13-10. [minutes](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p196)
- **[Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery (2024-5)](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p983)** (GA52/2025, granted) — Leading recent decision on BCO 5-2 mission churches: the rights of mission-church members and how a pastoral relationship is dissolved within a mission work. SJC distinguishes the (one-judge) *Harrell* concurrence and holds that BCO 5-5 assent does not give mission-church members the same congregational-vote protection as a particular church when a call is dissolved. Frames precisely the member-protection gap O17 seeks to close in 5-2.c. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p983)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found.

### Prior overtures
- **[GA9 O1](../overtures/ga09_1981__o1.md)** (1981, Answered by reference) — "Amend BCO 5-2 to Clarify Presbytery Oversight of Unorganized Congregations" (Presbytery of the Covenant). Earliest attempt to sharpen 5-2's treatment of presbytery oversight of unorganized/mission congregations — same provision, kindred aim. [page](../markdown/ga09_1981.md#ga09-p41)
- **[GA38 O15](../overtures/ga38_2010__o15.md)** (2010, Approved & ratified 2011) — "Revise BCO 5-2 Through 5-11 and Add New BCO 5-5 Regarding Church Organization" (Potomac, to CCB/OC). The wholesale restructuring of BCO 5 that produced the current 5-2.c text O17 now amends; the direct legislative ancestor of this section. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p368)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 5-2** — 2 citations, both [Central Florida](../rpr/central-florida.md) Presbytery (50th/2023 raised-open; 51st/2024 satisfactory-closed): "Presbytery assigned oversight of mission churches within its bounds to a different Presbytery." Real-world friction over presbytery oversight of mission churches under 5-2, the chapter O17 touches. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Provision-exact spine returned four cases; **pruned two as incidental**: *Complaint of the Session of Hope Community Church v. Central Carolina Presbytery* (2013-4, GA42) turns on a Session's BCO 12-5e authority over multi-site particularization and cites BCO 5-2 only in passing, not the dissolution/member-care question; and *Gordon v. Southern New England* (2020-6, GA49) is a jurisdiction/membership-vow (OPC↔PCA) case where 5-2 is incidental. Kept Case 92-1 (dissolution + member care) and Bigelow (mission-church member rights on dissolution) as squarely bearing. No renumbering affects BCO 5-2 itself: the one ch. 5 entry in bco_renumberings.jsonl (2011/GA39, "add new 5-5 & renumber") is an insert-and-shift that adds a new 5-5 and shifts only sections 5-5 and later, leaving 5-2 untouched; the modern 5-2.c text derives from GA38 O15 (2011). Caveat on GA9 O1: its corpus anchor (ga09-p41) lands on a page that also carries a licensure overture; the cited subject/title is the 5-2 oversight overture matched by body+title. Companion protective provisions named in the grounds — BCO 13-10 (notice) and BCO 25-10 (property) — are worth cross-checking against any GA53 overtures touching those chapters.

---

## O18 — Amend BCO 5-4 to Allow a Mother Church to Call a Church Planter
**Targets:** BCO 5-4 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-18_Westminster_5-4.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-18_Westminster_5-4.pdf)

**What it does:** Inserts a new option into BCO 5-4's list of how pastoral ministry for a mission church may be provided — a minister of the Presbytery called by the Session of the "mother" church to serve as pastor (cross-referencing BCO 5-2.a.ii and 5-3.b), still requiring Presbytery's approval. Recognizes the mother–daughter church-planting model, where the mother church usually supplies most funding and often the planter, by letting the call originate from the mother church's Session rather than only from Presbytery.

**Cites in its own grounds:** No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries. It cites only BCO provisions: 5-2, 5-3, 5-2.a.ii, 5-3.b, 22-5, 22-6, and 12-5.e.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-5 — Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-05.md)** (GA52/2025, granted) — Directly bearing real-world friction. TE Bigelow served as Assistant Pastor of a mother church (Christ Church East) while also serving as planting pastor of its daughter mission church (Christ Church Beaches); the dispute concerned dissolution of that call. The SJC opinion construes BCO 5-4 alongside 5-2, 5-3, and 12-5.e — the exact provision cluster O18 amends — and illustrates the very mother–daughter church-planting arrangement the overture seeks to regularize. [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p983)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found.

### Prior overtures
- **[GA8 O15](../overtures/ga08_1980__o15.md)** (1981, Approved & ratified) — Mid-Atlantic, "Add BCO 5-4 on calling pastors in new congregations." The original adoption of BCO 5-4 itself — the foundational text O18 amends. [page](../markdown/ga08_1980.md#ga08-p40)
- **[GA38 O11](../overtures/ga38_2010__o11.md)** (2011, Approved & ratified) — Blue Ridge, "Amend BCO 5-3 to Allow Latitude in Oversight of Mission Churches." Topical supplement: companion chapter-5 reform liberalizing the mother/daughter oversight relationship O18 builds on. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p356)
- **[GA44 O38](../overtures/ga44_2016__o38.md)** (2017, Approved & ratified) — Pacific Northwest, "Amend BCO 5-3 to Require Minute Reporting for Mission Church Governments." Topical supplement: closely-related recent chapter-5 mission-church amendment. [page](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p638)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 5-4** — 3 citations. Strongest: [Wisconsin](../rpr/wisconsin.md) Presbytery flagged twice (49th/2022, unsatisfactory-outstanding; 51st/2024, raised-open): "The nature of provision for pastoral ministry for a mission church not clearly defined" — recurring real-world friction on the exact subject of 5-4 that O18 aims to clarify. Also [Siouxlands](../rpr/exc/siouxlands__040.md) (28th/2000): improper procedure organizing a particular church (BCO 5-4,5,6,7,8). [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Cross-link: O18 is part of Westminster's chapter-5 mission-church suite (companion O17 amends BCO 5-2). Critically, GA53 O2 (Wisconsin) ALSO amends BCO 5-4 ("Consent of Mission Church Members in Calling a Pastor"), so two GA53 overtures edit the same section and must be harmonized by CCB. The exact-provision spine returned only case 2024-5 (Bigelow) and only title-matched prior overture GA8 O15; both kept as strongly bearing. Added under Step 3c (closely-related provisions): GA38 O11 and GA44 O38, two chapter-5 mission-church amendments showing the recent reform trajectory. Pruned from the first pass: the 1981-4 King case (mission church but not the 5-4 call-origin question — incidental), and the GA44 CI / GA38 O15 / GA9 O7 citations, which lacked verifiable corpus deep-links in the deterministic spine. No renumbering of BCO 5-4 found in bco_renumberings.jsonl, so older actions cite the same number. No inquiries or CCB advice on 5-4. No GA48–52 prior overtures on 5-4, so no ⭐.

---

## O19 — Amend BCO 5-8 to Include Ecclesiastical Government
**Targets:** BCO 5-8 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-19_Westminster_5-8.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-19_Westminster_5-8.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 5-8 by adding two words so that mission churches "enjoy the same status as particular churches in relation to civil *and ecclesiastical* government," extending the existing civil-government parity to ecclesiastical government as well.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — the whereas clauses argue only from the text of BCO 5-8 and the nature of mission-church supervision; no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries are cited.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[1981-4 — Teaching Elder Rodney King, et al. v. Presbytery of Western Carolinas](../cases/ga09_1981__case3.md)** (9th/1981, Complaint not sustained) — Construes a presbytery's ecclesiastical authority over a mission church: the presbytery declined to allow a mission church to organize for a year, and the complaint over that exercise of supervisory authority was not sustained. Bears on the very relationship O19 addresses (mission- vs. particular-church status under ecclesiastical government), though it construes presbytery organizing authority generally rather than the text of BCO 5-8. [minutes](../markdown/ga09_1981.md#ga09-p224)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found.

### Prior overtures
- **[GA38 O15](../overtures/ga38_2010__o15.md)** (2010, Approved & ratified 2011) — Potomac, "Revise BCO 5-2 Through 5-11 and Add New BCO 5-5 Regarding Church Organization." The comprehensive 2011 restructure of Chapter 5 that produced the current 5-8 text and its "civil government"-only wording — the most directly relevant prior amendment to the very provision O19 now seeks to broaden. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p368)
- **[GA38 O11](../overtures/ga38_2010__o11.md)** (2010, Approved & ratified 2011) — Blue Ridge, "Amend BCO 5-3 to Allow Latitude in Oversight of Mission Churches." Same 2010–11 mission-church revision cycle; bears on the degree of presbytery/ecclesiastical oversight of mission churches that O19's parity language touches. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p356)
- **[GA44 O38](../overtures/ga44_2016__o38.md)** (2016, Approved & ratified 2017) — Pacific Northwest, "Amend BCO 5-3 to Require Minute Reporting for Mission Church Governments." More recent action on the ecclesiastical governance/reporting of mission churches — the same subject of mission-church ecclesiastical standing. [page](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p638)
- **[GA9 O19](../overtures/ga09_1981__o19.md)** (1981, Adopted final) — Western Carolinas, "Develop Procedures for Organizing Congregations and Ordaining Officers." Early action on the organization of mission/unorganized congregations into particular churches — the practical context of the mission-vs-particular distinction in BCO 5-8. [page](../markdown/ga09_1981.md#ga09-p51)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 5-8** — 5 presbytery-minute exceptions cite this provision, all concerning failures in the organization/particularization of mission churches: [Philadelphia](../rpr/philadelphia.md) (19th/1991, raised), [Korean Southern](../rpr/korean-southern.md) (33rd/2005, satisfactory), [Northern Illinois](../rpr/northern-illinois.md) (34th/2006, unsatisfactory), [Chicago Metro](../rpr/chicago-metro.md) (36th/2008, satisfactory), [Eastern Canada](../rpr/exc/eastern-canada__012.md) (36th/2008, unsatisfactory — "no record of change from a mission to particular church"). They show recurring real-world friction over presbytery supervision of mission churches under 5-8 — the practical backdrop to clarifying ecclesiastical-government status. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Provision-exact spine returned zero cases, inquiries, or prior overtures for BCO 5-8 and 5 RPR rows. The judicial case and the four prior overtures above are TOPICAL supplements (matched by concept — "mission church," "organization," and the BCO 5 chapter rewrites — since the spine is provision-exact and older actions either predate the modern numbering or cite §5-3/5-2 rather than 5-8). Renumbering caveat: Chapter 5 was restructured at GA39 (2011, bco_renumberings.jsonl chapter "5": new 5-5 inserted, 5-5+ shifted +1), so pre-2011 actions cite different section numbers — the modern 5-8 originated in the GA38 O15 rewrite. O19 is part of Westminster's BCO 5 cluster at GA53: companion to verified **O17** (5-2 dissolution of mission churches), **O18** (5-4 mother church calling a planter), and **O20** (new 5-C, churches without a governing body) — all Westminster, all Chapter 5. No GA48–52 actions found, hence no starred recent overtures. Because the change is a narrow two-word clarification, the most load-bearing material is the GA38 O15 rewrite of this chapter and the King case construing presbytery ecclesiastical authority over a mission church.

---

## O20 — Add to BCO 5 a Section "C. Churches Without a Governing Body"
**Targets:** BCO 5 (new Section C, paragraphs 5-11 to 5-14) · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-20_Westminster_5C.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-20_Westminster_5C.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a new Section C to BCO 5 for a particular church that, due to extraordinary circumstances, cannot provide government (BCO 12-1) from its own membership: the Presbytery may appoint a transitory Session of elders from within its bounds (5-11), which must seek the congregation's concurrence and move toward electing elders under BCO 24 or affiliation under BCO 2-2 / 25-11 (5-12); a particular church may be changed to a mission church only by a 3/4 Presbytery vote with members cited and given opportunity to concur or petition, and the reasons recorded (5-13); and each member retains the right to complain under BCO 43 (5-14).

**Cites in its own grounds:** No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by name. Cites only constitutional text — Preliminary Principle 6, BCO 12-1, BCO 24, BCO 13-9, BCO 2-2, BCO 25-11, BCO 43 — and observes the issue "has arisen through the process of review and control."

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2016-14 — Wills v. Metro Atlanta Presbytery](../cases/ga45_2017__2016-14.md)** (GA45/2017, denied) — Construes BCO 13-9(f): Presbytery has inherent authority to dissolve a church without a mandated procedure. The overture would supply exactly such a procedure for the cognate act of changing a particular church to mission status (3/4 vote, citation of members, recorded reasons, right to complain). [minutes](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p543)
- **[1991-2 — Nickoley and Stephens v. Southwest Presbytery](../cases/ga20_1992__1991-02.md)** (GA20/1992, not sustained) — Held the Presbytery correctly determined it lacked constitutional authority to suspend a session or act as a "Session pro tem." Bears directly on the overture's novel "transitory Session" device, which would for the first time expressly authorize a Presbytery-appointed session. [minutes](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p142)
- **[2022-7 — Harrell et al. v. Covenant Presbytery](../cases/ga50_2023__2022-07.md)** (GA50/2023, sustained) — Members of a mission church were censured by a provisional Session; SJC reversed, addressing provisional-Session authority and congregational rights (BCO 5). Bears on the protections the overture builds in for members under a Presbytery-appointed/transitory Session. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p852)
- **[2024-5 — Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-05.md)** (GA52/2025, granted) — Mission-church governance dispute involving a provisional session, dissolution of a call, and congregational rights under BCO 5/12-5; SJC found Presbytery erred. Illustrates the governance-gap friction (provisional/transitory session, member rights) the overture targets. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p981)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **App. O II.E (GA39/2011)** — "Temporary governance for churches lacking ruling elders": CCB found a proposed overture on temporary governance for elder-less churches *may have conflicted* with the Constitution if read as prescriptive under Preliminary Principles 2 and 6 and BCO 12-1. Closest prior action; this overture revives that project and must navigate the same conflict caution. [page](../inquiries/ga39_2011__ci01.md)
- **12-53 III, 62 (GA12/1984)** — "Minimum ruling elders required to constitute a valid session": one RE plus a pastor is a valid session; a church without a pastor needs at least two REs (BCO 12-1). Defines the very "no governing body" threshold the overture's 5-11 presupposes. [page](../inquiries/ga12_1984__ci08.md)
- **CI #15 (GA14/1986)** — "Whether a congregation may dissolve the session": a congregation cannot dissolve its session, but Presbytery may assume jurisdiction under BCO 13-9. Bears on the overture's allocation of authority between congregation and Presbytery when a church loses its governing body. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci18.md)
- **16-77 III (GA16/1988)** — "Membership status and session authority upon dissolution of a congregation": on dissolution the session terminates and membership is dissolved for those not transferred; Presbytery may not unilaterally reassign members. Bears on the member rights the overture's 5-13/5-14 seek to protect on a change of status. [page](../inquiries/ga16_1988__ci08.md)
- **App. O II.G (GA44/2016)** — On a mission-church government overture, CCB found conflict with BCO 5-3.a (an evangelist has no minutes to submit). Shows CCB's exacting scrutiny of BCO 5 mission-church amendments; relevant to how 5-C will be reviewed. [page](../inquiries/ga44_2016__ci02.md)

### Prior overtures
- **GA41 O2 (2013, Referred)** — North Texas, "Amend BCO 5-1, 5-2, 5-9 and Add Sections 5-11 and 5-12 Regarding Mission Churches." A prior attempt to add new 5-11/5-12 to BCO 5; this overture occupies the same numbering space (5-11 to 5-14). [page](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p816)
- **GA42 O2 (2014, Out of order)** — North Texas, renewed "Amend BCO 5-1, 5-2, 5-9 and Add Sections 5-11, 5-12 Regarding Mission Churches"; ruled out of order. Same provision real estate; cautionary precedent. [page](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p253)
- **GA30 O25 (2002)** — Ascension, "Revise BCO 12-2, Add 12-11, Revise 25-6 & 15-1 Regarding Non-Functioning Sessions." Earlier attempt to solve the very "non-functioning session" problem — via Chapter 12 — that this overture now handles in Chapter 5. [page](../markdown/ga30_2002.md#ga30-p76)
- **GA38 O15 (2010, Approved & ratified 2011)** — Potomac, "Revise BCO 5-2 Through 5-11 and Add New BCO 5-5 Regarding Church Organization." The restructure that set Chapter 5's current shape and the 5-x numbering; the framework into which 5-C must fit. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p368)
- **GA12 O33 (1984, Approved but not ratified)** — Covenant, "Amend BCO 11-4 to Clarify Presbytery Authority to Dissolve Sessions." A prior attempt to fix the same gap (presbytery power over a church's session) that failed ratification. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p56)
- **GA24 O28 (1996, Answered in the negative)** — Potomac, "Amend BCO 13-9f to Clarify Dissolving Churches." A rejected attempt to define how a church is dissolved or changed in status. [page](../markdown/ga24_1996.md#ga24-p54)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 13-9 / 5-3 (interim/temporary session)** — Recurrent friction where a presbytery improvises governance for a church without a session — the exact problem the overture addresses: **[Potomac](../rpr/exc/potomac__009.md), 39th (2011)** — "appointed a commission to act as the interim session" (BCO 3-1, 13-9, 16-1, 25-8ff); **[Eastern Canada](../rpr/exc/eastern-canada__018.md), 40th (2012)** — "may not assign a temporary session without the concurrence of the church"; **[Illiana](../rpr/illiana.md), 22nd (1994)** — "no notation of congregational approval of a commission replacing the session"; **[Korean Southwest](../rpr/exc/korean-southwest__232.md), 52nd (2025)** — "received organized churches without sessions and without providing rationale." The overture's concurrence requirement (5-12) and recorded-reasons requirement (5-13) respond directly to these. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 12-1** — **[Grace](../rpr/exc/grace__028.md), 51st (2024)** — Presbytery "approved REs to 'augment' church sessions apart from constitutional election"; shows presbyteries straining BCO 12-1 where a church cannot constitute its own session. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Spine join returned provisions=[] (non-provision overture adding a *new* section), so there were no exact-provision spine hits to inherit; every citation here comes from a topical corpus search (BCO 5 mission-church / "temporary government," BCO 12-1 session constitution, BCO 13-9(f) dissolution, and "transitory/provisional/interim session"). **Numbering collision:** GA53 O51 (MS Valley, "Amend BCO 5 to add a Section on 'Assisted Churches'") also adds a new 5-11 to BCO 5 — the two cannot both pass as written; cross-check O51. Also part of a Westminster BCO 5 cluster (companions O17–O19). **Renumbering caveat:** Chapter 5 was last restructured by GA38 O15 (ratified 2011), which shifted 5-5+; the prior 5-11/5-12 proposals (GA41/42 O2) were never ratified, so the 5-11..5-14 slots are currently free. **Pruned as incidental:** *Melton et al. v. Tennessee Valley Presbytery* (1990-5, GA19) — case is about proxy voting rules and Robert's Rules at a congregational dissolution meeting (BCO 24-4, 13-9, 11-4, 43); it does not construe presbytery authority to appoint transitory sessions or the BCO 5 new-Section-C procedures the overture adds. Kim v. Korean Eastern (2005-9, admin-commission pastoral dissolution — different question), Hope Community v. Central Carolina (2013-4, session vs. presbytery over a worship site — tangential), Lovelace v. Northeast (1991-6, complainant standing — tangential), and the GA22/GA23 dissolution overtures (cumulative with GA24 O28). Also dropped the first pass's unverifiable "2018-4 / 1985-5 / 2001-1" case string and its non-deep-link citations.

## O21 — Amend BCO 13-6 to Clarify Exams for Ministers from Another Denomination
**Targets:** BCO 13-6 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/Overture-21_Westminster_13-6.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/Overture-21_Westminster_13-6.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 13-6.b so that a minister transferring from another denomination is examined "thoroughly as required by the trials listed in BCO 21-4.a, 21-4.c(1), 21-4.c(4), and 21-4.e and any additional trials deemed necessary," rather than under all of BCO 21-4 — pruning the thesis/exegetical-paper requirements that the pre-52nd-GA "knowledge and views" standard never imposed. Preserves the ordination-questions requirement (BCO 21-5) and the extraordinary-provisions sentence.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None by case/overture number. The grounds react to "the recent amendment" of BCO 13-6 made prior to the 52nd GA (the GA51 O2 / O27 changes below) and cross-reference companion GA53 Overture 25.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2015-13 — Barnes v. Heartland Presbytery](../cases/ga45_2017__2015-13.md)** (GA45/2017, sustained) — construes the adequacy of presbytery examination under BCO 13-6, the same examination-scope question the overture clarifies. [minutes](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p480)
- **[2022-21 — Senters v. Savannah River Presbytery](../cases/ga51_2024__2022-21.md)** (GA51/2024, not sustained) — recent complaint turning on what BCO 13-6 requires when receiving a minister; bears on the examination standard being amended. [minutes](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p721)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **7-41 III, 21** (GA7/1979) — CCB advised BCO 13-6 requires ordination questions be put to any minister from another denomination, and presbytery may require re-ordination if deemed necessary; directly construes the transfer-examination subject the overture refines. [page](../inquiries/ga07_1979__ci01.md)
- **CI #16** (GA13/1985) — CCB advised that neither BCO 13-6 nor BCO 21-4 contains an extraordinary clause applicable to ministers transferring from other denominations; bears on the extraordinary-provisions sentence the overture retains. [page](../inquiries/ga13_1985__ci12.md)
- **34-34 IV.B** (GA34/2006) — CCB advice on conduct of presbytery examinations under BCO 13-6/21-4 (use of translators), construing the same exam framework. [page](../inquiries/ga34_2006__ci03.md)
- **II.B** (GA51/2024) — CCB found no conflict in amending BCO 13-6 for greater clarity in transferring ordination (Overture 2, Northern California); the immediately prior amendment this overture reacts to. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci02.md)
- **II.V** (GA51/2024) — CCB found amending BCO 13-6 to add character/family-management to transfer examinations not in conflict (Overture 27, Potomac); same recent reshaping of 13-6 transfer exams. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci22.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA25 O1](../overtures/ga25_1997__o1.md)** (1997, Approved & ratified 1998) — "Amend BCO 13-6 to Require Full Examination of Transfers" (Southwest Florida); the origin of the full-examination standard this overture now narrows. [page](../markdown/ga25_1997.md#ga25-p49)
- **[GA37 O8](../overtures/ga37_2009__o8.md)** (2009, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 13-6 to Clarify Examinations for Men Coming from Other Denominations" (Ascension); a prior attempt at substantially the same clarification, rejected. [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p275)
- **[GA37 O9](../overtures/ga37_2009__o9.md)** (2009, Approved & ratified 2011) — "Amend BCO 13-6 to Require Men from Other Denominations to Declare Differences with the Confession" (Ascension); shaped the current transfer-exam text. [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p276)
- **[GA51 O2](../overtures/ga51_2024__o2.md)** (2024, Approved & ratified 2025) — "Amend BCO 13-6 for Clarity in Transfers of Ordination" (Northern California); part of "the recent amendment" the overture's grounds respond to. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1060)
- **[GA51 O27](../overtures/ga51_2024__o27.md)** (2024, Approved & ratified 2025) — "Amend BCO 13-6 to Add Personal Character and Family Management to Transfer Examination" (Potomac); the most recent change to 13-6.b examination scope. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1179)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 13-6** — 309 RPR citations, overwhelmingly presbytery-minutes deficiencies in transfer/reception examinations (e.g., [North Florida](../rpr/north-florida.md) 28th/2000: "No evidence that the TE was examined on Sacraments and Church Government"; [Korean Capital](../rpr/exc/korean-capital__007.md) 25th/1997: "Incomplete record of transfer exam for minister of another denomination"); the real-world record-keeping friction that motivates clarifying what 13-6 actually requires. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Companion: GA53 **Overture 25** also touches BCO 21-4 numbering, and O21's PDF includes a NOTE specifying how its BCO 21-4 cross-references renumber if both pass — treat the two as a coordinated pair. No renumbering of BCO 13 itself (bco_renumberings.jsonl is silent on chapter 13), so the old-number search step is moot; 13-6 has been provision-stable. **Pruned as incidental:** *Evans v. Arizona Presbytery* (2023-7, GA51) — case is about withdrawal from the denomination and divestiture without censure under BCO 38-3a; BCO 13-6 is cited only in passing and the case has nothing to do with transfer-examination scope.

**Pruned as incidental** from the high-recall spine: the cluster of GA50–51 background-check actions (CCB II.C/II.E/II.K/II.L/II.R/II.S; Overtures GA50 O6, GA51 O16/O17/O23/O24) — these amend 13-6 to add background checks, a different question from examination scope; CCB items II.U/II.Z (moral-qualification overtures co-citing 13-6 only in passing); inquiry 24-23 ref. #2 (session re-examination of RE/deacon nominees); and the body+title overture matches unrelated to 13-6 (GA19 O1, GA20 O29, GA21 O23, GA24 O1, GA29 O7, GA38 O28, GA43 O7, GA50 O13). Of the cases, Jones v. Louisiana (2007-8), Edison v. Southwest Florida (2009-11), Reese and Bech (2011-14), Aven (2016-1), Schrock (2019-2), and Klett (2022-3) cite 13-6 within broader complaints not centered on transfer-exam scope and were pruned in favor of the three that most directly construe the examination standard.

## O22 — Amend BCO 13-8 to Apply Only to Churches from Outside the PCA
**Targets:** BCO 13-8 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-22_Westminster_13-8.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-22_Westminster_13-8.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds "from outside of the Presbyterian Church in America" to BCO 13-8 so the commission-to-examine and re-affirmation-of-ordination-vows requirement applies only to churches joining from outside the PCA — not to a PCA congregation already in the denomination that a General Assembly boundary change moves from one presbytery to another (such transfers to be regarded as immediate).

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — the whereas clauses reason from the text of 13-8 and the boundary-change scenario; no prior case, overture, or inquiry is named.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2020-06 — Gordon v. Southern New England Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2020-06.md)** (GA49/2022, denied) — directly applies BCO 13-8: First Presbyterian Church North Shore left the OPC and joined the PCA, and the SNEP commission interviewed its ruling elders "in accordance with BCO 13-8." The appeal (and a dissent) turned on jurisdiction over a member when a church is received into the PCA. This is the exact "church from outside the PCA" reception that O22 preserves, and shows 13-8 functioning as intended on external reception. [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p719)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found. (The spine surfaced inquiry **10-23** (GA10/1982), but it lists BCO 13-8 only in passing among provisions on Committee-of-Commissioners authority over MtW cooperative agreements — wholly unrelated to receiving churches; pruned.)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA6 O33](../overtures/ga06_1978__o33.md)** (1978) — "Amend BCO by Adding BCO 14-7 Requiring Elder Examination Before Receiving Churches"; the historical origin of the elder-examination-on-reception duty now housed in BCO 13-8. Bears as the enacting rationale O22 narrows. [page](../markdown/ga06_1978.md#ga06-p38)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 13-8** — 29 citations of presbytery minutes lacking the required commission/elder-examination record on receiving a church; many concern churches *transferring into or petitioning to join the PCA* (e.g., [Korean Eastern](../rpr/korean-eastern.md) 49th/2022 & 51st/2024: "no record of examination of elders for a church that has petitioned to join the PCA"; [Korean Southern](../rpr/korean-southern.md) 49th/2022: "received a new church into its membership without examining its ruling elders"; [Korean Northwest](../rpr/korean-northwest.md) 48th/2021 & 51st/2024: "no record of commission of Presbytery meeting with church ruling elders before receiving the church"). This recurring friction is the live evidence behind O22's premise that 13-8's exam duty is meaningful on external reception. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Built on the deterministic BCO 13-8 spine. PRUNED as incidental: inquiry **10-23** (1982, MtW cooperative agreements — 13-8 cited only in a provision list) and prior overtures **GA18 O4 / O9** (1990, OPC union and joining-and-receiving under BCO 14-6 — matched only by the keyword "receiving," not a prior attempt at this 13-8 change). KEPT after verification: case **2020-06 Gordon**, which the first pass nearly treated as marginal but in fact construes 13-8 reception squarely. **[GA6 O33](../overtures/ga06_1978__o33.md)** is a verified topical supplement from /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md (not the provision-exact spine), because the duty originated under a then-proposed section number before the 1982 Chapter 13 rework; no formal renumbering record for chapter 13 was found in bco_renumberings.jsonl. Companion check: any GA53 boundary/reception overtures should be cross-linked, since O22's mechanism depends on GA boundary changes taking effect without re-examination.

---

## O23 — Restructure and Renumber BCO 14 for Clarity and Ease of Reference
**Targets:** BCO 14 (entire chapter; also cross-references in BCO, RAO, OMSJC, Corporate Bylaws) · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-23_Westminster_14.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-23_Westminster_14.pdf)

**What it does:** Purely structural cleanup — breaks the overloaded BCO 14-1 (15 subsections covering GA organization principles, the Nominating Committee, permanent committees, personnel/salaries, the Theological Examining Committee, and floor procedure) into separate numbered sections, renumbers the rest of the chapter, and conforms cross-references in the BCO, RAO, OMSJC, and Corporate Bylaws. Worked example in the grounds: old "14-1.12.b.4" becomes "14-3.2.d." No substantive change of meaning is intended.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None. The grounds cite no prior case, overture, or inquiry — only the bare fact that "BCO Chapter 14 has been proposed for amendment approximately forty (40) times … with seven (7) of those proposed changes being ratified," leaving the chapter disordered.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (The provision-exact spine returned no provisions for this whole-chapter overture; topical case search surfaced only RAO 14 / case-number "14-" false matches and Chin v. Covenant 2003-4 — a Lord's-Supper-admission complaint whose "14-7" reference does not construe the GA-organization Chapter 14 that O23 renumbers. Pruned as incidental.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **10-23** (GA10/1982) — construed BCO 14-1-5, 14-1-7, and 14-6 on committee-of-commissioners vs. commission authority and the Assembly's retained authority; one of the subsections O23 re-sections (confirms cross-references must be conformed, not the meaning changed). [page](../inquiries/ga10_1982__ci01.md)
- **13-27** (GA13/1985) — construed BCO 14-1-12 (trustee nominations / eligibility of an expired-term trustee). [page](../inquiries/ga13_1985__ci01.md)
- **30-29 Item 2** (GA30/2002) — construed BCO 14-1.4 (held GA cannot mandate minister health coverage); shows 14-1's substantive subsections that the renumbering must preserve verbatim. [page](../inquiries/ga30_2002__ci07.md)
- **III.B** (GA47/2019) — construed BCO 14-1.12 on consecutive permanent-committee service; recent CCB reading of the very subsection O23 would re-letter to 14-3. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci23.md)

### Prior overtures
Chapter 14 has the corpus's longest amendment history; O23 is the first comprehensive restructure/renumber rather than a substantive change. Representative bearing attempts (none a prior renumbering):
- **[GA8 O16](../overtures/ga08_1980__o16.md)** (1980, Approved & ratified 1981) — amend BCO 14-1 on teaching/ruling elder balance. [page](../markdown/ga08_1980.md#ga08-p41)
- **[GA29 O1](../overtures/ga29_2001__o1.md)** (2001, Approved & ratified 2002) — amend BCO 14-1(12), increase committee size and extend terms. [page](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p55)
- **[GA46 O26](../overtures/ga46_2018__o26.md)** (2018, Answered in the negative 76-32-3) — amend BCO 14-1.11 re non-ordained Covenant College trustees. [page](../markdown/ga46_2018.md#ga46-p722)
- **[GA47 O8](../overtures/ga47_2019__o8.md)** (2019, Answered in the negative) — amend BCO 14-1.10/.11/.12 to allow non-ordained persons on committees/boards (one of a five-presbytery cluster that year). [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p601)
- **[GA51 O31](../overtures/ga51_2024__o31.md)** (2024, Answered in the negative) — amend BCO 14-1 to clarify permanent-committee and agency policy authority. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1187)
- **[GA52 O9](../overtures/ga52_2025__o9.md)** (2025, Referred back to Presbytery 75-51-1) — amend BCO 14-1 to make committee-appointed AC members non-voting. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p120)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 14-6.c / 14-6c** — 5 citations combined (e.g., [Susquehanna Valley](../rpr/exc/susquehanna-valley__050.md) 48th/2021; [Missouri](../rpr/missouri.md) 46th/2018; [Great Lakes](../rpr/great-lakes.md) 40th/2012), all for missing executive-session minutes. Marginally bearing: it is exactly such live cross-references to "14-6" that O23 must conform when it renumbers the chapter. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 14-1.11** — 1 citation ([Heritage](../rpr/heritage.md) 40th/2012, alternate serving on a committee of commissioners). [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 14-9.b** — 1 citation ([Nashville](../rpr/nashville.md) 51st/2024). [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
This is a non-substantive formatting/renumbering overture, so by design it has no true "bearing precedent"; the cases, inquiries, overtures, and RPR rows above are listed to show the live references that O23 must conform, not as adverse authority. Pruning: the spine returned provisions=[] (whole-chapter overture), so all results here come from topical index search; RAO 14-x and case-number "14-" hits, and Chin v. Covenant 2003-4, were dropped as false/incidental matches. The real practical risk is collision with any GA53 overture that substantively amends Chapter 14 — if such a companion passes alongside O23, the two renumbering/amendment texts must be reconciled. No chapter-wide BCO 14 renumbering exists in the corpus to use as a drafting precedent.

## O24 — Amend BCO 15-2 to Clarify that Presbytery Itself Must Conduct Ordination Exams
**Targets:** BCO 15-2 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-24_Westminster_15-2.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-24_Westminster_15-2.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds language to BCO 15-2 — "Presbytery shall always conduct the final trials of examination for ordination. A committee of Presbytery may conduct preliminary examinations, but the examination required for ordination must be sustained before the Presbytery itself." It closes the gap that the current text (which only requires Presbytery to conduct the "previous examination" when ordination is committed to a commission) does not explicitly forbid a commission from conducting the entire ordination examination.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — the grounds reason only from the existing text of BCO 15-2; no cases, overtures, or inquiries are named.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (All 15 spine cases cite BCO 15-2 only for commission quorum, judicial-commission constitution, or judicial process — none construes the ordination-examination clause this overture clarifies. See Note.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI #15** (GA13/1985) — CCB advised that BCO 15-2's list of matters assignable to commissions is "typical but not exhaustive," other matters assignable subject to review and control; bears on the outer limit of what Presbytery may delegate to a commission, which is the precise concern O24 sharpens. [page](../inquiries/ga13_1985__ci11.md)
- **II.M** (GA49/2022) — CCB found a proposed BCO 15-2 amendment (Overture 19 from Northwest Georgia) clarifying commission membership and quorum "not in conflict" with the BCO; bears as the most recent CCB engagement amending the same section and as a review template for a 15-2 amendment. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci13.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA6 O19](../overtures/ga06_1978__o19.md)** (1978, Answered in the negative) — Covenant, "Amend BCO 15-2 to Remove Cap on Commissioners from a Single Congregation"; earliest 15-2 commission overture, same provision but on composition, not exams. [p.38](../markdown/ga06_1978.md#ga06-p38)
- **[GA14 O2](../overtures/ga14_1986__o2.md)** (1986, Answered by reference) — Western Carolina, "Amend BCO to Require Final Ordination Exams on the Full Presbytery Floor"; a prior attempt at exactly O24's concern — that the whole presbytery, not a commission, must conduct ordination exams. [p.50](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p50)
- **[GA18 O11](../overtures/ga18_1990__o11.md)** (1990) — Eastern Canada, "Amend BCO 15-2 Regarding Quorum of Commission as Session"; same provision, commission-quorum question. [p.73](../markdown/ga18_1990.md#ga18-p71)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 15-2** — 105 RPR rows cite this section, but only a few construe the ordination-examination clause O24 targets (the rest concern commission *quorum/composition*, incidental here). Squarely on point: **[Mid-America](../rpr/exc/mid-america__003.md) 21st (1993)** — "Presbytery cannot entrust an ordination examination to a commission (BCO 15-2, last sentence)"; **[Southern New England](../rpr/exc/southern-new-england__015.md) 35th (2007)** — "Only Presbytery as a whole can conduct examination of minister from another denomination. BCO 15-2"; and **[Korean Southeastern](../rpr/korean-southeastern.md) 52nd (2025)** — incomplete record of ordination exam, citing "When the ordination of a minister is committed to a commission, the Presbytery…". These show recurring real-world friction over exactly the clause being clarified. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Highest-value bearing action (found via concept search, missed by the provision-exact spine): **[GA14 O2](../overtures/ga14_1986__o2.md)** (1986, Western Carolina, Answered by reference to Overture 4) — overtured to amend the BCO "to make it clear that the final examination for candidacy, licensure and ordination must be conducted by the presbytery as a whole and not be delegated to a commission," accepting a Judicial Business Committee ruling on matters properly executed by commissions. This is the direct precursor — same change, same rationale — and is recorded at [ga14_1986 p.50](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p50). Cross-link: GA49 O19 (Northwest Georgia) amended BCO 15-2 on commission membership/quorum (CCB review at II.M above) — a different clause of the same section, useful as drafting/review precedent. Renumbering caveat: BCO ch. 15 was renumbered at the 17th GA (1989; new 15-1..15-5 inserted, old 15-4→15-6), but the commission provisions have stood as 15-2 throughout the period of these actions, so no old-number search was needed. Pruning: ALL 15 spine judicial cases pruned as incidental (Lee, Kim, DeJong, Dunn, Pesnell, Wills, Speck, Woodward, Marshall, Fitzsimmons, Mays, and the GA36 decision — all commission-quorum / judicial-process, not the exam clause); inquiries 14-44 and CI #14 pruned (judicial/visitation commissions, not ordination exams); the bulk of the 105 RPR quorum/composition rows pruned; and the RAO 15-2 RPR row (Piedmont Triad) pruned as a false hit on a different code (RAO ≠ BCO).
