## O25 — Restructure and Amend BCO 21-1 through 21-4 for Clarity, Consistency, and Ease of Reference
**Targets:** BCO 21-1..21-4 (renumbers the remainder of BCO 21 and cross-references in BCO/RAO/OMSJC accordingly) · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/Overture-25_Westminster_21.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/Overture-25_Westminster_21.pdf)

**What it does:** Restructures and renumbers BCO 21-1 through 21-4 — consolidating overlapping/repeated ordination-and-installation clauses into a cleaner flow (e.g., folding old 21-2 into 21-1, regrouping the educational/examination requirements under a new "Ordination Requirements and Procedures" head), and renumbering the rest of the chapter. The overture expressly states it "does not alter the substance of the ordination process but simply restructures and renumbers the chapter for clarity."

**Cites in its own grounds:** No specific case, overture, or inquiry is cited. The grounds rest on one aggregate fact — "BCO Chapter 21 has been proposed for amendment thirty-six (36) times in the history of the PCA, with seven (7) of those proposals being ratified" — i.e., the accumulated piecemeal amendments are themselves the problem. (A drafting NOTE flags companion GA53 Overture 21; see Note.)

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[1976-2 — Trinity Church, Slidell, LA v. Grace Pby](../markdown/ga04_1976.md#ga04-p52)** (GA4/1976, administratively out of order) — construes BCO 21-1 (call/permission before ministerial labor); bears on the 21-1 text being consolidated. [minutes](../markdown/ga04_1976.md#ga04-p52)
- **[2011-14 — Reese and Bech v. Philadelphia Presbytery](../cases/ga42_2014__2011-14.md)** (GA42/2014, sustained) — construes BCO 21-1 (presbytery handling of a call); bears on the provision being restructured. [minutes](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p530)
- **[1980-4 — Bogue et al. v. Ascension Presbytery](../markdown/ga08_1980.md#ga08-p52)** (GA8/1980, sustained in part) — construes BCO 21-1 and 21-4 (ordination examination / extraordinary reception); bears on the examination text being regrouped. [minutes](../markdown/ga08_1980.md#ga08-p52)
- **[2015-13 — Barnes v. Heartland Presbytery](../cases/ga45_2017__2015-13.md)** (GA45/2017, sustained) — construes BCO 21-4 (examination/exceptions); bears on the 21-4 procedural text being moved. [minutes](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p480)
- **[2022-21 — Senters v. Savannah River Presbytery](../cases/ga51_2024__2022-21.md)** (GA51/2024, not sustained) — recent construal of BCO 21-4 examination requirements; bears on the 21-4 text. [minutes](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p721)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **22-13 (2)** (GA22/1994) — sequence of placing a call versus examining a candidate under BCO 21-1; directly construes the ordering/flow of 21-1, the provision being consolidated. [page](../inquiries/ga22_1994__ci01.md)
- **15-83 III,21** (GA15/1987) — jurisdiction over candidates/licentiates moving to a new field under BCO 21-1, 21-2; bears on the 21-1/21-2 consolidation. [page](../inquiries/ga15_1987__ci07.md)
- **13-45 III,61** (GA13/1985) — proper limits on presbyterial use of the BCO 21-4 extraordinary clause; construes the 21-4 text being regrouped. [page](../inquiries/ga13_1985__ci04.md)
- **16-77 III,9** (GA16/1988) — scope of the extraordinary clause for ordination candidates (BCO 21-4); bears on the educational-requirement text moved into the new 21-3/21-4 head. [page](../inquiries/ga16_1988__ci02.md)
- **30-29 III** (CCB, GA30/2002) — found a mandate to report ordination exceptions in conflict with BCO 21-4; construes the exception-handling text being restructured. [page](../inquiries/ga30_2002__ci04.md)
- **31-56 VI** (CCB, GA31/2003) — split advice on specifying procedure for handling ordination exceptions in BCO 21-4; directly construes the 21-4 procedural text. [page](../inquiries/ga31_2003__ci04.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA12 O19](../overtures/ga12_1984__o19.md)** (1984, answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 21-1 re ministers moving to field before examination; a prior attempt to amend the same 21-1 text. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p52)
- **[GA16 O15](../overtures/ga16_1988__o15.md)** (1988, —) — Amend BCO 21-1 to restrict candidates from moving to field before examination; prior friction with the 21-1 language. [page](../markdown/ga16_1988.md#ga16-p60)
- **[GA35 O4](../overtures/ga35_2007__o4.md)** (2007, answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 21-1 to affirm presbytery's authority to deny pastoral calls; prior attempt on 21-1. [page](../markdown/ga35_2007.md#ga35-p156)
- **[GA12 O12](../overtures/ga12_1984__o12.md)** (1984, answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 19-2 and 21-4 to add church history to ordination exams; prior attempt on 21-4 examination text. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p50)
- **[GA14 O43](../overtures/ga14_1986__o43.md)** (1986, referred) — Amend BCO 21-4 re extraordinary reception of ministers from other denominations; prior attempt on the 21-4 extraordinary clause. [page](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p55)
- **[GA15 O43](../overtures/ga15_1987__o43.md)** (1987, referred) — Amend BCO 21-4 to clarify extraordinary provisions for ordained ministers; prior attempt on the 21-4 extraordinary clause. [page](../markdown/ga15_1987.md#ga15-p68)
- **[GA16 O22](../overtures/ga16_1988__o22.md)** (1988, answered by reference) — Amend BCO 21-4 to allow ordination without undergraduate degree by supermajority; prior attempt on the 21-4 educational requirements being regrouped. [page](../markdown/ga16_1988.md#ga16-p73)
- **[GA21 O20](../overtures/ga21_1993__o20.md)** (1993, approved & ratified 1994) — Amend BCO 21-4d to permit ordination sermons heard by commission; a ratified amendment that is part of the accumulated piecemeal history this overture cleans up. [page](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p55)
- **[GA31 O6](../overtures/ga31_2003__o6.md)** (2003, answered by reference) — Amend BCO 21-4 to specify procedure for handling confessional exceptions; prior attempt on the 21-4 procedural text. [page](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p63)
- **[GA34 O17](../overtures/ga34_2006__o17.md)** (2006, answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 21-4 par. 7 re teaching approved confessional exceptions; prior attempt on the 21-4 text. [page](../markdown/ga34_2006.md#ga34-p207)
- **[GA48 O37](../overtures/ga48_2021__o37.md)** (2021, approved & ratified 2022) — Amend BCO 21-4 and 24-1 to clarify moral requirements for church office; a ratified amendment that altered 21-4 wording this overture must now carry forward. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1069)
- **[GA48 O30](../overtures/ga48_2021__o30.md)** (2021, answered by reference) — Amend BCO 21 and 24 to clarify moral requirements for church office; companion to O37 on the same text. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1055)
- **[GA49 O31](../overtures/ga49_2022__o31.md)** (2022, —) — Amend BCO 21-4 and 24-1 adding ordination examination requirements; recent attempt on the 21-4 examination text. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1348)
- **[GA51 O17](../overtures/ga51_2024__o17.md)** (2024, approved → sent to presbyteries) — Amend BCO 13-6, 21-4, and 24-1 to require background checks; recent amendment touching the 21-4 examination text. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1101)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 21-1** — 36 citations (e.g., Korean Southern, 23rd GA/1995) faulting missing record of calls/permission before ordination; shows real-world reliance on the 21-1 text being consolidated. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 21-2** — 16 citations (e.g., Tennessee Valley, 23rd GA/1995) on internship/ordination prerequisites; bears on old 21-2, which this overture folds into 21-1. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 21-3** — 1 citation (Hills and Plains, 48th GA/2021) on ordaining without a call to specific work; bears on the laboring-within-bounds text being renumbered. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 21-4** — 805 citations (earliest e.g. Philadelphia, 18th GA/1990) on missing educational/exam/exception records; the most-cited provision in the chapter, confirming heavy practical reliance on the exact 21-4 text being restructured. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
**Companion overture (cross-link):** O25 carries an explicit drafting NOTE — "If both this overture and Overture 21 pass, the references to BCO 21-4 in BCO 13-6 [must be reconciled]." GA53 Overture 21 (also a BCO 21 amendment routed through CCB) is a substantive companion; the two must be harmonized if both pass, and clerks/the committee should read O25 against O21.

**Renumbering caveat:** BCO chapter 21 has no entry in the renumbering index, so all the older citations above (which use 21-1 … 21-4 as they stand today) are directly comparable. But O25 itself *is* a renumbering event — it absorbs old 21-2 into 21-1, regroups the requirements, and shifts every later section — so after ratification the actions cited here will point to provisions that have moved. That downstream-citation churn is exactly the friction the overture's "36 amendments, 7 ratified" grounds invoke.

**Pruned as incidental:** *Judicial Case 31-3* (GA21/1993) — BCO 21-1 appears only in a dissenting commissioner's protest about a separate case (92-2), not in the court's holding; the case turns on complaint procedure and non-membership jurisdiction (BCO 31-2, 32-3, 38-3). *Gonzales v. Great Lakes Presbytery* (2013-6, GA43) — BCO 21-1 is cited only in passing as an illustration of "the Church" meaning the broader church; the case is about BCO 34-10 divestiture without censure and does not construe the call/permission requirements of 21-1.

**Pruning:** The exact-provision spine returned 47 cases, 25 inquiries, 24 CCB items, and 57 prior overtures — almost all reaching deep into BCO 21-5 through 21-21 (ordination vows, assistant pastors, evangelists, installation). Because O25 is a clarity/restructure overture aimed squarely at **21-1 through 21-4**, the large volume of 21-5+ vow-substance disputes (the Good Faith Subscription overture cluster at GA30–31; the GA48 same-sex-attraction CCB inquiries; the many 21-5 ordination-vow appeals such as Williams, Psiaki, Flatgard, Martinez; assistant-pastor and evangelist installation matters) is **incidental** to this renumbering and was pruned. Kept here: actions that construe the *meaning or flow of 21-1 through 21-4 specifically*, prior *attempts to amend that same text* (the piecemeal history the overture cites), and RPR reliance on 21-1 through 21-4. The full high-recall hit-list is reproducible via `python3 /workspace/ga53/ga53_join.py O25 --json`.

---

## O26 — Amend BCO 26-2 to Only Count Presbyteries Who Submit Votes
**Targets:** BCO 26-2 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-26_Westminster_26-2.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-26_Westminster_26-2.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 26-2.2 so the two-thirds (2/3) advice-and-consent threshold for ratifying constitutional amendments is computed only against presbyteries that actually submit a vote ("two-thirds (2/3) of the *voting* Presbyteries"), rather than counting a non-submitting presbytery's silence as a "no." It treats a non-reporting presbytery as absent (not abstaining) and points to BCO 26-6 deferral as the remedy when a presbytery later wishes to be heard.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (no prior PCA cases, overtures, or inquiries cited; the grounds rest on RONR § 44:3 and BCO 26-6).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. *(The four spine hits — Mays v. New River GA8, the GA27 p.61 SJC decision, the BCO 40-5 Metro New York matter GA51, and Myers v. Illiana GA51 — all cite "26-2" only as an incidental string in a large provision list and concern discipline/contumacy/review, not how presbytery amendment votes are counted. Pruned as non-bearing. See the Note for the GA27 amendment-deferral page, which does bear.)*

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **III.C** (GA47/2019, advice given; Adopted by the CCB) — "Questions on the Effect of Presbytery Division upon Advice and Consent": the CCB advised that a newly erected presbytery may give advice and consent on amendments already voted by its predecessor, but individual presbyters may not vote twice after transfer (provisions: BCO 8-2.a.1, **BCO 26**). Directly construes how the advice-and-consent count under BCO 26 is composed — the same question O26 raises about which presbyteries count toward the 2/3. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci24.md)

*(The eight spine CCB hits — 30-29 III, GA45 App. O II.A, GA46 App. O II.E/II.H, GA48 II.I/II.P, GA50 II.K, GA51 II.C — each cite BCO 26-2 only as the generic "this change must go through the 26-2 amendment process" boilerplate while construing other chapters (BCO 53, 59, 7, 17, deaconesses). They bear on *whether* the amendment process applies, not on *how* presbytery votes are tallied; pruned as non-bearing on O26's question.)*

### Prior overtures
- **[GA38 O5](../overtures/ga38_2010__o5.md)** (2010, Answered in the negative) — Covenant Presbytery, "Amend BCO 26-2 to Clarify How Non-binding Sections of the BCO May Be Amended" — the only prior overture to amend the very subsection (BCO 26-2) governing the amendment process; a direct prior attempt to refine 26-2's mechanics, answered in the negative. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p407)
- **[GA30 O27](../overtures/ga30_2002__o27.md)** (2002, Answered in the negative) — Eastern Canada Presbytery, "Add to BCO 26-1 Procedure for Conflicts Between Scripture & Constitution" — adjacent attempt to amend the BCO 26 amendment/conflict procedure; bears as a same-chapter procedural precedent (also generated CCB advice 30-29 III). [page](../markdown/ga30_2002.md#ga30-p102)

*(The remaining spine "body+title" matches — GA29 O7 creation days, GA32 O9 subscription, GA35 O9 RAO committee terms, GA39 O8 / GA46 O24 BCO 59 marriage status, GA40 O44 IRC anniversary, GA41 O23 SJC 2012-09 — are false-positive title/body collisions, not attempts to change 26-2's vote-counting rule; pruned.)*

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
Spine was provision-exact on "BCO 26-2" and high-recall: every one of its judicial-case and CCB hits proved incidental (26-2 appearing in a long citation list, or as boilerplate that an amendment must follow the 26-2 process), so they were pruned — only GA38 O5 (prior 26-2 amendment) and the adjacent GA30 O27 / CCB 30-29 III survive from the spine. The genuinely on-point action, GA47 CI III.C, was MISSED by the exact-provision spine because it is tagged "BCO 26" (not "BCO 26-2"); it was recovered by topical search and is the closest construction of the advice-and-consent count. Real-world friction confirming the need O26 addresses appears at [GA27 p.59](../markdown/ga27_1999.md#ga27-p59) (1999): an amendment to BCO 24-1 fell short of the required two-thirds (the floor vote was FOR 33, AGAINST 13) and so was "Deferred to the 28th General Assembly [BCO 26-2; 26-6]," with non-reporting presbyteries "urged to report their judgment to the next General Assembly" — exactly the scenario where treating silence as "no" can defeat ratification, which O26 seeks to correct. No renumbering of BCO 26-2 is recorded (bco_renumberings.jsonl has no Chapter 26 entry). No GA48–52 overture revisited 26-2, so no recent (⭐) overture applies.

---

## O27 — Amend BCO 34-1 Regarding GA Assuming Original Jurisdiction
**Targets:** BCO 34-1 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-27_Westminster_34-1.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-27_Westminster_34-1.pdf)

**What it does:** Rewrites BCO 34-1 so the General Assembly may assume original jurisdiction over a teaching elder only when his presbytery receives a report of false teaching or heinous sin and fails to indict, raising the trigger from two presbyteries (current text) to three presbyteries concerning the same matter; and adds an alternative letting GA instead require the original presbytery to indict and submit the record for review.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (cites only the general fact that BCO 34-1 has been "proposed for amendment eleven (11) times … yet none … ratified," and Preliminary Principle #3; no specific case, overture, or inquiry by number).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[1999-1 — Western Carolina v. Tennessee Valley (John Wood OJ request)](../cases/ga28_2000__1999-01.md)** (GA28/2000, dismissed) — The paradigm BCO 34-1 original-jurisdiction request: presbyteries asked SJC/GA to assume OJ over a TE; SJC declined. Directly construes the OJ mechanism this overture rewrites. [minutes](../markdown/ga28_2000.md#ga28-p240)
- **The John Wood Matter** (GA29/2001, other) — Continuation of the same OJ controversy that first exposed the practical weakness of the two-presbytery trigger the overture targets. [minutes](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p72)
- **2020-2 — In the Matter of BCO 34-1 Requests to Assume Original Jurisdiction** (GA49/2022, other) — SJC matter squarely about whether/how OJ requests under 34-1 are handled; central to the threshold and procedure this overture amends. [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p842)
- **[2020-12 — Speck v. Missouri Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2020-12.md)** (GA49/2022, sustained) — Real-world friction (the Greg Johnson controversy) that generated multiple OJ overtures against Missouri Presbytery; illustrates the stakes of the failure-to-indict scenario the overture codifies. [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p747)
- **[2022-11 — BCO 34-1 Petitions re: Central Indiana Presbytery](../cases/ga50_2023__2022-11.md)** (GA50/2023, administrative) — Petitions invoking 34-1 OJ against Central Indiana; construes the petition/threshold procedure being revised. [minutes](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p926)
- **[2022-12 — BCO 34-1 Petitions re: Missouri Presbytery](../cases/ga50_2023__2022-12.md)** (GA50/2023, dismissed) — Companion 34-1 OJ petitions re: Missouri; same OJ mechanism at issue. [minutes](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p927)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **28-19 III.2 — Whether a BCO 34-1 Case May Be Declared Without Being Heard** (GA28/2000, advice given) — CCB advised that a 34-1 case may be declared without being heard; construes the OJ procedure. [page](../inquiries/ga28_2000__ci01.md)
- **37-29 II.C — Higher court assumption of original jurisdiction before lower court concludes** (GA37/2009, in conflict) — CCB found a proposed amendment letting a higher court intervene before the lower court finishes conflicts with BCO 11-3; directly relevant to this overture's "require the original Presbytery to indict" alternative. [page](../inquiries/ga37_2009__ci01.md)
- **49 II.D — Percentage threshold for original jurisdiction requests (BCO 33-1/34-1)** (GA49/2022, in conflict) — CCB found Houston Metro's numerical-percentage threshold for OJ requests in conflict; bears on this overture's move from 2 to 3 presbyteries. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci04.md)
- **49 II.E — Numerical threshold for original jurisdiction requests (BCO 34-1)** (GA49/2022, in conflict) — Same threshold question for a Calvary Presbytery overture; cautionary precedent on threshold mechanics. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci05.md)
- **50 II.N — Specifying causes and processes for original jurisdiction requests** (GA50/2023, not in conflict) — CCB found amending 33-1/34-1 to specify causes and processes for OJ requests is NOT in conflict; the closest favorable precedent for this overture's approach. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci14.md)
- **52 II.D — Advisors and original jurisdiction in process against a TE** (GA52/2025, not in conflict) — CCB found Missouri's 34-1 amendment on advisors/OJ in TE process not in conflict; immediately prior-year 34-1 amendment effort. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci04.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA52 O7](../overtures/ga52_2025__o7.md)** (2025, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 34-1 Regarding Advisors and Original Jurisdiction in Process Against a TE. ⭐ Most recent 34-1 OJ amendment attempt; failed at GA. [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1173)
- **[GA50 O21](../overtures/ga50_2023__o21.md)** (2023, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 33-1 and 34-1 to Specify Causes and Processes for Original Jurisdiction Requests. ⭐ Same reform direction (specify causes/process); CCB approved but GA rejected. [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1016)

- **[GA49 O9](../overtures/ga49_2022__o9.md)** (2022) — Amend BCO 34-1 to Establish Percentage Threshold for Original Jurisdiction Requests. ⭐ Companion threshold attempt; found in conflict. [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1297)
- **[GA48 O25](../overtures/ga48_2021__o25.md)** (2021, Answered by reference) — Assume Original Jurisdiction over TE Greg Johnson Under BCO 34-1. ⭐ OJ request that drove the recent 34-1 reform wave. [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1006)
- **[GA41 O16](../overtures/ga41_2013__o16.md)** (2013, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 34-1 & 33-1 to Clarify Prerequisites for Original Jurisdiction. Prior attempt to clarify OJ prerequisites. [page](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p91)
- **[GA40 O18](../overtures/ga40_2012__o18.md)** (2012, Referred) — Amend BCO 34-1 & 33-1 on Threshold for Assumption of Original Jurisdiction. Prior threshold attempt. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p87)
- **[GA37 O3](../overtures/ga37_2009__o3.md)** (2009, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 34-1 and 33-1 Regarding Assumption of Original Jurisdiction (the overture behind CCB advice 37-29 II.C). [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p263)
- **[GA30 O5](../overtures/ga30_2002__o5.md)** (2002, Approved but not ratified) — Require Ten Percent of Presbyteries to Assume Original Jurisdiction in BCO 34-1. Closest historical analogue: a threshold-raising amendment that passed GA but was not ratified by presbyteries (one of the "eleven" the overture cites). [page](../markdown/ga30_2002.md#ga30-p100)
- **[GA29 O11](../overtures/ga29_2001__o11.md)** (2001, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 34-1 on Assuming Original Jurisdiction of Ministers. Early OJ-of-ministers reform tied to the John Wood matter. [page](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p140)
- **[GA20 O32](../overtures/ga20_1992__o32.md)** (1992, Approved but not ratified) — Amend BCO 34-1 to Allow Neighboring Presbytery to Adjudicate Cases. Early 34-1 amendment passed-but-not-ratified, part of the unratified "eleven." [page](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p58)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 34-1** — 1 citation; [Siouxlands](../rpr/siouxlands.md) Presbytery, 33rd GA (2005): "No record of 2/3 vote to divest TE without censure" — bears on the divestiture/OJ machinery of 34-1 in practice. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Pruning: the provision-exact join returned 35 cases citing "34-1," but most (Hathaway 1982-4/5, Hopper, St. Paul, Chung 2001-15, Ball 2001-28, Delhi 2002-16, Merriam, Thornton 2003-5/2004-8, the 2006-2 memorial, 2007-8, 2007-14, Sartorious, Hedman, Bethel, Hahn, North Port, Doty, Fordice, Frazier, Lewis, Durand, Herron, Wilson, Biese) are ordinary minister discipline complaints/appeals that cite 34-1 only because it is the minister-process chapter heading — they do NOT construe the original-jurisdiction threshold this overture rewrites, so they are pruned as incidental. Kept the six cases that actually concern OJ requests/petitions or supply the real-world friction (John Wood, the GA49 "Matter of BCO 34-1 Requests," the GA50 34-1 Petitions cases, and Speck/Greg Johnson).

Pruned as incidental: 2024-5 Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery — call-dissolution complaint; cites BCO 34-1 among ~37 provisions but does not concern an original-jurisdiction request. Companion provision BCO 33-1 (OJ over members) recurs across these overtures; several prior overtures amended 33-1 and 34-1 together. No renumbering: BCO chapter 34 has been stable, so older actions cite "34-1" directly. The overture's own grounds stress that all eleven prior 34-1 amendments failed ratification — the GA30 O5 and GA20 O32 "approved but not ratified" overtures above are concrete instances of that pattern.

## O28 — Add BCO 41-7 to Provide a Right to Complain when a Presbytery Acts on a Reference
**Targets:** BCO 41-7 (new) · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-28_Westminster_41-7.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-28_Westminster_41-7.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a new BCO 41-7 providing that when a Session makes a reference *with final disposition* to Presbytery and the Presbytery acts on it, the members of the congregation retain the right to complain against any action of the Presbytery related to the reference, as if the Session itself had taken the action. The grounds argue that referring (rather than deciding) a matter currently strips members of the BCO 43 right to complain against the lower court's action.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (the grounds argue from general principles of BCO 43 complaint rights and due process; no specific prior case, overture, or inquiry is cited).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (See Note — the exact-provision join returned no cases, and the reference-related cases in the corpus address dismissal/disposition of particular references, not the complaint-recourse question O28 raises.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI #10, GA14/1986** (advice given) — Held that the Assembly's refusal to accept a judicial *reference* applies to the entire judicial process in PCA courts, ensuring no party is left without recourse. Directly bears: O28 likewise targets the recourse available to members when a reference (rather than a direct decision) governs a matter. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci13.md)
- **CI 2 (12-53 III), GA12/1984** (advice given) — When a judicial case is *transferred/referred*, the receiving court becomes the court of original jurisdiction and exercises the lower court's duties. Bears: O28's mechanism treats the Presbytery's action on a reference "as if the Session itself had taken the action," the same court-of-original-jurisdiction logic. [page](../inquiries/ga12_1984__ci03.md)
- **CI 20-75, GA20/1992** (advice given) — A presbyter may complain against a court's decision because that reception/decision is itself a court action under BCO 43-1. Bears: confirms the BCO 43-1 principle O28 seeks to preserve — that members may complain against any *action* of a court. [page](../inquiries/ga20_1992__ci04.md)
- **CI 29-28 III.6 (Reference 6), GA29/2001** (advice given) — A complainant may not go to a higher court until the lower court has acted on the complaint (BCO 43-2, 43-3). Bears: clarifies the complaint pathway O28 would preserve where a reference otherwise removes a layer of lower-court action. [page](../inquiries/ga29_2001__ci06.md)
- **CI Non-Judicial Reference 1, GA48/2021** (answered/adopted) — CCB opinions on procedure, anonymity, and standing for BCO 40-5 reports of sessional delinquency, addressing standing to complain (BCO 43-1) about Session-level acts. Bears on the standing-to-complain dimension of O28. [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci29.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA29 O16](../overtures/ga29_2001__o16.md)** (2002, Approved & ratified) — Amend BCO 43-1 to Allow Complaint After Appeal Dismissed or Abandoned. Closest prior analogue: like O28, it closed a *gap* in the right to complain created by a particular procedural posture. [page](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p208)
- **[GA41 O15](../overtures/ga41_2013__o15.md)** (2014, Approved & ratified) — Amend BCO 43-10 to Require Higher Court to Accept Reference in Doctrinal Cases. Bears: directly addresses how a higher court handles a *reference*, the same procedural mechanism O28 concerns. [page](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p847)
- **[GA44 O40](../overtures/ga44_2016__o40.md)** (2016, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 43-1 to Clarify Timing of Higher Court Complaint Review. Bears: a prior attempt to refine the right-to-complain framework O28 extends. [page](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p641)
- **[GA45 O15](../overtures/ga45_2017__o15.md)** (2017, Referred) — Amend BCO 43-1 Restricting Complaints During Judicial Process. Bears: companion debate over the scope of the BCO 43-1 right to complain against court actions. [page](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p667)
- **[GA49 O2](../overtures/ga49_2022__o2.md)** (2022) — Amend BCO 22-3 to Allow Assistant Pastors to File Complaints Against Sessions. Bears: a recent move to expand who/when may complain against a Session's action, the same accountability concern. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1286)
- **[GA51 O21](../overtures/ga51_2024__o21.md)** (2024, Approved & ratified 2025) — Amend BCO 43-1 to Clarify Prohibition on Complaints During Judicial Process. Most recent ratified change to the BCO 43-1 right-to-complain framework O28 builds upon. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1165)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
The deterministic provision-exact join (`ga53_join.py O28`) returned empty across cases, inquiries, CCB advice, prior overtures, and RPR, because **BCO 41-7 is a brand-new section** — no past action cites a provision that does not yet exist. Everything above is therefore a **topical supplement** built on the two concepts O28 fuses: (1) **BCO 41 references** (esp. the recourse available after a higher court acts on a reference — CI #10/GA14, CI 2/GA12, GA41 O15) and (2) the **right to complain against a court action under BCO 43-1** (CI 20-75/GA20, CI 29-28 III.6/GA29; the GA29/GA44/GA45/GA51 O-series on BCO 43-1). **No renumbering** affects chapters 41 or 43, so no old-number search was needed. **Pruned as incidental:** the judicial reference cases in the corpus (e.g., 1992-08 Reference from Central Carolina Presbytery; 1995-10 Stuart Merriam vs. Tennessee Valley Presbytery, a referred matter) — they dispose of particular references but do not construe the members'-right-to-complain question O28 raises, so they are not bearing. Companion GA53 cross-link to watch: any other GA53 overtures touching BCO 41 (references) or BCO 43 (complaints).

---

## O29 — Amend BCO 42 to Clarify Between Verbal and Written Notice of Appeal
**Targets:** BCO 42-4, BCO 42-6 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-29_Westminster_42.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-29_Westminster_42.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 42-4 to label its notice provision as "Verbal notice of appeal," and rewrites BCO 42-6 to distinguish the suspending effect of each kind of notice — verbal notice suspending the lower court's judgment for thirty (30) days, written notice suspending it until the case is finally decided in the higher court.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (grounds reference only BCO 42, 42-4, and 42-6 themselves; no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[13-61 — Mayfield v. Siouxlands Presbytery](../markdown/ga13_1985.md#ga13-p103)** (GA13/1985, dismissed) — appeal found not in order under BCO 42-4 because notice was filed roughly a year and a half after adjudication; construes the timing/validity of a notice of appeal, the mechanism O29 relabels. [minutes](../markdown/ga13_1985.md#ga13-p103)
- **[1986-4 — Steele v. Presbytery of Great Lakes](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p331)** (GA14/1986, administrative) — turns squarely on BCO 42-6's suspension-of-judgment effect, holding a divestiture is suspended during appeal unless the lower court separately places the censure into effect; bears directly on the suspending-effect rule O29 rewrites. [minutes](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p331)
- **[2004-9 — Robar v. Central Carolina Presbytery](../cases/ga33_2005__2004-09.md)** (GA33/2005, dismissed) — appeal dismissed because notice was filed only with the presbytery's stated clerk and not as required; precisely the kind of notice-of-appeal defect O29's 42-4/42-6 clarification addresses. [minutes](../markdown/ga33_2005.md#ga33-p485)
- **[2013-11 — Session of FPC North Port v. Presbytery of Southwest Florida](../cases/ga42_2014__2013-11.md)** (GA42/2014, sustained) — sustained an appeal from a presbytery judgment suspending a Session, engaging when and how a lower court's judgment is held in abeyance pending appeal under BCO 42-6. [minutes](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p575)
- **[2016-2 — Robertstad v. North Texas Presbytery](../cases/ga45_2017__2016-02.md)** (GA45/2017, administrative) — found administratively out of order because the complaint was filed via e-mail rather than by hard copy, contrary to BCO 43-3 and OMSJC 18.10.b; the decision discusses BCO 42-4 and 43-3 together as parallel filing-notice provisions whose shared 2012 amendment history clarified that neither authorises e-mail filing. [minutes](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p511)
- **[2018-6 — Edwards v. North Texas Presbytery](../cases/ga47_2019__2018-06.md)** (GA47/2019, administrative) — out of order because the case was never properly filed; construes the filing/notice requirement of BCO 42-4. [minutes](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p579)
- **[2021-13 — Dudt v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2021-13.md)** (GA49/2022, sustained) — one of the few recent cases citing both BCO 42-4 and 42-6 in a contested appeal of a Session suspension; engages the appeal-notice and suspension framework O29 amends. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p909)
- **[2024-10 — Gozé v. Hills and Plains Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-10.md)** (GA52/2025, dismissed) — dismissed as judicially out of order because the appeal was not filed within 30 days of notification; live, recent friction over the 42-4 notice-timing rule O29 touches. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1013)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI #12 (GA14, ci15)** (GA14/1986) — CCB advised that a judgment of divestiture is suspended during appeal to the GA unless the lower court separately places the censure into immediate effect; directly construes the BCO 42-6 suspending effect O29 redrafts. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci15.md)
- **20-67 2 (GA20, ci03)** (GA20/1992) — advised that the effect of an unconstitutional act is suspended upon appeal while judicial proceedings are pending (BCO 42-6); bears on the suspension-of-judgment rule. [page](../inquiries/ga20_1992__ci03.md)
- **CCB App. O II.N (GA48, ci14)** (GA48/2021) — CCB found O21 (PNW), amending BCO 42-6 to specify the vote required to maintain a censure during appeal, not in conflict and adopted; same provision, same suspension-during-appeal question. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci14.md)
- **CCB App. O II.C (GA49, ci03)** (GA49/2022) — CCB found O7 (Nashville), amending BCO 42-6 regarding suspension of judgment pending appeal, not in conflict and adopted; the closest prior CCB review to O29's own subject. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci03.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA14 O37](../overtures/ga14_1986__o37.md)** (1987, Approved & ratified) — amended BCO 42-4 (and 43-2) to extend the appeal/complaint filing period; a prior amendment to the same notice-of-appeal subsection. [page](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p55)
- **[GA40 O14](../overtures/ga40_2012__o14.md)** (2013, Approved & ratified) — amended BCO 42-4 to change the start of the thirty-day filing period for appeal; prior change to the 42-4 timing mechanism O29 relabels. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p87)
- **[GA41 O5](../overtures/ga41_2013__o5.md)** (2013, Answered in the negative) — proposed adding BCO 42-13 to define terms in Chapter 42; a prior attempt at the same kind of goal O29 pursues — clarifying terminology in Chapter 42 — that the Assembly rejected. [page](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p90)
- **[GA47 O9](../overtures/ga47_2019__o9.md)** (2019, Platte Valley) — amended BCO 42-4, 43-2, 43-3 regarding method and deadlines of filing cases; prior 42-4 amendment on the form/timing of filing. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p608)
- **[GA47 O34](../overtures/ga47_2019__o34.md)** (2021, Approved & ratified) — amended BCO 42-4, 43-2, 43-3, and OMSJC to allow electronic filings; prior change to how a notice of appeal is given. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p672)
- **[GA48 O21](../overtures/ga48_2021__o21.md)** (2021, PNW) — proposed amending BCO 42-6 to require a two-thirds majority for maintaining censure during appeal; prior overture on the 42-6 suspension-during-appeal regime. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p998)
- **[GA49 O7](../overtures/ga49_2022__o7.md)** (2022, Nashville) — proposed amending BCO 42-6 regarding suspending judgment during appeal; the most on-point prior overture, addressing the very suspending-effect clause O29 rewrites. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1292)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 42-4** — 1 citation: [Savannah River](../rpr/savannah-river.md), 48th (2021) — no record of the court's action regarding a timely-filed appeal (satisfactory/closed); real-world friction over recording a notice of appeal. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 42-6** — 1 citation: [Illiana](../rpr/illiana.md), 49th (2022) — motion made pursuant to BCO 42-6 with no record of a continuing judicial process in the record aside from it (satisfactory/closed); bears on the suspension-of-judgment mechanism. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
No renumbering applies to BCO 42, so older actions cite the same 42-4 / 42-6 section numbers. There is no GA53 companion overture on Chapter 42. **Pruning:** the join returned provisions=[] (a chapter-level overture), so the case spine above was rebuilt deterministically on the two exact provisions O29 amends (42-4, 42-6) using the same case_pages_map link logic. That 42-6 spine is high-recall because nearly every appeal of a censure boilerplate-cites 42-6 as the suspending provision; roughly twenty cases that cite it only incidentally were pruned (Clark 1993-10, Smith 1998-8, Plowman 2002-5, Thornton 2004-8, Chastain 2005-1, Kim 2005-8, Lee 2003-3, Ehrlich 2006-6, Hardie 2015-8, Frazier 2016-11, Bachmann 2016-15, Mapes 2018-1, Evans 2019-10, Crouse 2019-3, Williams 2021-10, Herron 2021-6, Myers 2023-9, Sears 2023-18, Bigelow 2024-5, plus several pre-SJC GA9/GA12 entries). The eight retained cases each construe either the form/timing of the notice of appeal (42-4) or the suspending effect of an appeal (42-6) — the two questions O29 actually changes. Fixed description: 2016-2 Robertstad v. North Texas Presbytery — prior gloss said "notice of appeal under BCO 42-4" but the case is a complaint dismissed under BCO 43-3 (e-mail filing prohibition); BCO 42-4 appears only as a parallel provision discussed in explaining the 2012 amendment history, not as the operative rule. Judgment call: GA49 O7 and the GA49 CCB advice on it are the closest precedents, and the prior negative on GA41 O5 (defining terms in Chapter 42) is a useful caution that the Assembly has previously declined a Chapter 42 terminology clarification.

---

## O30 — Amend BCO 46-6 to Require Recording of Reception of One Dismissed to Another Presbytery
**Targets:** BCO 46-6 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-30_Westminster_46-6.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-30_Westminster_46-6.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a sentence to BCO 46-6 requiring a Presbytery to record in its minutes the date of reception of a minister, licentiate, or candidate who was dismissed to another Presbytery. The grounds reason that, because the man remains under the dismissing Presbytery's jurisdiction until actually received by the other, the court holding original jurisdiction must be clearly known and recorded.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None. The grounds rest only on the text of BCO 46-6 itself (jurisdiction continues until received by the other); no SJC case, prior overture, or CCB ruling is cited by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **Judicial Case 2005-2** (GA36/2008, dismissed) — cites BCO 46-6 in a dismissal/transfer-jurisdiction matter; bears on the jurisdiction-continuity principle of 46-6 but not specifically on the recording requirement O30 adds. (No case page in corpus; minutes only.) [minutes](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p283)
- **[2022-23 — Woodham v. South Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga51_2024__2022-23.md)** (GA51/2024, denied) — recent SJC case citing 46-6 on transfer/jurisdiction of a TE demitting/leaving the PCA; bears on jurisdiction continuity, not on the precise recording defect. [minutes](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p749)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **17-82 III** (GA17/1989, advice given) — a letter from a presbytery committee chairman is insufficient evidence of dismissal; BCO 46-6 requires a certificate bearing the stated clerk's signature (per BCO 10-4). Directly construes 46-6's dismissal/reception certificate mechanics that O30 amends — the most on-point non-RPR item. [page](../inquiries/ga17_1989__ci01.md)
- **36-30 II.C** (GA36/2008, in conflict) — CCB found a Southeast Alabama overture adding membership-transfer procedures (touching 38-3a/46-5/46-6/57-6) in conflict over profession-of-faith language; shows a prior attempt to amend the 46-x transfer cluster and the CCB's cautions, on a different issue than recording. [page](../inquiries/ga36_2008__ci02.md)
- **App. O II.T** (GA40/2012, in conflict) — CCB again found proposed Southeast Alabama membership overtures (touching 46-6 among others) in conflict over the required profession for membership; parallel CCB review of the same provision, tangential to recording. [page](../inquiries/ga40_2012__ci03.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA36 O3](../overtures/ga36_2008__o3.md)** (2008, Answered by reference) — Amend BCO 38-3a, 46-5, 46-6, and 57-5 to Specify Transfers of Church Membership; a prior overture squarely amending 46-6 (broader transfer-procedure scope, same provision). [page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p185)
- **[GA40 O33](../overtures/ga40_2012__o33.md)** (2012, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 38-3a, BCO 46, and Remove BCO 57-6 Regarding Church Membership Administration; another prior attempt to amend chapter 46, declined. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p89)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 46-6** — 50 citations, overwhelmingly the exact defect O30 fixes: "No record reflecting when a man who was transferred to another presbytery was received by that presbytery" and "No record regarding the reception of a certificate of dismission from transferring presbytery." Examples: [Korean Southwest Orange County](../rpr/korean-southwest-orange-county.md) (50th/2023, raised), [Tennessee Valley](../rpr/tennessee-valley.md) (50th/2023, raised), [Missouri](../rpr/missouri.md) (51st/2024, outstanding), Chicago Metro / James River / Siouxlands / Chesapeake / [Central Georgia](../rpr/central-georgia.md) / [Northern California](../rpr/northern-california.md) / [Rio Grande](../rpr/rio-grande.md) (52nd/2025, many raised/open). Strong, current, real-world friction directly motivating O30. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
The RPR record is the dominant bearing evidence: 50 BCO 46-6 exceptions across the 49th–52nd Assemblies (2022–2025), many still unsatisfactory/open, document the precise problem — Presbyteries failing to record reception of a dismissed man — that O30 is written to cure, making this one of the most RPR-grounded overtures in this batch. The two remaining judicial cases (2005-2 and Woodham 2022-23) and the two CCB-advice items are spine hits that cite 46-6 but turn on jurisdiction/discipline or profession-of-faith questions rather than the recording requirement; they are retained as construing the same provision but flagged tangential.

Pruned as incidental: 2010-26 Lee v. Korean Eastern Presbytery — BCO 46-6 does not appear in the case decision text; the case is about charges/discipline against two TEs and 46-6 appears only in the index metadata, not in the holding. Pruned as incidental: 2010-28 Gonzales v. Great Lakes Presbytery — BCO 46-6 appears only as a parenthetical reference ("may choose not to dismiss him to another presbytery or church (BCO 13-9a; 46-6)") in the Judicial Commission's recommendation; the case is about pastoral oversight and the BCO 31-2 investigation trigger, and 46-6 is not construed. Inquiry 17-82 III is the closest non-RPR analogue (certificate/recording mechanics). Prior overtures GA36 O3 and GA40 O33 are genuine prior attempts to amend chapter 46 within the broader membership-transfer cluster. No GA48–52 prior overture targets this provision, so no star applies. No renumbering caveat: BCO chapter 46 is not in bco_renumberings.jsonl. Cross-link: the parallel provision BCO 46-8 (reception/jurisdiction) carries its own large RPR record; v1's references to cases 1990-8 and overtures GA6 O4 / GA24 O21 were not in the deterministic spine and have been pruned.

---

## O31 — Amend BCO 58-5 to Specify that Ruling Elders Shall Distribute the Elements
**Targets:** BCO 58-5 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-31_Westminster_58-5.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-31_Westminster_58-5.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 58-5 (and adds an explanatory footnote) so that, apart from extraordinary circumstances, ruling elders shall assist the minister in distributing the elements — "distributing" defined as the act of handing elements to communicants, not the passive passing of trays down pews — thereby barring non-ordained members from the active serving role.

**Cites in its own grounds:** No PCA cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by number. Grounds rest on WCF 29.3; WLC 169, 173, 176; WCF 30.1–4; BCO 30-3; BCO 12-5.a; BCO 57; Matthew 16:19; 1 Cor 11:27–32; the Scots Confession of 1560 ch. 22; and a Charles Hodge quotation.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.H** (GA52/2025) — CCB found the GA52 amendment to BCO 58-5 limiting Lord's Supper distribution to officers "not in conflict" with the Constitution, adopted 8-0-0. Directly on point: the constitutional vetting of the immediately preceding attempt to restrict who distributes the elements under this exact clause; O31 is the narrower successor (ruling elders assist, vs. officers-only). [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci08.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA52 O12](../overtures/ga52_2025__o12.md)** (2025, Approved but not ratified) — Providence, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Restrict Distribution of Lord's Supper to Officers." The direct predecessor on the same question (who may distribute the elements); passed the Assembly but failed presbytery ratification. O31 is the re-attempt on a narrower footing. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1189)
- **[GA40 O30](../overtures/ga40_2012__o30.md)** (2012, Approved but not ratified) — Savannah River, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Prohibit Intinction." A prior 58-5 amendment over the *manner* of administering the Supper; approved by the Assembly but not ratified — precedent on the difficulty of amending 58-5 administration practice. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p88)
- **[GA40 O29](../overtures/ga40_2012__o29.md)** (2012, Answered by reference) — Savannah River, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Prohibit the Practice of Intinction." Companion to O30 on the same intinction/administration question; answered by reference. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p88)
- **[GA31 O21](../overtures/ga31_2003__o21.md)** (2003, Approved & ratified 2004) — Ascension, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Delete 'Broken' in Communion Liturgy." A successful, ratified 58-5 amendment — shows the clause is amendable, though on liturgical wording rather than distribution. [page](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p65)
- **[GA29 O2](../overtures/ga29_2001__o2.md)** (2001, Answered in the negative) — New Jersey, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Permit Use of Leavened Bread in the Lord's Supper." Same-provision amendment, different subject (elements used). [page](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p139)
- **[GA18 O14](../overtures/ga18_1990__o14.md)** (1990, Answered in the negative) — Presbytery of the Southwest, "Amend BCO 58-5 by Replacing 'Wine' with 'Fruit of the Vine'." Same-provision amendment, different subject (elements used). [page](../markdown/ga18_1990.md#ga18-p72)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
Companion to **GA53 O60** (Calvary, also BCO 58-5, "Only Men Lawfully Ordained Shall Distribute the Elements") — both amend the same distribution clause; O60 is the stricter ordained-men-only version, O31 the ruling-elders-assist version, and both descend from GA52 O12 (passed but not ratified). CCB has already cleared the officer-distribution concept as constitutionally sound (II.H, GA52), so the live question is policy, not constitutionality. Pruned as incidental from the spine: inquiry **6-111 III** (1978) and prior overture **[GA7 O22](../overtures/ga07_1979__o22.md)** (1979), which cite 58-5 only for the *membership reaffirmation-of-faith vows* — an unrelated portion of the chapter, not the Lord's Supper. The wine / leavened-bread / "broken" overtures are kept as same-provision amendment history (they bear on the Assembly's willingness to revise 58-5) but address different questions than *who distributes*. No BCO ch. 58 renumbering and no RPR exceptions for 58-5.

---

## O32 — Amend RAO 14-3 for the Review of Committee and Agency Standing Rules and Manuals
**Targets:** RAO 14-3 · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-32_Westminster_RAO14-3.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-32_Westminster_RAO14-3.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends RAO 14-3 so permanent Committees and Agencies must submit not only their minutes but also their standing rules or manuals to their Committee of Commissioners for review, on the rationale (BCO 14-1.7) that committees serve and execute rather than direct and establish policy, yet can in effect set policy through manuals that never appear in reviewed minutes.

**Cites in its own grounds:** BCO 14-1.7 only. No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found. (The spine's CCB items — 31-56 VI and 32-36 III — match RAO 14-3 only through its confessional-subscription sub-clause RAO 14-3e.5 and concern whether presbyteries must record ministers'/candidates' exceptions to the Standards; that is a different question than reviewing committee/agency manuals, so they are pruned. See Note.)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA47 O24](../overtures/ga47_2019__o24.md)** (2019, Adopted final) — "Add Constitutional Precedence Statement to Permanent Committee and Agency Policy Manuals." Most directly bearing: same concern that committee/agency manuals can drift from constitutional/GA authority; GA addressed it via a precedence statement rather than mandatory review. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p651)
- **[GA48 O14](../overtures/ga48_2021__o14.md)** (2021, Adopted final) — "Direct MTW to Revise Policy Manual to Restrict Leadership to Ordained Elders." ⭐ Recent real-world friction over an unreviewed committee policy manual setting practice, the exact gap O32 targets. [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p978)
- **[GA21 O8](../overtures/ga21_1993__o8.md)** (1993, Other) — "Amend BCO and RAO to Require SJC Oversight by Committee of Commissioners." Same lever — extending Committee-of-Commissioners review authority over a permanent committee. [page](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p54)
- **[GA21 O29](../overtures/ga21_1993__o29.md)** (1993, Adopted final) — "Direct Review of Presbytery Records Committee to Remove Unwarranted Clerk Requirements" (also Westminster). Touches the review-of-records process O32 invokes as its model (RPR reviews presbytery standing rules, not just minutes). [page](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p56)
- **[GA12 O7](../overtures/ga12_1984__o7.md)** (1984, Answered in the negative) — "Instruct MTW and MNA Committees to Align Practices with Policy Manuals" (also Westminster). Early attempt to make committee practice answerable through its manuals; GA declined. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p63)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (The join returned 7 RAO 14-3 RPR rows — e.g. [Illiana](../rpr/illiana.md) 25th (1997) and [Korean Central](../rpr/korean-central.md) 34th (2006) — but all concern presbytery minute-keeping defects under RAO 14-3 e.4/e.5/e.6, not committee/agency standing-rules review; pruned as off-topic. The overture's own grounds nonetheless analogize to RPR's practice of reviewing presbytery standing rules.)

### Note
The deterministic spine matched RAO 14-3 only via its confessional-subscription sub-clauses (RAO 14-3e.5). All of the spine's inquiries (31-56 IV/VI, 32-36 III) and prior overtures (GA31 O5, GA31 O18) concern whether presbyteries must record ministers'/candidates' exceptions to the Standards — a different question than O32's review of committee/agency manuals — so they are pruned as provision-exact-but-incidental, and all 7 RAO 14-3 RPR rows are pruned likewise. The bearing actions above come from the topical supplement (committee/agency manual review and Committee-of-Commissioners review authority). No renumbering applies (RAO 14-3 is current). Closest companion is GA47 O24, which chose a "precedence statement" solution to the same manual-drift problem O32 attacks via mandatory review.

## O33 — Amend RAO 16-7.h Regarding Minority Reports from RPR
**Targets:** RAO 16-7.h · **Source:** Westminster · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-33_Westminster_RAO16-7.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-33_Westminster_RAO16-7.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends RAO 16-7.h so that only members of the Committee on Review of Presbytery Records who voted in the minority on the Presbytery report as a whole may indicate an intention to file, or sign, an RPR minority report (currently "any member" may give notice of intent; at least six members must file). Aligns RPR practice with RONR 51:64–70, under which only those who did not concur with the majority may sign a minority report.

**Cites in its own grounds:** Robert's Rules of Order (RONR 12th ed., 51:64–70) — no PCA cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **GA48 II.E (CI05)** (GA48/2021) — "Number of members required to file an Overtures Committee minority report"; CCB found the RAO 15-6.s threshold amendment not in conflict (adopted). Directly parallel: regulating how many / which members may file a minority report — the exact mechanic O33 touches. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci05.md)
- **GA48 II.F (CI06)** (GA48/2021) — "Content requirements for Overtures Committee minority reports"; CCB found the RAO 15-6.s content amendment not in conflict (adopted). Bears on regulating minority-report mechanics by RAO amendment. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci06.md)
- **GA50 II.O (CI15)** (GA50/2023) — "When minority reports are permitted under the RAO" (RAO 8-4.h, 17-1, 19-2); CCB found not in conflict (8-0-0), though the underlying overture failed on the floor. Bears on the recurring question of constraining who/when may bring a minority report. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci15.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA48 O9](../overtures/ga48_2021__o9.md)** (2021, Adopted (final)) — Amend RAO 15-6.s.2-3 Regarding Number of Members Required to File a Minority Report (Ascension). Closest analogue: sets a numeric threshold of committee members to file a minority report — the same mechanic as O33's "at least six members" clause. ⭐ [p.982](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p965), [p.1146](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1129)
- **[GA48 O10](../overtures/ga48_2021__o10.md)** (2021, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 15-6.s to Regulate Content of Overtures Committee Minority Reports (Ascension). Companion attempt to regulate minority-report mechanics; failed. ⭐ [p.984](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p967), [p.1146](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1129)
- **[GA50 O22](../overtures/ga50_2023__o22.md)** (2023, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 8-4.h, 17-1, and 19-2 to Specify When Minority Reports Are Permitted (First Pres. Montgomery). Same family of effort — constraining minority reports by RAO amendment; CCB cleared it but the GA declined to adopt (caution flag for O33). ⭐ [p.1027](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1019), [p.1085](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1077)
- **[GA37 O2](../overtures/ga37_2009__o2.md)** (2009, Adopted (final)) — Amend RAO 19-4.d, 14-9.h, and 15-8.g Governing Debate on Minority Reports (Potomac). Earlier successful RAO amendment governing minority-report procedure across Assembly committees. [p.59](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p57), [p.309](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p307), [p.589](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p587)
- **[GA52 O34](../overtures/ga52_2025__o34.md)** (2025, Adopted (final)) — Amend RAO 16 to Require Reporting on Session and Diaconate Membership and Duties (Savannah River). Recent RAO 16 (CRPR) amendment showing the chapter is actively revised. ⭐ [p.1272](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1270), [p.1362](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1360)
- **[GA51 O28](../overtures/ga51_2024__o28.md)** (2024, Referred back to presbytery) — Amend RAO 16-6.c.1 to Eliminate Conflict with BCO 40-5 (New Jersey). Recent RPR-chapter procedural amendment (CCB not-in-conflict 8-0-0); GA referred it back for further refinement. ⭐ [p.1187](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1180), [p.1278](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1271)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
This is an RAO (not BCO) provision, so the provision-exact join returned no cases/inquiries/overtures/RPR rows; all bearing actions above were found by topical search (minority-report mechanics + the RPR/RAO 16 chapter). Pruned: every RPR-BY-PROVISION "RAO 16-7" string match was actually RAO **16-3** records-review content (executive-session minutes, recording of exceptions, etc.) — none concern RAO 16-7.h minority reports — so all such RPR rows are incidental and excluded. Strongest analogues are GA48 O9 (adopted) and O10 (failed), which regulate the same mechanic (member count + minority status), and GA50 O22 (failed) on constraining when minority reports may be filed. Renumbering caveat: the CRPR was historically RAO ch.14 (older actions cite RAO 14-3.e.5 / 14-6.c alongside the modern RAO 16-x), but the renumbering data has no 14→16 chapter-shift entry and none of the ch.14 actions touch the minority-report subsection. The mixed track record — GA adopted a numeric-threshold change (GA48 O9) but declined a "when permitted" restriction (GA50 O22) even after CCB cleared it — is the key signal for O33.
