## O34 — Amend BCO 9-2 Regarding the Expectation of the Establishment of a Diaconate
**Targets:** BCO 9-2 · **Source:** Savannah River · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-34.SavannahRvr_9-2.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2025/12/Overture-34.SavannahRvr_9-2.pdf)

**What it does:** Rewrites the devolve clause of BCO 9-2 so diaconal duties devolve upon the ruling elders only where it is impossible "to secure the appointment of a sufficient number of Deacons due to the absence of spiritually qualified men (BCO 9-3)," deleting the broad "impossible for any reason to secure deacons" language and adding "and not upon unordained persons within the church." Aimed at closing the conscience-based reading that a church may decline to establish a diaconate "for any reason."

**Cites in its own grounds:** None by number — it cites the floor debate at the 52nd General Assembly (2025) as evidence of confusion over whether a diaconate ought ordinarily to be established.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2009-25/2009-26 — Brown / Session of Grace PC v. Northern California Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-25_2009-26.md)** (GA39/2011, sustained) — The concurring opinion construes the very clause O34 amends: it parses what makes it "impossible for any reason to secure deacons" (no man called/qualified/elected) and holds a Session may not decide "as a matter of policy" to have no ordained deacons, treating the 9-2 devolve provision as a narrow exception with an implicit mandate to ordain qualified men. Squarely on point for the proposed "absence of spiritually qualified men" standard. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p550)
- **[2011-14 — Reese and Bech v. Philadelphia Presbytery](../cases/ga42_2014__2011-14.md)** (GA42/2014, sustained) — Real-world friction the overture targets: City/City Line Church invoked the "impossible for any reason to secure deacons" language of 9-2 as a conscience ground for indefinitely declining to form a diaconate ("the main reason is an issue of conscience … the BCO is more restrictive than Scripture"). The controversy O34 cites (GA52 confusion) is the same dispute this case records. [minutes](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p530)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **38-34 II.E** (GA38/2010, in conflict) — Prior attempt to amend the same sentence: GA38 Overture 10 (Northern California) proposed deleting "In a church in which it is impossible for any reason to secure deacons, the duties of the office shall devolve upon the ruling elders" and substituting unordained-diaconate language. CCB found it in conflict with BCO 17-1. Shows the drafting pitfalls O34's narrower wording must avoid. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci04.md)
- **II.W (GA52 O34)** (GA52/2025, in conflict; adopted 8-0-0) — Companion/predecessor from the SAME Savannah River Presbytery: its GA52 Overture 34 tried to require RAO 16 reporting on why a diaconate was not established. CCB found it in conflict precisely because 9-2 already requires duties devolve upon the ruling elders, not other persons/entities. This GA53 O34 is Savannah River's follow-on, now amending 9-2 itself. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci23.md)

### Prior overtures
None found. (The exact-provision spine matched GA10 O17 — trustees assuming deacon administrative duties under BCO 25-6/25-7 — but it does not touch the 9-2 devolve clause; pruned as incidental.)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 9-2** — 2 citations, [Metro Atlanta](../rpr/metro-atlanta.md) Presbytery, 38th GA (2010), both unsatisfactory/outstanding: exceptions to practices that selected diaconal servants by congregational election and "denied the BCO provision for men leading the diaconate." Same diaconate-establishment friction O34 addresses. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Direct companion to **[GA52 O34](../overtures/ga52_2025__o34.md)** (same presbytery, same diaconate concern; CCB found that version in conflict on 9-2 grounds — see II.W above). No BCO 9-2 renumbering bears on the devolve clause (the only chapter-9 renumbering is the 1980 merger of old ch. 9 into ch. 8). Pruned three high-recall spine hits as incidental to O34's specific change: case 2007-13 (Kniseley — titling unordained staff "minister," not the devolve clause; it survives only as the source of the Kniseley standard quoted inside 2009-25/26); inquiry 27-43 II.1 (deacons' authority to sell donated property — first sentence of 9-2, unrelated); and GA10 O17 (trustees vs. deacons on property under 25-6/25-7).

---

## O35 — Amend BCO 31-2 to Establish a Deadline for the Issuing of an Indictment
**Targets:** BCO 31-2 · **Source:** Illiana · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/01/Overture-35_Illiana_31-2.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/01/Overture-35_Illiana_31-2.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a hard deadline to BCO 31-2: once an investigation raises a strong presumption of guilt and the court appoints a prosecutor, the indictment "shall be filed with the clerk of the court within sixty (60) days following the meeting of the court," and a prosecutor who neglects to file is rebuked, dismissed, and replaced. The drafters note the enforcement language is borrowed from BCO 42-7 (clerk's failure to transmit the Record of the Case).

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — the grounds rest only on Scripture (Eccl. 8:11; Deut. 16:19–20) and a textual cross-reference to BCO 42-7; no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries are cited.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2008-14 — White v. Siouxlands Presbytery](../cases/ga38_2010__2008-14.md)** (GA38/2010, sustained) — Turns on the presbytery's handling of the BCO 31-2 "strong presumption of guilt" finding and its failure to investigate properly; a leading exemplar of stalled/deficient 31-2 process. [minutes](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p137)
- **[2009-23 — Koerkenmeier v. Illiana Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-23.md)** (GA39/2011, sustained) — Sustained case from the same presbytery now bringing O35; the record discusses delays and a deadline in the disciplinary process, directly on point to the friction O35 addresses. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p540)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI 12-53 III** (GA12/1984, advice given) — On the scope of charges in a transferred 31-2 case; bears on how the indictment is framed once process is instituted. [page](../inquiries/ga12_1984__ci03.md)
- **26-68 ref. #R-1** (GA26/1998, advice given) — BCO 31-2 permits investigation before adjudication; CCB recommended amendments to clarify BCO 31/32/34 — the structural question O35 now revisits at the indictment-timing stage. [page](../inquiries/ga26_1998__ci01.md)
- **36-30 II.F** (GA36/2008, in conflict) — A 31-2 case "does not exist until process is actually instituted"; frames exactly the window (post-strong-presumption, at-indictment) O35 seeks to time-bound. [page](../inquiries/ga36_2008__ci04.md)
- **App. O II.K** (GA40/2012, not in conflict) — CCB on what triggers a required 31-2 investigative inquiry; companion to O35's concern with what must follow once the trigger is met. [page](../inquiries/ga40_2012__ci01.md)
- **II.G** (GA48/2021, not in conflict; adopted) — CCB found the Overture-12 proposal (clarifying that investigation must precede process under 31-2/32-2) not in conflict and the report item was adopted, though the overture itself was referred back to presbytery. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci07.md)
- **II.S** (GA48/2021, in conflict at multiple points; adopted) — CCB review of an overture prescribing an investigation *sequence* in 31-2; precedent for adding procedural steps/timing to 31-2. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci19.md)
- **II.R** (GA50/2023, in conflict; adopted 8-0-0) — Overture requiring *expedited*, conflict-free investigations in BCO 31; the closest analog to O35's promptness rationale. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci18.md)
- **II.T** (GA51/2024, not in conflict; adopted 7-1-0) — CCB on expanding who may assist a 31-2 investigation; recent 31-2 procedural amendment the CCB cleared. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci20.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA36 O6](../overtures/ga36_2008__o6.md)** (2008, answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 31-2 re: investigative procedures for a TE (Missouri); earliest 31-2 procedural-amendment attempt. [page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p190)
- **[GA48 O12](../overtures/ga48_2021__o12.md)** (2021, referred back to presbytery without prejudice) — Amend BCO 31-2 and 32-2 to clarify that investigation shall precede process (Phila. Metro West); the CCB found it not in conflict (II.G) but the Assembly did not adopt the amendment. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p972)
- **[GA48 O28](../overtures/ga48_2021__o28.md)** (2021, referred back to presbytery without prejudice) — Amend BCO 31-2 to describe a required *sequence* for discipline investigation (Phila. Metro West); the sequence-mandate cousin of O35's timing mandate. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1041)
- **[GA48 O29](../overtures/ga48_2021__o29.md)** (2021, referred back to presbytery without prejudice) — Add BCO Appendix of court investigation suggestions before process (Phila. Metro West); same GA48 push to structure 31-2 practice. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1046)
- **[GA51 O25](../overtures/ga51_2024__o25.md)** (2024, answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 31-2 to allow outside consultants to assist investigations (Tennessee Valley); recent 31-2 amendment attempt that failed. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1176)
- **[GA52 O1](../overtures/ga52_2025__o1.md)** (2025, answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 32-2 to clarify a court's authority to investigate before filing charges (Northern New England); the most recent attempt to fine-tune the investigation→charge sequence. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1163)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 31-2** — 12 RPR rows, almost all documenting the exact friction O35 targets: presbyteries failing to investigate or never disposing of accusations against a TE — e.g., [Southeast Alabama](../rpr/exc/southeast-alabama__036.md) 36th (2008, "Presbytery did not investigate allegations against a TE," outstanding), [South Florida](../rpr/south-florida.md) 40th (2012, charges laid but presbytery did not proceed, outstanding), [South Coast](../rpr/exc/south-coast__103.md) 51st (2024, "treats a BCO 31-2 report as a motion and defeats the motion to begin an investigation," outstanding), and [Metropolitan New York](../rpr/exc/metropolitan-new-york__093.md) 52nd (2025, "insufficient record… of actions taken… pursuant to their handling of a report," open). These are the real-world delay/inaction problems a 60-day deadline is meant to cure. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
The spine is high-recall for BCO 31-2 (132 case hits) because 31-2 governs the investigation that precedes *every* disciplinary case, so it is cited in passing throughout the SJC corpus. The overwhelming majority of those hits construe the substantive "strong presumption of guilt" standard, not the *timing* of indictment — and no prior case construes a filing deadline because none exists. I therefore pruned ~130 incidental case hits and kept only two that reflect genuine real-world friction at the investigation→indictment stage (including Koerkenmeier, from Illiana itself).

Pruned as incidental: 2007-12 Grady v. Southwest Florida Presbytery — BCO 31-2 appears only parenthetically as "see for example BCO 31-2"; the case holds that a presbytery imposed admonition without due process (BCO 30-2) by reading a Shepherding Committee report into its minutes, not about investigation timing or indictment. Pruned as incidental: 2019-10/2019-12 Evans & Pitts et al. v. Arizona Presbytery — case holds that AZP failed BCO 38-1 confession requirements in deposing TE Evans; BCO 31-2 is cited because an Investigative Committee was formed, but the holding turns on BCO 38-1 (approval of facts in confession), not on investigation delay or indictment deadline. The bearing weight of O35 sits in the **CCB/inquiry line** and the **string of recent 31-2 procedural-amendment overtures** (GA36, GA48 ×3, GA51, GA52): GA has repeatedly attempted to amend 31-2's procedure but never its indictment timing — and notably the recent Phila. Metro West cluster (GA48 O12/O28/O29) was each referred back to presbytery without prejudice rather than adopted, even where the CCB found the proposal not in conflict. The **RPR exceptions** are the documented friction the deadline answers. Among prior overtures I pruned body/title-only matches that do not bear on a 31-2 indictment deadline (BCO 34-1 neighboring-presbytery GA19 O12 / GA20 O32; BCO 38-3 renunciation GA24 O26 / GA25 O6; BCO 33-1 GA29 O9; the Greg Johnson original-jurisdiction overtures GA48 O4/O25, GA49 O36/O37; BCO 57-5 GA36 O4; BCO 15-3 GA36 O7; BCO 32-2 GA40 O16; BCO 43-1 GA45 O15; BCO 31-10 GA50 O8; BCO 36 GA52 O32; the SJC-direction GA29 O19 / GA41 O23; and the AC-funding GA40 O15). No renumbering caveat: BCO 31-2 has carried this number throughout the corpus. O35 is referred to CCB and OC.

---

## O36 — Add BCO 8-11 and 9-8 Regarding the Exercise of the Duties and Authority of Elder and Deacon
**Targets:** BCO 8-11 (new), 9-8 (new) · **Source:** Catawba Valley (to CCB, OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/Overture-36_CatawbaValley_8-11.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/03/Overture-36_CatawbaValley_8-11.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a new BCO 8-11 reserving the duties and authority of elders (leading worship, voting in Session, shepherding) to ordained elders, and a new BCO 9-8 reserving diaconal duties and authority (mercy-ministry leadership, voting in diaconal meetings, financial distributions, property oversight) to ordained deacons; both bar women and unordained men from performing those functions or being commissioned/appointed/installed in any manner implying parity with the ordained office. It also encourages presbyteries to review congregational practice for alignment.

**Cites in its own grounds:** 1 Tim 3:1–13; Titus 1:5–9; BCO 7-2 ("ordination… limited to qualified men"); and "recent General Assembly actions, including the affirmation of Overture 26 (2023)" — i.e., GA50 (2023) O26 "Amend BCO 7-3 to Prohibit Ecclesiastical Titles for Unordained People" (Approved & ratified 2024). No case or inquiry cited by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2009-25/2009-26 — Brown v. Northern California Presbytery / Session of Grace Presbyterian Church v. Northern California Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-25_2009-26.md)** (39th/2011, sustained) — Directly construes the underlying question O36 targets: whether and how women/unordained persons may perform diaconal functions. The SJC annulled Northern California Presbytery's abstract resolution declaring six diaconal views permissible, holding no court may issue binding abstract decrees beyond its jurisdiction; a concurring opinion analyzed each view of the diaconate (appointed/elected deaconess, "equal partners," "nobody ordained," GUMP and Kniseley standards). Topical supplement — not in the provision-exact spine because O36 adds entirely new sections. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p548)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **38-34 II.E** (38th/2010, in conflict) — CCB found an overture appointing unordained persons (men and women) to diaconal ministry roles in conflict with the Constitution, including because it implied an unordained office contrary to BCO 17-1; lists BCO 9-8 among the provisions in tension. Bears directly on O36's aim to fence diaconal functions to the ordained office, and shows the CCB has scrutinized legislation in this exact area. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci04.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA38 O10](../overtures/ga38_2010__o10.md)** (2010, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 1-4, 4-2, 5-10, 7-2, 9-2, 9-7 and Add BCO 9-8 for Unordained Diaconal Ministry" (Northern California Presbytery). The closest prior attempt to legislate a new BCO 9-8 about unordained diaconal service — it moved the opposite direction (enabling unordained diaconal ministry) and the Assembly declined it. Most directly bearing precedent on the section O36 now seeks to add. [p.394](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p392), [p.409](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p407), [p.776](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p774)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
O36 adds two brand-new sections (BCO 8-11, 9-8), so the deterministic provision-exact spine returned no judicial cases and no RPR exceptions citing those (non-existent) numbers; its only direct hits were CCB advice 38-34 II.E and prior overture GA38 O10, both of which list BCO 9-8 among their provisions and genuinely bear (no incidental hits to prune). The Brown/Grace v. Northern California cases (2009-25/26) were added by STEP-3 concept search (women/unordained diaconal functions) and verified against a real corpus case file with a live minutes anchor. Renumbering caveat: BCO chapter 8 was amended with an insert-and-shift at 8-8 in 2023 (GA50), so "8-11" is post-2023 numbering and the new section lands after the current 8-10. The overture's own grounds cite "Overture 26 (2023)," which maps to GA50 (2023) O26 (Northwest Georgia Presbytery; ratified 2024) on ecclesiastical titles for unordained people — see [GA50 minutes p.1036](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1028). No GA53 companion overtures are indexed in the corpus (current-year batch is not in OVERTURES.md).

---

## O37 — Amend BCO 9-3 to Allow Women to Serve as Ordained Deacons
**Targets:** BCO 9-3 (+ 12 conforming amendments: 5-9.c, 7-2, 17-3, 24-1, 24-6, 24-7, 24-8, 24-9, 24-10, 36-7, 37-1, 37-6) · **Source:** Pacific · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-37_Pacific_9-3.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-37_Pacific_9-3.pdf)

**What it does:** Strikes "men" from the deacon qualifications in BCO 9-3 (with 12 conforming amendments throughout the BCO) so that local Sessions may decide whether qualified women may be elected and ordained to the office of deacon; the office of elder remains restricted to men (7-2 amended to read "the office of elder is open to men only").

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — the grounds rest on Scripture (Rom. 16:1; 1 Tim. 3:11), complementarian and Reformed scholarship (Piper, Dever, Köstenberger, Schreiner, Calvin, Warfield, Strimple, Frame, Clowney), church history, WCF 20.2, and the practice of other NAPARC bodies. No prior PCA cases, overtures, or inquiries are cited.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2009-25 — Brown v. Northern California Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-25_2009-26.md)** (GA39/2011, sustained) — Construes BCO 9-3 directly: complaint sustained against a presbytery over deaconesses in a NorCal church. Bears squarely as judicial enforcement of the current "men"-only reading of 9-3 that O37 would overturn. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p550)
- **[2009-26 — Session of Grace Presbyterian Church v. Northern California Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-25_2009-26.md)** (GA39/2011, sustained) — Companion complaint on the same NorCal deaconess dispute under BCO 9-3; reinforces SJC enforcement of 9-3 against the practice O37 would legalize. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p550)
- **[2007-13 — Kniseley v. Rocky Mountain](../cases/ga37_2009__2007-13.md)** (GA37/2009, denied) — Cited under 9-3; concerned a woman with an M.Div. who was not ordained. Bears more loosely (reception/ordination of a woman, not deaconess commissioning), but sits in the women-in-office frame O37 engages. [minutes](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p150)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI 12-53 (III,69)** (GA12/1984, advice given) — "Ordination of men who believe women may serve as deacons"; advised that holding the view (while abiding by BCO standards in practice) is not by itself grounds to deny ordination or reception. Directly bears on the doctrinal-latitude question behind O37 (cites BCO 7-2, 9-3, 21-5). [page](../inquiries/ga12_1984__ci09.md)
- **CCB II.Q** (GA47/2019, not in conflict) — On Overture 29 (Metro New York) proposing to amend multiple BCO provisions so individual sessions could decide locally whether women may serve as deacons; CCB found it not in conflict. This is the closest prior precedent to O37's "let local Sessions decide" mechanism (cites 5-9.c, 5-9.i(1), 7-2, 9-3, 17-3, 24, 25). [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci17.md)
- **CCB II.P** (GA50/2023, not in conflict, 8-0-0) ⭐ — On Overture 23 (Mississippi Valley) amending BCO 8-2 and 9-3 to require officers to conform to biblical chastity in self-description; CCB found it not in conflict. Bears only as a recent CCB construction of the same provision's amendment mechanics, not on the women-deacon question (low-bearing). [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci16.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA36 O9](../overtures/ga36_2008__o9.md)** (2008, Answered in the negative) — "Erect Ad Interim Study Committee on Deaconesses" (Philadelphia). A defeated denominational attempt to open the women-deacon question; bears as a direct precursor to O37's aim. [page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p205)
- **GA19 O22 / GA20 O33** (1991–93, ratified) — "Amend BCO 24-5 to Permit Session to Ordain Elders & Deacons." Body+title match concerning ordination-*service* mechanics, not the gender qualification; low-bearing (see Note). [GA19 page](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p58) · [GA20 page](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p58)
- **[GA33 O10](../overtures/ga33_2005__o10.md)** (2006, ratified) — "Amend BCO 24-1 to Require Bible Content Examination for Elders and Deacons." Incidental body+title match on "deacons"; does not bear on the women-deacon question (see Note). [page](../markdown/ga33_2005.md#ga33-p200)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 9-3** — 9 exceptions of record, the cluster directly bearing: [Korean Southern](../rpr/korean-southern.md) (30th/2002 raised, 31st/2003 unsatisfactory — "Ordination of women as deaconesses not provided for"), [Northern California](../rpr/northern-california.md) (35th/2007, 36th/2008, 40th/2012 — repeated "Deaconesses commissioned contrary to BCO 9-3"), [Philadelphia](../rpr/exc/philadelphia__028.md) (35th/2007), [Korean Southern](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__103.md) (40th/2012 — men and women appointed as deacons), and [Chesapeake](../rpr/chesapeake.md) (42nd/2014 — BCO 7-2 & 9-3 compliance). Documents sustained real-world friction: presbyteries permitting deaconesses against 9-3 — exactly the practice O37 would legalize. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
**Topical supplement — the provision-exact spine misses the main battleground.** The central PCA debate on women deacons ran through provisions *other than* 9-3, so the deterministic join did not surface it. The GA38 (2010) cluster is the key historical record and bears strongly on O37: **[GA38 O7](../overtures/ga38_2010__o7.md)** "Reconsider Ordination of Women to the Office of Deacon" (Adopted, [p.386](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p384)); **[GA38 O2](../overtures/ga38_2010__o2.md)** "Amend BCO 9-7 to Prohibit Deaconesses" ([p.388](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p386)); **[GA38 O16](../overtures/ga38_2010__o16.md)** "Affirm the Permissibility of Unordained Deaconesses in the PCA" ([p.392](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p390)); **[GA38 O25](../overtures/ga38_2010__o25.md)** "Reaffirm BCO Standards on Roles of Men and Women in Church Office" (Answered in the negative, [p.396](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p394)). Earlier: **[GA19 O40](../overtures/ga19_1991__o40.md)** "Declare Ordination of Deaconesses a Violation of BCO" ([p.61](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p59)) and **[GA22 O8](../overtures/ga22_1994__o8.md)** "Encourage Godly Men & Women to Assist Deacons" ([p.65](../markdown/ga22_1994.md#ga22-p63)). Most directly, **[GA46 O9](../overtures/ga46_2018__o9.md)** "Amend BCO 9-7 and Add BCO 24-11 Regarding Women Serving as Deaconesses" (Grace, approved → sent to presbyteries, [p.686](../markdown/ga46_2018.md#ga46-p684)) is the most recent prior amendment attempt on this question — but it pursued *unordained* deaconesses via 9-7/24-11, whereas O37 seeks *ordained* women deacons via 9-3, a more direct change than any prior PCA overture. These page links are reproduced verbatim from /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md.
**Pruning:** GA33 O10 (Bible-content exam) and the GA19 O22 / GA20 O33 pair (24-5 ordination-service mechanics) are incidental body+title matches on "deacon(s)" and do not construe the gender qualification; retained but flagged low-bearing. CCB II.P (GA50/2023 chastity self-description) is a 9-3-mechanics match only, not on point. **Renumbering caveat:** BCO chapters 8 & 9 were combined in 1980 (8th GA; section-level mappings unverified in the corpus), so any pre-1980 deacon material may sit under old numbering — none surfaced here.
Pruned as incidental: 2019-11 Crouse v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery — BCO 9-3 appears only in the dissenting opinion's passing list of officer-qualification standards; the majority construes the re-election process under BCO 24-1/39-3, not 9-3's men-only ordination requirement.

---

## O38 — Amend BCO 7-3 and add 9-8 to Allow Sessions Flexibility Regarding the Diaconate
**Targets:** BCO 7-3, 9-8 (new) (plus footnotes to 24-1 and 24-6) · **Source:** Metro Atlanta · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-38_MetroAtlanta_7-3.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-38_MetroAtlanta_7-3.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 7-3 and adds a new BCO 9-8 to let each Session choose among three diaconate models — only ordained male deacons; ordained male deacons plus commissioned/appointed women who are non-officers but may "bear the title of deacon"; or only commissioned/appointed men and women who are non-officers but may bear the title of deacon. It reframes BCO 7-3's title restriction so the deacon title may be applied to unordained persons when a Session has explicitly chosen to do so, partially reversing the effect of the GA50 O26 / 2024 titling amendment. It works the unordained/commissioned route and does not ordain women.

**Cites in its own grounds:** The 2017 Report of the Ad Interim Committee on Women Serving in the Ministry of the Church (45th GA), which it says "deemed [the practice] not prohibited by the BCO"; Overture 26 adopted at GA51 (2024) [= GA50 O26, ratified 2024], which it says made charitable forbearance "more difficult"; Westminster Confession 20.2 (Christian liberty); BCO 9-7, 10-1, 24-6; and Morton H. Smith's BCO Commentary. (No prior judicial case or inquiry is cited by id.)

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (The only spine hit was an aggregated pre-SJC entry from GA12/1984 tagged to "7-3" with no case page and no real construal of the provision — pruned as incidental; see Note.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **38-34 II.E** (GA38/2010, in conflict) — CCB found an overture appointing unordained persons to diaconal ministry in conflict with the Constitution, including because it implied an unordained office contrary to BCO 17-1; cited provisions include BCO 7-2, 9-7, and 9-8. Directly bears: O38 proposes the same "unordained persons bearing the title of deacon / new 9-8" structure the CCB previously flagged. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci04.md)
- **II.S** (GA50/2023, not in conflict; Adopted 6-1-1) — CCB found no constitutional conflict in amending BCO 7-3 to regulate the titling of unordained individuals (the predecessor to O26). Bears directly: O38 reopens the very BCO 7-3 titling question the CCB addressed, in the opposite direction. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci19.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA38 O10](../overtures/ga38_2010__o10.md)** (2010, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 1-4, 4-2, 5-10, 7-2, 9-2, 9-7 and Add BCO 9-8 for Unordained Diaconal Ministry" (Northern California). The near-twin of O38: same proposed new BCO 9-8 creating an unordained-diaconal-ministry track; rejected. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p392)
- ⭐ **[GA50 O26](../overtures/ga50_2023__o26.md)** (2023, Approved & ratified 2024) — "Amend BCO 7-3 to Prohibit Ecclesiastical Titles for Unordained People" (Northwest Georgia). The enacted amendment O38 expressly seeks to soften; this is the immediate change in BCO 7-3 that O38 rewrites. [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1028)
- **[GA46 O9](../overtures/ga46_2018__o9.md)** (2018, Approved → sent to presbyteries; ratification not located) — "Amend BCO 9-7 and Add BCO 24-11 Regarding Women Serving as Deaconesses" (Grace). A recent prior attempt to provide for women in diaconal service. [page](../markdown/ga46_2018.md#ga46-p684)
- **[GA46 O25](../overtures/ga46_2018__o25.md)** (2018, Answered in the negative) — "Address the Unordained Diaconate" (Savannah River). Recent prior overture on the unordained diaconate question O38 raises. [page](../markdown/ga46_2018.md#ga46-p774)
- **[GA38 O16](../overtures/ga38_2010__o16.md)** (2010, no outcome recorded) — "Affirm the Permissibility of Unordained Deaconesses in the PCA" (Tennessee Valley). Same liberty-to-commission-women rationale as O38. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p390)
- **[GA38 O2](../overtures/ga38_2010__o2.md)** (2010) — "Amend BCO 9-7 to Prohibit Deaconesses" (Central Carolina). The contrary motion from the same Assembly; frames the long-running BCO 9-7/diaconate dispute O38 enters. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p386)
- **GA36 O9 / O19** (2008, Answered in the negative / Answered by reference) — competing overtures to erect vs. decline an Ad Interim Study Committee on Deaconesses. Shows the GA repeatedly declining to formalize a deaconess track. [O9 page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p205) · [O19 page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p212)
- **[GA19 O40](../overtures/ga19_1991__o40.md)** (1991) — "Declare Ordination of Deaconesses a Violation of BCO" (TE Shipman). Early framing of the office/title boundary O38 navigates. [page](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p59)
- **[GA12 O28](../overtures/ga12_1984__o28.md)** (1984, Answered in the negative) — "Study the Question of Women Serving in the Diaconate" (Delmarva). The earliest of the recurring diaconate-and-women overtures; rejected. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p44)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (The single BCO 7-3 RPR row — [Korean Southwest](../rpr/korean-southwest.md), 52nd/2025 — concerns a presbytery's delinquency in reporting on a member church, not the titling/diaconate substance of 7-3; pruned as non-bearing. See Note.)

### Note
O38 is the latest move in the PCA's decades-long deaconess/unordained-diaconate debate; the spine's exact-provision join (BCO 7-3, 9-8) surfaced only two CCB items and a near-empty case/RPR list, so the bearing record here is built largely from the **topical supplement** (concept = "women/unordained serving as deacons; deacon titling"), all citations verbatim from /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md. **Strongest bearing actions:** GA38 O10 (the structural near-twin proposing the same new BCO 9-8, rejected) and GA50 O26 (the enacted 7-3 titling rule O38 rewrites — and which O38 cites in its grounds as "Overture 26 ... 51st GA 2024," the same amendment ratified in 2024). Inquiry 12-53/1984 (ordination of men who believe women may serve as deacons; advice that such belief alone is not grounds to deny ordination) is also topically relevant but was not in the join and is left out of the formatted list to keep every bullet on a join-sourced deep-link. **Pruned as incidental:** (1) the GA12/1984 aggregated pre-SJC "judicial cases" entry tagged "7-3" — no case page, no substantive construal; (2) GA51 O32 from the spine's prior_overtures — it is actually "Amend BCO 23 ... Dissolution of Call for Permanent Committee and Agency Ministers," unrelated to the diaconate (a stray 9-8 page match); (3) the Korean Southwest BCO 7-3 RPR row (delinquency reporting, not titling). **Renumbering:** none — BCO chapters 7 and 9 carry no entries in bco_renumberings.jsonl. **Recency star window (GA48–52):** GA50 O26 (2023, ratified 2024) falls within GA48–52 and is starred; no other bearing prior overture is in that window.

---

## O39 — Amend BCO 22 to Affirm the Consent of the Governed for Assistant Pastors
**Targets:** BCO 22 (specifically 22-3 and 22-4) · **Source:** Central Florida Presbytery (CFL) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-39_CFL_22.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-39_CFL_22.pdf)

**What it does:** Caps an assistant pastor's call at a definite period (ordinarily ≤5 years); to retain him beyond that, the Session must recommend him to the **congregation** for election as associate pastor (majority vote), or else move to dissolve the call under BCO 23 — giving the congregation a periodic consent vote over a continuing teaching elder. Adds an editorial comment grandfathering calls established before June 22, 2027.

**Cites in its own grounds:** **Overture 10, 52nd GA (2025)** — O39 expressly states it "improves Overture 10 from the 52nd General Assembly, which was referred back to the Central Florida Presbytery for refinement and potential resubmission" (O39 is that resubmission). It also invokes the editorial-comment precedent following BCO 24-10 to justify its effective-date carve-out (BCO 24-10 is a constitutional text, not a past judicial/legislative action, so it is not listed below). Scriptural/constitutional grounds cited: Preliminary Principle 6, BCO 3-1, 8-9, 16-2; Acts 6:3, 14:23; and the 1945 PCUS BCO (ch. xxiv ¶126).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-05 — Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-05.md)** (GA52/2025, granted in part) — Directly construes BCO 22-2, 22-3, and 22-4 in dissolving an assistant pastor's call; the SJC held that no congregational vote was constitutionally required to dissolve an assistant pastor's call — the precise lay-consent gap O39 seeks to close. ⭐ [full text](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-05.md)
- **[2007-09/2007-10 — Complaints of TE Eliot Lee vs. Korean Eastern Presbytery](../cases/ga37_2009__2007-09_2007-10.md)** (GA37/2009, sustained) — Annulled higher-court action over a local pastoral relation taken "without congregational consent," articulating the non-hierarchical, consent-of-the-governed principle O39 builds its grounds upon. [full text](../cases/ga37_2009__2007-09_2007-10.md)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CCB II.G — advice on Overture 10** (GA52/2025) — The CCB's advice on O39's own predecessor: it found the consent-for-assistant-pastors amendment "ambiguous… [because] it did not address how current assistant pastors would be treated upon adoption." O39's new effective-date editorial comment is the direct fix for this objection — the single highest-value bearing action. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci07.md)
- **CCB 33-29 II.C** (GA33/2005) — CCB found a prior overture detailing how assistant pastors are called to be in conflict with BCO 3-2 and 12-2 through 12-4, on the view that the assistant pastor's relationship to a congregation "is best left to the session" — the polity counter-argument O39 must overcome. [page](../inquiries/ga33_2005__ci02.md)
- **CI 17-82 III,17** (GA17/1989) — Tennessee Valley Presbytery asked whether the 1988 BCO 22-3/22-4 assistant pastor amendments applied retroactively; bears directly on O39's effective-date / non-retroactivity editorial comment. [page](../inquiries/ga17_1989__ci03.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA52 O10](../overtures/ga52_2025__o10.md)** (2025, Referred) — "Amend BCO 22 to Affirm the 'Consent of the Governed' Regarding Assistant Pastors" (Central Florida). The direct predecessor; referred back to CFL for refinement and resubmitted as O39. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1185)
- **[GA49 O2](../overtures/ga49_2022__o2.md)** (2022) — "Amend BCO 22-3 to Allow Assistant Pastors to File Complaints Against Sessions" (Tennessee Valley); another attempt to recalibrate the assistant pastor / Session relationship under 22-3. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1286)
- **[GA48 O31](../overtures/ga48_2021__o31.md)** (2021, Approved & ratified 2022) — "Amend BCO 22 Process for Assistant to Associate Pastor" (Northwest Georgia); the most recent successful BCO 22 assistant-pastor amendment, establishing the assistant→associate conversion process O39 modifies. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1131)
- **[GA33 O7](../overtures/ga33_2005__o7.md)** (2005, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 21-5, 6, 7, 8, 10 and 22-4 Regarding Assistant Pastors" (Chesapeake); a failed prior attempt to reshape assistant pastor calls (the overture the CCB 33-29 advice above addressed). [page](../markdown/ga33_2005.md#ga33-p195)
- **[GA16 O3](../overtures/ga16_1988__o3.md)** (1988, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 22-2 to Require Congregational Election of Assistant Pastors" (Northeast); the earliest and most on-point prior attempt at the very change O39 seeks — congregational consent/election for assistant pastors — and it failed. [page](../markdown/ga16_1988.md#ga16-p46)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 22-3** — 6 citations faulting assistant pastor calls (e.g., [Georgia Foothills](../rpr/exc/georgia-foothills__053.md) 52nd/2025: assistant pastor appointed "without record of receiving a call"; [Korean Capital](../rpr/korean-capital.md) 52nd/2025: assistant-to-associate change without proper election); recurring friction at the call/consent boundary O39 targets. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 22-4** — 10 citations repeatedly faulting the lack of congregational/session action in changing or dissolving assistant pastor calls (e.g., [Gulfstream](../rpr/gulfstream.md) 50th/2023 & 51st/2024: "No record of request from congregation to a change of call from assistant pastor to associate pastor"); concrete evidence that the consent gap O39 addresses generates records exceptions. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Non-provision (chapter-level "BCO 22") overture: the deterministic join returned provisions=[] and zero exact-provision hits, so every action above comes from a topical search of the index (CASES.md / cases.jsonl, INQUIRIES.md, CCB-OVERTURE-ADVICE.md, OVERTURES.md, RPR-BY-PROVISION.md). Highest-value bearing action: the CCB's GA52 advice on predecessor Overture 10 — O39's added editorial comment exists precisely to cure the ambiguity the CCB flagged. PRUNED as incidental: cases 1997-17 (Lebo — assistant pastor *fund*/budget under 12-5b) and 2005-1 (Chastain — divisive-behavior discipline that merely mentions an assistant pastor); the two GA30/2001 Korean cases (2001-17/2001-19), which involve assistant pastors only factually and have no corpus case page; and the GA13/GA14 inquiries on associate-pastor voting/salary under 22-2, which do not reach the assistant pastor call question. No chapter renumbering affects BCO 22 (22-3/22-4 have carried these numbers since the 1988 amendments cited in the overture's own grounds).

---

## O40 — Amend RAO 4-9 to Set Calendar Year Terms for Stated Clerk and Coordinators
**Targets:** RAO 4-9 · **Source:** Savannah River · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-40_SavannahRiver_RAO4-9.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-40_SavannahRiver_RAO4-9.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends RAO 4-9 so the term of service for all permanent-committee coordinators and the Stated Clerk runs by calendar year (January 1 – December 31) instead of ending at the close of the Assembly; if a man is not re-elected, his term continues through December 31, and beginning January 1 the committee appoints a non-candidate provisional coordinator who presents a candidate at the next General Assembly.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — the whereas clauses argue from policy (vocational uncertainty, transition lead time, denominational growth) and cite no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **Supplemental II.2** (52nd GA / 2025) — Floor nominations for Stated Clerk when the AC brings no nominee; CCB ruled floor nominations are permitted under RAO 3-4. Construes RAO 4-9's election mechanism for the Stated Clerk, which O40 restructures. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci35.md)
- **Supplemental III.1** (49th GA / 2022) — Whether Committees of Commissioners may nominate substitute program coordinators; CCB ruled a CoC may only approve or disapprove, not nominate a substitute. Construes the RAO 4-9 coordinator-nomination/election mechanism O40 amends. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci29.md)
- **Supplemental III.2** (49th GA / 2022) — Floor nomination procedure for the office of Stated Clerk (same procedure as other contested offices; nominee must be examined by TEC). Bears on the RAO 4-9 election/examination clause O40 retains while changing terms. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci30.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA39 O2](../overtures/ga39_2011__o2.md)** (2011, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 4-9 to set term limits for program-committee coordinators and the Stated Clerk. Closest precedent: a prior attempt to replace the annual-reelection scheme of the same provision, declined. [page](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p77)
- **[GA19 O43](../overtures/ga19_1991__o43.md)** (1991, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 4-9 to limit coordinators and Stated Clerk to two four-year terms. Earliest attempt to replace annual reelection under RAO 4-9 with fixed terms; also declined. [page](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p60)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
The provision-exact spine pulled three CCB inquiries (GA49 Supplemental III.1, GA49 Supplemental III.2, GA52 Supplemental II.2) and two prior RAO 4-9 overtures (GA19 O43, GA39 O2); all are retained as bearing on the same election/term mechanism. PRUNED from the spine: nothing incidental — the GA47 RAO-4-series inquiries did not surface here. Topical supplement considered but PRUNED as less on-point than the exact-4-9 prior overtures: GA15 O37 ("Amend RAO Article III on GA Coordinator and Stated Clerk Selection," adopted, [page](../markdown/ga15_1987.md#ga15-p42)) and GA12 O38 ("Require GA Coordinator Candidates to Be Examined Before Election," negatived, [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p57)) — both touch coordinator/clerk selection but not the term-of-service structure O40 changes. Also noted topically: GA52 Supplemental II.1 (substitute nomination for Stated Clerk) is part of the same June-2025 cluster as Supplemental II.2 but indexes under RAO 14-6, so it is left out of the bearing list. No SJC/CJB case and no RPR exception cites RAO 4-9. No renumbering applies (RAO 4-9 absent from bco_renumberings.jsonl). The salient pattern: both prior RAO 4-9 term overtures were defeated.

---

## O41 — Amend RAO 4-9 to Require 2/3 Majority to Elect Stated Clerk and Coordinators
**Targets:** RAO 4-9 · **Source:** Savannah River · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-41_SavannahRiver_RAO4-9.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-41_SavannahRiver_RAO4-9.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends RAO 4-9 to add that a permanent-Committee coordinator and the Stated Clerk "shall be elected or re-elected only by a two-thirds (2/3) majority vote of the commissioners present and voting," replacing the current simple-majority threshold; effective immediately upon adoption for all future elections and re-elections.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None by case/overture/inquiry. The grounds cite only provisions by analogy — supermajority precedents in BCO 26-2, 3 (amendments); BCO 31-10; 34-8, 10 (discipline); BCO 42-6 (judicial appeals); and RAO 4-11 (budget modifications).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **Supplemental II.2** (GA52/2025) — Floor nominations for Stated Clerk when the AC brings no nominee; CCB ruled (8-0-0) that floor nominations are permitted under RAO 3-4 even if the AC brings no nominee. Construes the RAO 4-9 Stated-Clerk election mechanism a 2/3 threshold would re-condition. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci35.md)
- **Supplemental III.2** (GA49/2022) — Floor nomination procedure for the office of Stated Clerk; CCB advised floor nominations follow the same procedure as other contested offices, with TEC examination required. Directly construes the RAO 4-9 Stated-Clerk election the overture would re-threshold. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci30.md)
- **Supplemental III.1** (GA49/2022) — Whether Committees of Commissioners may nominate substitute program coordinators; CCB ruled a CoC may only approve or disapprove a coordinator nominee, not nominate a substitute. Construes the RAO 4-9 coordinator-election framework the overture amends. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci29.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA39 O2](../overtures/ga39_2011__o2.md)** (2011, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 4-9 to set term limits for program-committee coordinators and the Stated Clerk. A prior, provision-exact attempt to tighten this same officer-election rule (term limits, not vote threshold); declined. [page](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p77)
- **[GA19 O43](../overtures/ga19_1991__o43.md)** (1991, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 4-9 to limit coordinators and the Stated Clerk to two four-year terms. The earliest attempt to amend RAO 4-9's officer rules; also declined, showing the Assembly's long-standing reluctance to tighten this provision. [page](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p60)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
RAO 4-9 is a Rules-of-Assembly-Operations provision, not BCO, so there are no SJC/CJB cases or RPR exceptions on it (the spine returned both empty) — expected and correct. The two prior overtures are provision-exact RAO 4-9 amendments but targeted **term limits**, not a **vote threshold**; they bear as prior attempts to amend the same officer-election provision and as evidence the Assembly has twice declined to tighten it, though neither tested a supermajority specifically. All three inquiries are genuine RAO 4-9 construction (Stated Clerk / coordinator election procedure) and are retained; none pruned as incidental. The prior first-pass draft cited a GA29/2001 CCB inquiry, GA40 O9, and GA15 O37, plus an O40/O43/O73/O77 GA53 cluster — none of these appear in the deterministic RAO 4-9 spine and could not be verified as real corpus deep-links, so they have been dropped to keep every citation provision-exact and link-backed.

---

## O42 — Restore the Reference to the Westminster Standards at the end of BCO 29-1
**Targets:** BCO 29-1 · **Source:** NorCal · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-42_NorCal_29-1.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-42_NorCal_29-1.pdf)

**What it does:** Directs the Stated Clerk to restore the phrase "as interpreted in these Standards" to the end of BCO 29-1's final sentence, so an offense must be provable "from Scripture as interpreted in these Standards" (the Westminster Standards) — language the overture says was in the original 1973 BCO but disappeared from modern editions with no located GA action removing it. It treats this as a clerical restoration (no ratification needed), while welcoming an amendment process if CCB deems ratification required.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (cites only commentaries — Almquist's *Our Bond of Union* (2025) p.247, Ramsay's *Exposition* (1898), Morton Smith's *Commentary* (2007) — the original 1973 BCO, WLC 136, and the OPC Book of Discipline; no GA cases, overtures, or inquiries).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2007-8 — Jones v. Louisiana Presbytery (Wilkins)](../cases/ga36_2008__2007-08.md)** (GA36/2008, sustained) — Turns on the "proper Constitutional standard" for judging whether a TE's doctrine is out of accord with "the standards of our Constitution" / the Westminster Standards — exactly the offense-judging function the lost phrase performs. [minutes](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p117)
- **[2006-2 — Central Carolina memorial re: Louisiana & TE Wilkins](../cases/ga36_2008__2006-02.md)** (GA36/2008, other) — Frames the charge as teaching doctrine "in flagrant contradiction to our Standards," i.e. whether a doctrinal offense is measured against the Westminster Standards. [minutes](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p75)
- **[2011-11 — Hahn v. Philadelphia Metro West Presbytery](../cases/ga42_2014__2011-11_2011-12_2011-15_2011-16.md)** (GA42/2014, denied) — Quotes the final sentence of BCO 29-1 *already missing* "as interpreted in these Standards" — direct evidence of the omission O42 seeks to cure and of the SJC operating on the truncated text. [minutes](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p502)
- **[2024-18 — Harris v. Wisconsin Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-18.md)** (GA52/2025, denied) — Construes BCO 29-1's definition of an offense as "the proper object of judicial process," cautioning "Sometimes, we take BCO 29-1 too far" — bears on the scope-limiting purpose of the restored phrase. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1037)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **App. O II.E** (GA46/2018, in conflict) — CCB found a proposed BCO 59 marriage-consent revision in conflict, reasoning in part from BCO 29-1; bears insofar as it uses 29-1's offense definition to test whether a contested practice may be treated as an offense. [page](../inquiries/ga46_2018__ci02.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA22 O32](../overtures/ga22_1994__o32.md)** (1994, no recorded outcome) — Heartland Presbytery to CCB, "Clarify Distinction Between Biblical & Organizational BCO Violations" — directly concerns what may be charged as an offense, the same definitional question BCO 29-1 governs. [page](../markdown/ga22_1994.md#ga22-p65)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 29-1** — 1 citation ([Central Indiana](../rpr/central-indiana.md), 48th/2021, unsatisfactory/outstanding): a presbytery committee reported on a member's Christian character without the presbytery initiating process — loosely touches 29-1's offense/process threshold. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
O42 is a corrective/restoration overture, so the highest-value evidence is not adverse precedent but the corpus showing the *current* (truncated) text in operation — see Hahn (2011-11), which quotes 29-1's final sentence without the phrase. The provision-exact spine returned 32 cases citing BCO 29-1; the great majority cite it only for the boilerplate "anything... contrary to the Word of God" definition of an offense in passing (1990-8, 1993-10, 1993-12, the John Wood Matter, 2002-1, 2005-1, the bare GA36 p.85 entry, 2009-28, the 2009-16 and 2009-03 matters, 2010-26, 2011-6, 2012-4, 2012-5, 2013-1, 2015-10, 2015-11, 2016-8, 2016-9, 2016-11, 2019-1, 2019-3, 2020-4, 2020-6, 2021-13, 2022-7, 2024-2). These 27 are pruned as incidental. The four retained cases each engage the *standard by which a (especially doctrinal) offense is judged against the Westminster Standards* — the exact function of the restored phrase. The 2025 CI on BCO 32-2 (II.A) cites 29-1 only as part of the discipline framework and is pruned; the 2018 marriage advice (App. O II.E) is retained as borderline-bearing. GA40 O26 (in thesi statements on evolution/Adam) is pruned as too tangential. No renumbering applies — chapter 29 is not in bco_renumberings.jsonl. (This replaces a first pass whose CI ga27/1999 ci03 citation did not appear in the deterministic spine and could not be verified as a corpus deep-link; it has been dropped.)
Pruned as incidental: 2019-11 Crouse v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery — BCO 29-1 appears once in the majority opinion (alongside 29-2 and 32-18) for the narrow proposition that a Session need not bring charges before exercising election discretion; the case construes BCO 24-1/39-3 re-election procedure, not 29-1's Westminster Standards interpretive role. The Westminster Standards references in the case concern the candidate's examination questions, unconnected to 29-1.

---

## O43 — Amend RAO 4-9 so that Coordinators of Committees are Elected to 4-year Terms
**Targets:** RAO 4-9 · **Source:** Pacific Northwest Presbytery · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-43_PNW_RAO4-9.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-43_PNW_RAO4-9.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends RAO 4-9 so the four program Committees and the Administrative Committee nominate a coordinator/Stated Clerk for election to a four-year term (rather than annually), with men eligible to serve multiple successive terms if reelected. The effect is to replace annual reelection with staggered four-year terms beginning at GA53 (2026).

**Cites in its own grounds:** None — the rationale argues by analogy to AC (4-yr) and CDM/MNA/MTW/RUF (5-yr) member terms and to the agencies' presidents/EDs, but names no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **Supplemental III.1** (GA49/2022) — Whether Committees of Commissioners may nominate substitute program coordinators; CCB ruled a CoC may only approve or disapprove nominees for program coordinator, not nominate substitutes. Bears as a construction of how RAO 4-9 coordinator nomination/election operates, though it concerns the nomination mechanism, not term length. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci29.md)
- **Supplemental III.2** (GA49/2022) — Floor nomination procedure for the office of Stated Clerk; CCB advised floor nominations follow the same procedure as other contested offices and nominees must be examined by the TEC. Bears on the RAO 4-9 election/examination clause this overture leaves intact. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci30.md)
- **Supplemental II.2** (GA52/2025) — Floor nominations for Stated Clerk when the AC brings no nominee; CCB ruled floor nominations are permitted under RAO 3-4 even absent an AC nominee (Adopted 8-0-0). Recent construction of the RAO 4-9 nomination-by-committee scheme that this overture amends. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci35.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA39 O2](../overtures/ga39_2011__o2.md)** (2011, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 4-9 to Set Term Limits for Program Committee Coordinators and Stated Clerk (South Florida Presbytery). Directly on point: a prior attempt to change the term structure of the very same provision; the Assembly declined. [page](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p77)
- **[GA19 O43](../overtures/ga19_1991__o43.md)** (1991, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 4-9 to Limit Coordinators & Stated Clerk to Two Four-Year Terms (Presbytery of the Ascension). The earliest attempt to restructure RAO 4-9 coordinator/clerk terms into four-year terms; declined. [page](../markdown/ga19_1991.md#ga19-p60)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
The two prior overtures (GA39 O2, GA19 O43) are the controlling precedent — both proposed multi-year terms for RAO 4-9 coordinators/clerk and both were answered in the negative, making this the third bite at the same apple (this version omits the two-term cap both predecessors carried). Neither prior overture is GA48–52, so neither is starred. The three inquiries all cite RAO 4-9 but construe its *nomination / floor-nomination* mechanics rather than term length; they are kept as bearing-but-peripheral context, not as direct precedent on the change. Pruned from the topical search: GA12 O38 (examine coordinators before election), GA15 O37 (amend RAO Article III on coordinator/clerk selection), and GA18 O8 (keep the title "Coordinator") — all touch the coordinator/clerk election machinery but are not provision-exact to RAO 4-9 and address different questions (examination / Article III / title), so they are noted here rather than listed. Companion GA53 RAO 4-9 overtures to cross-check on the floor: O40/O41 (Savannah River), O73 (TE Hooper), and O77 (SEAL) — O77 in particular is nearly identical (four-year terms for coordinators and Stated Clerk), while O40 sets calendar-year terms and O41/O73 raise the election threshold. No judicial cases, CCB stand-alone advice, or RPR exceptions cite RAO 4-9. No renumbering applies (RAO 4-9 is stable; bco_renumberings covers BCO 24 only).

---

## O44 — Divide Covenant Presbytery into Two Presbyteries
**Targets:** (boundaries) — BCO 14-6.e; BCO Chapter 13 · **Source:** Covenant · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-44_Covenant_DividingPresbytery.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-44_Covenant_DividingPresbytery.pdf)

**What it does:** Asks the GA, pursuant to BCO 14-6.e, to remove the Arkansas counties from Covenant Presbytery (now 46 churches, ~7,000 members across W. Tennessee, N. Mississippi, and Arkansas) and erect a new "Arkansas Presbytery" comprising all Arkansas counties except Benton, Carroll, Washington, Madison, and Boone (~9 churches + 1 mission work, ~1,200 members), authorizing it to conduct business effective July 1, 2026 consistent with BCO Chapter 13.

**Cites in its own grounds:** No prior case, overture, or inquiry by number. Cites the 16th GA (1988) "guidelines for the multiplication of existing Presbyteries" and the 41st GA (2013) "Guidelines for Forming New Presbyteries through the Division or Multiplication of Existing Presbyteries"; grounds its prayer in BCO 14-6.e and BCO Chapter 13.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (The exact-provision spine returns no provisions; cases citing BCO 14-6 invoke the chapter's general enumeration of GA powers in complaints against presbyteries, not the GA's power to divide/erect a presbytery — incidental. See Note.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **GA50 IV. Non-Judicial Reference 1** (2023) — "Whether one presbytery may involuntarily dissociate another presbytery from the PCA." Construes BCO 14-6.e — the exact provision O44 invokes; CCB held no involuntary-dissociation procedure exists, confirming that restructuring presbyteries runs through the GA-action route under 14-6.e that O44 follows. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci21.md)
- **GA47 III.C** (2019) — "Effect of presbytery division on advice and consent voting." Directly addresses the mechanics of dividing a presbytery: a newly erected presbytery may give advice and consent on amendments already voted by its predecessor, but transferred presbyters may not vote twice — the housekeeping question the new "Arkansas Presbytery" will raise. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci24.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA45 O21](../overtures/ga45_2017__o21.md)** (2017, Adopted) — Covenant Presbytery, "Form a New Presbytery from North Texas and Covenant Presbyteries." Covenant's own most recent presbytery-formation action and the closest precedent for the present division. [page](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p675)
- **[GA45 O19](../overtures/ga45_2017__o19.md)** (2017, Adopted) — Southwest, "Divide the Presbytery of the Southwest into Two Presbyteries." Recent template for a straight geographic division. [page](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p673)
- **[GA46 O22](../overtures/ga46_2018__o22.md)** (2018, Adopted) — Metropolitan New York, "Divide Metropolitan New York into Two Presbyteries." Recent division precedent. [page](../markdown/ga46_2018.md#ga46-p715)
- **[GA39 O1](../overtures/ga39_2011__o1.md)** (2011, Adopted) — Central Carolina, "Multiply Central Carolina Presbytery and Form Additional Presbytery." Modern division performed under the multiplication guidelines O44 relies on. [page](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p77)
- **[GA22 O19](../overtures/ga22_1994__o19.md)** (1994, Adopted) — Calvary, "Divide Calvary Presbytery to Form a New Fellowship Presbytery." Long-standing pattern of GA approving divisions on MNA recommendation. [page](../markdown/ga22_1994.md#ga22-p64)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (Chapter 13 RPR exceptions all concern presbytery meeting/records procedure — quorum, annual review of session records, recording of actions — none bears on dividing or erecting a presbytery. See Note.)

### Note
Non-provision (boundary) overture: the deterministic spine returns provisions=[], so every bearing action here comes from a concept search (presbytery division/erection; BCO 14-6.e; Chapter 13). **Pruning:** the cases citing BCO 14-6 (Bogue v. Ascension; Brown / Grace Ch. v. Northern California 2009-25/26; Barnes v. Heartland; the GA51 BCO 40-5 matters) invoke Chapter 14's general powers in judicial complaints against presbyteries, not the GA's power to divide/erect — pruned as incidental. The Chapter-13 RPR exceptions (records/quorum) are off-point and pruned. **Companions:** O44 sits in the GA53 boundary cluster (per /workspace/ga53/GA53-OVERTURE-RESEARCH.md, with O10/O87 Pittsburgh-Ohio, O62, O70) and is the latest in a long Covenant boundary series (GA34 O1 enlarge; GA40 O5 Montgomery Co.; GA42 O1/O10; GA45 O21 form new presbytery; GA51 O8 Choctaw; GA52 O20 Lowndes; GA52 O21 Hills & Plains, withdrawn) — this is the first full *division* of Covenant. **Judgment call:** division overtures route to MNA and have a near-uniform "Adopted" record, so the bearing here is precedential/procedural (the 14-6.e route and the post-division voting mechanics of GA47 III.C) rather than contested.

---

## O45 — Amend RAO 8-4.i to Require Floor Nominations Come from Previously Submitted Presbytery Nominees
**Targets:** RAO 8-4.i · **Source:** Covenant Presbytery (to CCB, OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-45_Covenant_RAO8-4.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-45_Covenant_RAO8-4.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a sentence to RAO 8-4.i so that floor ("additional") nominations for Permanent Committees and Agencies are valid only if the individual was previously submitted by a Presbytery to the Nominating Committee but left off its final report — preserving the Assembly's right to elect non-recommended nominees while requiring all nominees to have passed through Presbytery review.

**Cites in its own grounds:** No cases/overtures/inquiries by number. Rationale #5 cites by analogy the 2016 RAO amendment on personal resolutions (RAO 11-10); Rationale #4 analogizes floor nominations to minority reports.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.I** (GA47/2019) — Overture 12 from Northern New England Presbytery to amend **RAO 8-4 regarding floor nominations** was found not in conflict and adopted by the CCB. Bears directly: a prior attempt to amend the very provision and question O45 addresses. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci09.md)
- **III** (GA49/2022) — CCB advised that Tennessee Valley Presbytery's proposed **amendment to RAO 8-4** is in order and not in conflict with BCO/RAO standards. Bears: prior amendment of the same provision passing CCB review. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci26.md)
- **Supplemental III.2** (GA49/2022) — CCB advised that **floor nominations** for Stated Clerk follow the same procedure as other contested offices and nominees must be examined by the TEC (cites RAO 3-4, RAO 8-4, BCO 14-1, RAO 4-9). Bears: construes floor-nomination procedure under RAO 8-4. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci30.md)
- **II.O** (GA50/2023) — CCB found that amending **RAO 8-4.h**, 17-1 & 19-2 to specify when minority reports are permitted is not in conflict with the BCO. Bears: governs the adjacent subsection (8-4.h) and the minority-report concept O45's Rationale #4 invokes. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci15.md)
- **Supplemental II.2** (GA52/2025) — CCB ruled **floor nominations are permitted under RAO 3-4** even if the AC brings no Stated Clerk nominee (cites RAO 3-4, RAO 4-9, **RAO 8-4.i**, RAO 13, BCO 14-1.14); Adopted 8-0-0. Bears strongly: most recent construction, and the only action citing RAO 8-4.i exactly. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci35.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA50 O22](../overtures/ga50_2023__o22.md)** (2023, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 8-4.h, 17-1 & 19-2 to Specify When Minority Reports Are Permitted. Bears: a prior attempt to amend an adjacent subsection of RAO 8-4, and the minority-report analogy is the structural model O45's Rationale #4 relies on. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1077)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
O45 self-anchors to the 2016 personal-resolutions reform (RAO 11-10) and to minority-report procedure (RAO 8-4.h) rather than to any numbered prior action. **Pruned as incidental:** (1) All 21 RPR rows in the spine cite **BCO 8-4** (annual reports of teaching elders laboring out of bounds) — a wholly unrelated provision the provision-exact join false-matched against the string "8-4"; none bear on RAO 8-4.i floor nominations. (2) Prior overture **GA47 O12 "Reaffirm the GA's Original Statement on Abortion"** (Evangel Presbytery) is a title/body false positive matched on "Northern New England," unrelated to nominations — pruned. The retained CCB item II.O / overture O22 (RAO 8-4.h) is one provision-letter removed from O45's exact target but is genuinely bearing because O45 itself argues by analogy to minority reports.

---

## O46 — Add BCO 29-5 on Public Allegations without Prior Reporting to the Court of Jurisdiction as Probable Violations of the Ninth Commandment
**Targets:** BCO 29-5 (new) · **Source:** New York State · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-46_NewYorkState_29-5.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-46_NewYorkState_29-5.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a new BCO 29-5 declaring that any public statement made outside a church court alleging an offense or unconstitutional action of a church, Presbytery, agency, committee, or member — that was not first reported to the court of original jurisdiction (ordinarily after a reasonable effort to contact the alleged errant party) — "shall be considered a probable violation of the ninth commandment and an offense under this chapter to be addressed by normal judicial process (BCO 31, etc.)."

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (the rationale quotes only Westminster Larger Catechism Q/A 144 and 145; it cites no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[1993-11 — McDade v. Susquehanna Valley Presbytery](../cases/ga23_1995__1993-11.md)** (GA23/1995, denied) — Directly on the overture's premise: a slander / ninth-commandment complaint where the SJC upheld the Presbytery's choice to *investigate before charging* and found proper procedure followed. Construes how 9th-commandment allegations move through judicial process. [minutes](../markdown/ga23_1995.md#ga23-p110)
- **[2002-14 — Lachman v. Philadelphia Presbytery](../cases/ga32_2004__2002-14.md)** (GA32/2004, denied) — Ninth-commandment offense charged through the Matthew 18 process before the session as court of original jurisdiction — the "proper channels first" model O46 would codify. [minutes](../markdown/ga32_2004.md#ga32-p73)
- **[2021-6 — Herron et al. v. Central Indiana Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2021-06.md)** (GA49/2022, not sustained) — Squarely tests whether a *public statement* by a court (a press release about an investigation) was proper. Most on-point on the line O46 draws between public airing and reporting to the court. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p785)
- **[2021-13 — Dudt v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2021-13.md)** (GA49/2022, sustained) — RE convicted by his Session partly for a 9th-commandment violation via an email to the congregation; SJC reversed. Cuts *against* the overture's premise — shows the risk in treating a member's out-of-court public communication as an offense. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p909)
- **[2022-7 — Harrell et al. v. Covenant Presbytery](../cases/ga50_2023__2022-07.md)** (GA50/2023, sustained) — Indictment-specificity case (BCO 29/32) in which slander / ninth-commandment counts were charged; bears on how a "probable 9th-commandment violation" must be pleaded as an offense. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p860)
- **[2022-10 — Presbyterian Church in America v. TE Daniel Herron](../cases/ga50_2023__2022-10.md)** (GA50/2023, other) — Trial touching a defamation lawsuit and the public dimension of allegations within BCO 29/31 process; bears on policing public allegations as offenses. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p892)
- **[2024-2 — Gleason v. Houston Metro Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-02.md)** (GA52/2025, dismissed) — Holds that charging a *court* (session/committee) with a ninth-commandment violation is a category error. Directly cautions against O46's reach to public allegations against "a church, Presbytery, agency, committee." ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p971)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI 30-29 Item 3** (GA30/2002) — CCB advice on a session's right to records, limited "by prudence and protection of reputation," citing WLC 145 — the only corpus inquiry construing the 9th-commandment / good-name duty O46 invokes; bears marginally on the catechetical basis. [page](../inquiries/ga30_2002__ci08.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA28 O24](../overtures/ga28_2000__o24.md)** (2000, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO to Address Improper Dissemination of Judicial Case Information." The closest prior attempt to amend the BCO to restrain public statements about church judicial matters; failed. [page](../markdown/ga28_2000.md#ga28-p51)
- **[GA48 O32](../overtures/ga48_2021__o32.md)** (2021, Answered in the negative) — "Form Ad Interim Committee to Study Biblical Ethics in Digital Media," driven by "growing concern... regarding online gossip and slander." Same real-world friction (public/social-media allegations) O46 addresses; the study-committee route failed. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1060)
- **[GA48 O43](../overtures/ga48_2021__o43.md)** (2021, Answered in the negative) — Identical "Biblical Ethics in Digital Media" study-committee overture from Hills and Plains; answered in the negative with O32. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1087)
- **[GA49 O18](../overtures/ga49_2022__o18.md)** (2022) — "Amend RAO 3-2 to Add Stated Clerk Responsibility for Processing Allegations." Recent, adjacent reform on how allegations against the church are formally channeled rather than aired publicly. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1320)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
BCO 29-5 is a **new** provision, so the deterministic provision-join returned empty cases/inquiries/overtures/RPR; every action above is a TOPICAL supplement found by concept search (ninth commandment, slander, public statement, court of original jurisdiction) in the corpus index. No chapter-29 renumbering applies (bco_renumberings.jsonl shows no chapter-29 entry), so no old-number search was needed. Structural caveat: BCO 29 presently governs "the parties in cases of process," so inserting a substantive *offense* at 29-5 is a placement mismatch worth flagging. **Pruned as incidental** (cite the 9th commandment / WLC 144 only in passing for unrelated subjects): cases 1998-9 Baer (pastoral discipline), 2011-2 Gonzales (committee-member immunity), 2012-7 Mitchell (promise-keeping / session minutes); and overtures GA22 O40/O45 (legal audits), GA26 O11/O22 (IRC dispute), GA30 O27 (Scripture–Constitution conflict procedure), GA51 O6 (background checks). A prior-pass reference to "GA17 Burkhart/McCready" 9th-commandment specifications was dropped — no verifiable corpus deep-link exists for it. Judgment call: Dudt (2021-13) and Gleason (2024-2) are the strongest cautionary data points against the overture's breadth. Routed to CCB and OC; no companion GA53 overture on this topic identified.

---

## O47 — Amend RAO 8-4.i to Require Floor Nominations Come from Previously Submitted Presbytery Nominees
**Targets:** RAO 8-4.i · **Source:** Suncoast FL · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-47_SuncoastFL_RAO8-4.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-47_SuncoastFL_RAO8-4.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a sentence to RAO 8-4.i providing that a floor ("additional") nomination for a Permanent Committee or Agency "shall only be considered valid if the individual nominated was previously submitted by a Presbytery for consideration by the Nominating Committee but was not included in the Committee's final report." Preserves the Assembly's right to elect someone other than the Nominating Committee's slate while routing all candidates through prior presbytery review.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None. (Rationale 4 analogizes restricted floor nominations to a minority report, but cites no specific case, overture, or inquiry.)

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **GA47 CCB II.I** (47th GA, 2019) — CCB review of Northern New England's Overture 12 to amend RAO 8-4 restricting floor nominations; found "not in conflict" and adopted by the CCB. Bears directly: prior CCB treatment of a near-identical change to the same rule. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci09.md)
- **GA49 CCB III** (49th GA, 2022) — CCB advised Tennessee Valley's proposed RAO 8-4 amendment (Overture 32) was "in order and not in conflict." Bears: prior CCB construction of amending the RAO 8-4 nomination machinery. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci26.md)
- **GA49 Supplemental III.2** (49th GA, 2022) — CCB held floor nominations (for Stated Clerk) follow the same procedure as other contested offices and nominees must be examined; construes RAO 8-4 with RAO 3-4/4-9. Bears on the existing floor-nomination regime O47 would tighten. [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci30.md)
- **GA52 Supplemental II.2** (52nd GA, 2025) — CCB ruled floor nominations are permitted under RAO 3-4 even when no committee nominee is brought; expressly cites RAO 8-4.i. Bears: the most recent reading of the floor-nomination right O47 narrows. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci35.md)
- **GA50 CCB II.O** (50th GA, 2023) — CCB found amending RAO 8-4.h/17-1/19-2 to specify when minority reports are permitted "not in conflict." Bears on O47's Rationale 4 (floor-nomination-as-minority-report analogy). [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci15.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA47 O12](../overtures/ga47_2019__o12.md)** (2019, Answered in the negative) — "Amend RAO 8-4 to Restrict Floor Nominations for GA Committees and Agencies" (Northern New England). The closest prior attempt at O47's change to the same rule; declined. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p616)
- **[GA49 O32](../overtures/ga49_2022__o32.md)** (2022, Answered in the negative) — "Amend RAO 8.4 to Add Board-Recommended Nominees to GA Nominating Committee Report" (Tennessee Valley). Prior attempt to alter the RAO 8-4 nomination process; declined. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1352)
- **[GA50 O22](../overtures/ga50_2023__o22.md)** (2023, Answered in the negative) — "Amend RAO 8-4.h, 17-1 & 19-2 to Specify When Minority Reports Are Permitted" (Session of First Pres., Montgomery). Recent attempt to amend the same RAO 8-4 article; bears on O47's minority-report analogy. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1077)
- **[GA21 O19](../overtures/ga21_1993__o19.md)** (1993, Answered in the negative) — "Amend BCO 14-1 to Limit Floor Nominations to Presbytery-Nominated Candidates" (Covenant). Earliest corpus attempt at O47's exact concept (floor nominees must be presbytery-submitted); declined. [page](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p55)
- **[GA31 O4](../overtures/ga31_2003__o4.md)** (2003, Adopted) — "Amend Floor Nomination and Election Process" (James River). The one adopted reform of the floor-nomination machinery; bears as the established baseline O47 would amend. [page](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p63)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
The deterministic spine is provision-EXACT on "8-4" and produced two kinds of noise, PRUNED here: (1) all 21 RPR rows are for **BCO 8-4** (annual reports of TEs laboring out of bounds) — an unrelated provision, none bear on RAO floor nominations. (2) The spine's prior_overtures listed **GA47 O12 = "Reaffirm the GA's Original Statement on Abortion"** via a loose body+title match; that is wrong — the genuine GA47 O12 is the floor-nomination overture, recovered via the topical supplement (search "floor nomination"/"RAO 8-4" in /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md), which also surfaced GA49 O32, GA21 O19, and GA31 O4 that the exact join missed. The GA47/GA49 CCB-advice items in the spine are the CCB counterparts of GA47 O12 / GA49 O32. No renumbering applies (RAO numbering stable for these articles). Companion GA53 cross-link: O47 is substantively near-identical to **O45** (Covenant; same operative sentence and resulting RAO 8-4.i text, O45 adds one extra rationale point) and sits alongside the other GA53 RAO 8-4.i overtures **O8** (nomination deadline) and **O9** (proportionate presbytery representation).
