## O48 — Amend BCO 7-2 and 7-3 Regarding Commissioning and Titling of Unordained Persons
**Targets:** BCO 7-2, 7-3 · **Source:** NWGA (Northwest Georgia Presbytery) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-48_NWGA_7.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-48_NWGA_7.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 7-2 to add that, because the offices are open to men only, "it is unlawful for any court to commission or otherwise appoint, or for a congregation to elect or otherwise approve, a woman as a deaconess, shepherdess, or any other pretended office," and amends BCO 7-3 to bar giving unordained persons "other titles which by their nature imply the authority of those offices." It further declares such women's-leadership practices an irregularity subject to review and control of higher courts under BCO 40-3.

**Cites in its own grounds:** No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by number. Grounds rest on Scripture (1 Tim 3:1-13; Titus 1:5-16) and on BCO provisions: 7-2, 7-3, 17-2, 21-7, 24-6 (laying on of hands), 20-3, 24-1, 9-7 (election/appointment), and 40-3 (review and control).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **38-34 II.E** (GA38/2010) — CCB found an overture appointing unordained men and women to diaconal ministry roles **in conflict** with the Constitution, partly because it implied an unordained office contrary to BCO 17-1; bears directly on the "pretended office" concern in O48's 7-2 amendment. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci04.md)
- **II.Q** (GA47/2019) — CCB found an overture letting individual sessions decide locally whether women may serve as deacons **not in conflict** (BCO 7-2, 9-3); the opposite policy O48 forecloses, showing the CCB has treated the question as one the Assembly may resolve either way. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci17.md)
- **II.S** (GA50/2023) — CCB found no constitutional conflict in amending BCO 7-3 to regulate titling of unordained persons (adopted 6-1-1); the direct precedent for the 7-3 half of O48, and the very amendment O48 now extends. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci19.md)
- **II.J** (GA51/2024) — CCB found an overture restricting BCO 7-2 ordination to biological males **not in conflict** (adopted 8-0-0); the direct precedent that further substantive restrictions to 7-2 are constitutionally permissible. [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci10.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA36 O9](../overtures/ga36_2008__o9.md)** (2008, Answered in the negative) — Erect Ad Interim Study Committee on Deaconesses; an earlier, declined attempt to take up the deaconess question O48 addresses directly. [page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p205)
- **[GA36 O19](../overtures/ga36_2008__o19.md)** (2008, Answered by reference) — Decline to Elect Study Committee on Deaconesses; the counter-overture to O9, framing the same dispute. [page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p212)
- **[GA38 O2](../overtures/ga38_2010__o2.md)** (2010, Central Carolina) — Amend BCO 9-7 to Prohibit Deaconesses; a prior attempt at the same substantive restriction O48 now places in BCO 7-2. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p386)
- **[GA38 O9](../overtures/ga38_2010__o9.md)** (2010, Eastern Carolina) — Revise BCO 9-7 to Prohibit Commissioning Assistants to Deacons as Office Bearers; bears on the "commission or otherwise appoint" language in O48's 7-2 amendment. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p387)
- **[GA38 O13](../overtures/ga38_2010__o13.md)** (2010, Westminster) — Prohibit Electing or Installing Assistants to Deacons as Church Office Bearers; same cluster of restricting unordained diaconal service. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p389)
- **[GA50 O26](../overtures/ga50_2023__o26.md)** (2023, Northwest Georgia — **Approved & ratified 2024**) — Amend BCO 7-3 to Prohibit Ecclesiastical Titles for Unordained People; the exact predecessor amendment from the same presbytery that O48 now builds upon and extends. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1036)
- **[GA51 O15](../overtures/ga51_2024__o15.md)** (2024, West End PCA Session — Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 7-2 to Specify Ordination for Biological Males Only; the most recent attempt to add restrictive language to BCO 7-2 (CCB-cleared but failed on the floor), the closest companion to O48's 7-2 amendment. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1277)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 7-2** — 10 citations across the corpus; recurring real-world friction over women in office (e.g., Korean Southern, "office of Kwansa (translated 'eldress') is not recognized by BCO 7-2," 24th/1996, unsatisfactory; "Ordination of women as deaconesses not provided for in PCA Constitution," 34th/2006; "Church appoints women officers with no response from presbytery," 51st/2024). Demonstrates the persistent enforcement gap O48 targets. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 7-3** — 1 citation ([Korean Southwest](../rpr/korean-southwest.md), 52nd/2025, raised/open) regarding presbytery delinquency on a member-church report; marginal to titling but shows 7-3 is now live in review. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Companion to **[GA50 O26](../overtures/ga50_2023__o26.md)** (same presbytery, ratified 2024) — O48 is the next step in NWGA's program: O26 restricted *titles* in 7-3; O48 closes the *commissioning/electing* gap in 7-2 and broadens 7-3 to titles that "imply the authority" of office. No renumbering affects BCO chapter 7. Pruned as incidental spine hits: the GA12/1984 "serious accusations" case, GA29/2001 "The John Wood Matter" (both provision-exact but with no case page and no construction of the office-gender/titling question), and GA50/2023 case 2022-20 *Wilson v. Pacific Northwest Presbytery* (BCO 7-2 cited twice in a dissenting opinion as an analogy — "the church privilege to be nominated and elected an officer is suspended on the condition of being male (BCO 7-2; 24-1)" — in a case whose actual holding is about minor communicant voting rights, not unordained women's roles or titling); inquiry 12-53 (ordination of men who *believe* women may be deacons — a candidate-exception question, not the practice O48 bars), inquiry 23-43 (creation/male-office candidate exceptions), inquiry App. O III GA42 and CCB II.G GA45 (both 24-7 commissioner/sabbatical mechanics, incidental to 7-2). Also pruned numerous body+title overture matches unrelated to office/titling (Memorial Service, Freemasonry, BCO 46-5, RAO 9-4, BCO 27-46 judicial rules, RAO 4-21.d enrollment, the empty GA51 O32) and overtures touching deacon/elder mechanics but not the women's-office or titling question (GA14 O36 diaconal scope, GA15 O35 "Reverend," GA24 O2 committee voting, GA26 O12 deacon vows, GA30 O14 BCO 24-1, GA42 O22 third ordination vow, GA45 O8 dual office, GA46 O4 RE composition).

---

## O49 — Amend BCO 13-1 and 14-2 to Increase Ruling Elder Representation at Presbytery and GA
**Targets:** BCO 13-1, 14-2 · **Source:** Northwest Georgia Presbytery · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-49_NWGA_RE-Representation.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-49_NWGA_RE-Representation.pdf)

**What it does:** Raises each congregation's ruling-elder allotment from two to three RE representatives for the first 350 communing members in both presbytery (BCO 13-1) and General Assembly (BCO 14-2), keeping the existing "one additional RE per 500 members" tier. Aim: reverse the decline in RE participation (cited at ~20-30% of GA vs. 54% in 1973) without new mandated expense.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (cites BCO 7-1 on two-office parity and a 2018 byFaith article on RE participation; no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries by number).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. *(The provision spine returned 16 cases citing BCO 13-1/14-2, but all are incidental — quorum, geographic bounds, membership, and disciplinary disputes that cite these chapters in passing. None construes the RE-representation allotment this overture changes. Pruned; see Note.)*

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **47-II.A** (GA47/2019) — CCB found a prior Northwest Georgia Presbytery overture revising BCO 14-2 to permit additional RE representation at GA was **not in conflict** and adopted it; the single most on-point precedent — same presbytery, same goal, same provision. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci01.md)
- **31-56 VI** (GA31/2003) — CCB found an overture restricting presbytery/GA voting to pastors **in conflict** with BCO 3-1 and 14-2 (all TEs entitled to representation); construes the representation entitlement structure of 14-2. [page](../inquiries/ga31_2003__ci09.md)
- **32-40 II.D** (GA32/2004) — CCB reaffirmed the prior year's holding that limiting TE voting to pastors conflicts with BCO 3-1/14-2; bears on the parity/representation logic underlying this overture. [page](../inquiries/ga32_2004__ci04.md)
- **35-30 II.H** (GA35/2007) — CCB found an overture conditioning presbytery voting on church financial contributions **not in conflict** with BCO 13-1/14-2 (minority dissent); directly construes who is entitled to representation in the higher courts. [page](../inquiries/ga35_2007__ci03.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA47 O1](../overtures/ga47_2019__o1.md)** (2019, Approved → sent to presbyteries; ratification not located) — Northwest Georgia Presbytery: amend BCO 14-2 to permit additional RE representation at GA. Same presbytery and same objective as O49; the immediate predecessor effort. [p.583](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p581), [p.762](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p760)
- **[GA29 O21](../overtures/ga29_2001__o21.md)** (2001, Approved & ratified 2002) — Ellisville PC: amend BCO 13-1 to allow two REs per congregation in presbytery; this is the amendment that set the current "two (2)" number O49 now raises to three. [p.144](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p142)
- **[GA28 O18](../overtures/ga28_2000__o18.md)** (2000, Answered in the negative) — Ellisville PC: amend BCO 13-1 to allow additional RE commissioners; prior attempt at the same change, declined the year before GA29 succeeded. [p.53](../markdown/ga28_2000.md#ga28-p51), [p.287](../markdown/ga28_2000.md#ga28-p285)
- **[GA20 O11](../overtures/ga20_1992__o11.md)** (1992, Answered in the negative) — Western Carolina: amend BCO 13-1 & 14-2 to permit all REs to serve; same two-provision target, broader version of O49's aim. [p.59](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p57), [p.105](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p103)
- **[GA18 O1](../overtures/ga18_1990__o1.md)** (1990, Approved & ratified 1991) — Susquehanna Valley: amend BCO 14-2 to increase RE participation at GA; an earlier successful expansion of RE representation. [p.73](../markdown/ga18_1990.md#ga18-p71)
- **[GA14 O20](../overtures/ga14_1986__o20.md)** (1986, Approved → sent to presbyteries; ratification not located) — Westminster: amend BCO 14-2 to increase RE representation at GA; near-identical title and aim. [p.76](../markdown/ga14_1986.md#ga14-p76)
- **[GA11 O25](../overtures/ga11_1983__o25.md)** (1983, Answered in the negative) — Great Lakes: amend BCO 13-1 to equalize RE and TE attendance at presbytery; prior attempt at the presbytery-level half of O49. [p.47](../markdown/ga11_1983.md#ga11-p47)
- **[GA10 O9](../overtures/ga10_1982__o9.md)** (1982, Answered by reference) — Siouxlands: amend BCO 14-2 to require equal TE/RE representation; the earliest of the recurring parity overtures O49 continues. [p.44](../markdown/ga10_1982.md#ga10-p44)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 13-1** — 15 RPR citations; most directly: [Korean Northeastern](../rpr/exc/korean-northeastern__001.md) (42nd/2014) "more RE representation present from one church than allowed by BCO," and [South Texas](../rpr/south-texas.md) (51st/2024) flagging a sub-350-member church with three or more RE commissioners present — real-world friction over exactly the per-congregation RE cap O49 would raise. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
**Companion/lineage:** O49 is the latest in a long line of RE-representation overtures and the direct successor to Northwest Georgia's own GA47 O1 (2019). The current "two (2)" figure in BCO 13-1 was itself set by GA29 O21 (ratified 2002) — O49 simply raises that number to three and conforms 14-2 to match. **CCB precedent is favorable on constitutionality:** 47-II.A and 35-30 II.H both found representation-expansion/eligibility overtures not in conflict, while 31-56/32-40 only struck attempts to *restrict* (not expand) elder representation — so no constitutional bar to O49 appears in the record. **Pruning:** all 16 spine cases were dropped as incidental — the provision pair (13-1/14-2) is cited across quorum, geographic-bounds, membership, and discipline disputes, but none adjudicates the RE allotment count. Numerous additional 14-2 parity/delegated-assembly overtures from GA12–GA16 (e.g. GA13 O20, GA15 O20, GA16 O7) were pruned as restructuring efforts rather than simple allotment increases. **RPR caveat:** the join's "RAO 14-2" rows (8) concern commissioner *election* procedure under the RAO, not BCO 14-2, and were excluded. **Renumbering:** BCO 13 and 14 have not been renumbered; the old-number search was not needed.

---

## O50 — Call for a Day of Fasting and Prayer for Revival and Renewal of the Church
**Targets:** (prayer — non-provision overture) · **Source:** Mississippi Valley Presbytery (to OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-50_MSValley_DayOfPrayer.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-50_MSValley_DayOfPrayer.pdf)

**What it does:** Overtures the 53rd GA to call all PCA presbyteries to appoint a day during September 2026 for a solemn fast and prayer for the revival and renewal of the church, concluding in a convocation of praise, preaching, and prayer; empowers the Moderator to appoint a TE and RE to prepare prayer guidance; and invites NAPARC sister churches and like-minded evangelical churches to join.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (the whereas clauses cite only Scripture — John 4:35, Matt. 9:38, Acts 4:24-31, etc.; no prior GA actions, cases, or inquiries).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (Non-provision overture — it amends no constitutional text, so the deterministic provision-join returns no judicial actions.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found. (No inquiry or CCB advice bears on a denomination-wide call to fasting; the join produced no provision-exact hits and a topical scan of INQUIRIES.md and CCB-OVERTURE-ADVICE.md found nothing on point.)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA44 O32](../overtures/ga44_2016__o32.md)** (2016, Referred) — "Call Member Churches to a Day of Prayer and Fasting," from James River Presbytery, also routed to the Overtures Committee. This is the closest precedent: a near-identical denomination-wide call to fasting and prayer, and the GA's most recent disposition of such a request (referred rather than adopted). [p.634](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p632), [p.743](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p741)
- **[GA03 O20](../overtures/ga03_1975__o20.md)** (1975, Adopted) — "Call for a Day of Prayer and Fasting on July 4, 1976," from Grace Presbytery. Establishes that the GA has previously adopted exactly this kind of churchwide fast-and-prayer call, the strongest favorable precedent for the requested action. [p.32](../markdown/ga03_1975.md#ga03-p32)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (Non-provision overture — no BCO provision is targeted, so there are no Records-of-Presbytery exceptions to cite.)

### Note
The deterministic spine returned provisions=[] (non-provision/prayer overture), so all bearing actions come from a topical concept scan of /workspace/index/OVERTURES.md, INQUIRIES.md, and CCB-OVERTURE-ADVICE.md. I kept the two prior overtures that match the genre precisely — a churchwide call to **fasting and prayer** (GA44 O32 referred; GA03 O20 adopted). I pruned the many issue-specific "Day of Prayer" calls the topical scan surfaced but that do not bear on a general revival-and-renewal fast: GA02 O1 and GA22 O25 (prayer tied to missions strategy), GA14 O49 / GA15 O49 (Midwest farm crisis), GA22 O34 (Korean peninsula peace), GA24 O39 (pre-election prayer watch), and the repentance/racial-reconciliation *statement* overtures (GA32 O20, GA44 O16/O34) — a different instrument (a standing statement, not an appointed fast). No renumbering caveat applies (no provision). No companion GA53 overture on this topic was found.

## O51 — Amend BCO 5 to add a Section on 'Assisted Churches'
**Targets:** BCO 5 (new 5-11) · **Source:** MS Valley · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-51_MSValley_5-11.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-51_MSValley_5-11.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a new Section C to BCO Chapter 5 (paras 5-11.a–c) creating a third church category — the "Assisted Church": a church with only one ruling elder and no pastor that has been assigned a BCO 15-1 commission to serve as a temporary Session (cf. BCO 5-3.c). Presbytery must acknowledge the condition, choose among courses of action (train more ruling elders, or recommend dissolution/merger/reorganization under BCO 13-9.f), and review the church's status at least annually.

**Cites in its own grounds:** Cross-references BCO 15-1, BCO 5-3.c, and BCO 13-9.f in the proposed text, and appeals to the BCO Preliminary Principles. No prior case, overture, or inquiry cited by number.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (The provision-exact join returned no cases for new BCO 5-11. A concept search surfaced cases that cite Chapter 5 — e.g. Session of Hope Community Church v. Central Carolina (2013-4) on multi-site particularization, and Gordon v. Southern New England (2020-6) on inter-denominational excommunication — but neither concerns a session-less or declining church, so both are incidental and pruned.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **App. O II.E / 39-CI** (GA39/2011) — "Temporary governance for churches lacking ruling elders": CCB found a New Jersey overture on temporary governance for elder-less churches *may have been in conflict* with BCO Preliminary Principles 2 & 6 and BCO 12-1 if read as prescriptive. The single most on-point action — a prior attempt at exactly O51's idea, and a drafting-caution flag for O51's mandatory presbytery duties. [page](../inquiries/ga39_2011__ci01.md)
- **App. O II.G / 44-CI** (GA44/2016) — CCB found a mission-church minute-reporting overture in conflict with BCO 5-3.a because an evangelist, unlike a governing body, has no minutes to submit — construes the Chapter 5 temporary-government machinery O51 extends. [page](../inquiries/ga44_2016__ci02.md)
- **CI #15 / 14-86** (GA14/1986) — Whether a congregation may dissolve its session: CCB advised it cannot, but Presbytery may assume jurisdiction under BCO 13-9 — bears on Presbytery's authority over a church lacking a functioning governing body, the gap O51 fills. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci18.md)
- **16-77 III** (GA16/1988) — Membership status and session authority upon dissolution of a congregation — the downstream of O51's 5-11.b(2) dissolution/reorganization path. [page](../inquiries/ga16_1988__ci08.md)
- **II.H / 51-CI** (GA51/2024) — CCB found Overture 10 (add Presbytery care for TEs to BCO 13-9) not in conflict — recent CCB treatment of the BCO 13-9 care obligations O51 invokes via 13-9.f. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci08.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA41 O2](../overtures/ga41_2013__o2.md)** (2013, Referred) — North Texas, "Amend BCO 5-1, 5-2, 5-9 and Add Sections 5-11 and 5-12 Regarding Mission Churches" — a direct prior attempt to add a new BCO 5-11 (the very slot O51 uses); did not pass. [page](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p816)
- **[GA42 O2](../overtures/ga42_2014__o2.md)** (2014, Out of order) — North Texas, the re-filed attempt to add new 5-11, 5-12 re Mission Churches; ruled out of order. [page](../markdown/ga42_2014.md#ga42-p253)
- **[GA38 O15](../overtures/ga38_2010__o15.md)** (2010, Approved & ratified 2011) — Potomac, "Revise BCO 5-2 Through 5-11 and Add New BCO 5-5 Regarding Church Organization" — the last major BCO 5 restructuring; defines the current 5-2…5-11 framework (and today's 5-11 endpoint) O51 amends. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p368)
- **[GA38 O11](../overtures/ga38_2010__o11.md)** (2010, Approved & ratified 2011) — "Amend BCO 5-3 to Allow Latitude in Oversight of Mission Churches" — shaped the temporary-government framework (BCO 5-3) O51 builds on. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p356)
- **[GA44 O38](../overtures/ga44_2016__o38.md)** (2016, Approved & ratified 2017) — "Amend BCO 5-3 to Require Minute Reporting for Mission Church Governments" — most recent successful Chapter 5 amendment on session-substitute governments; the companion to the GA44 CCB advice above. [page](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p638)
- **[GA30 O25](../overtures/ga30_2002__o25.md)** (2002) — Ascension, "Revise BCO 12-2, Add 12-11, Revise 25-6 & 15-1 Regarding Non-Functioning Sessions" — closest structural analog: prior machinery for churches whose session cannot function, the same problem O51 addresses. [page](../markdown/ga30_2002.md#ga30-p76)
- **[GA09 O1](../overtures/ga09_1981__o1.md)** (1981, Answered by reference) — Covenant, "Amend BCO 5-2 to Clarify Presbytery Oversight of Unorganized Congregations" — earliest attempt to define Presbytery oversight outside the mission/particular binary. [page](../markdown/ga09_1981.md#ga09-p41)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 5-3** — 18 citations; recurring Presbytery-review exceptions for failing to provide a temporary government to churches lacking a session (e.g. [Northern Illinois](../rpr/northern-illinois.md) 18th/1990, which used none of the three lawful methods; [Providence](../rpr/providence.md) 52nd/2025) — the real-world friction O51's new category targets. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 5-3.c** — 4 citations, all recent ([New Jersey](../rpr/exc/new-jersey__039.md) 51st/2024; [New River](../rpr/new-river.md), [Rio Grande](../rpr/rio-grande.md), [Siouxlands](../rpr/siouxlands.md) all 52nd/2025), several describing commissions/temporary sessions with as few as one TE and one RE for a session-less church — almost exactly O51's "assisted church" fact pattern, evidencing live confusion. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
The provision-exact join was empty because BCO 5-11 is a *new* section (no past action can cite a provision that does not yet exist), so this page rests on the topical supplement. Renumbering caveat: Chapter 5 was renumbered at GA38/2011 (new 5-5 inserted, sections shifted +1; see bco_renumberings.jsonl), so the GA41/GA42 "Add Sections 5-11, 5-12" overtures use post-2011 numbering and are genuine prior attempts to occupy the very slot O51 now seeks; GA38 O15 is the renumbering that fixed today's 5-11 endpoint. Pruning: the only cases surfaced concern multi-site particularization and inter-denominational discipline, not a session-less/declining church, and were dropped as incidental. Strongest bearing actions are GA39 App. O II.E (a prior near-identical idea, flagged as possibly in conflict) and the BCO 5-3.c RPR cluster (GA51–52). Companion: O51 cross-references BCO 15-1 and 13-9.f — check GA53 overtures touching those chapters for cross-links.

---

## O52 — Add BCO 7-4 Prohibiting the Creation of Ecclesiastical Offices
**Targets:** BCO 7-4 (new) · **Source:** MS Valley · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-52_MSValley_7-4.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-52_MSValley_7-4.pdf)

**What it does:** Inserts a new BCO 7-4 that, while permitting courts to use qualified unordained men and women in a variety of ministry positions, bars church courts from creating ecclesiastical offices, vesting any part of the ordained-officer power in an unordained person, or intruding such persons upon the church or its members' consciences by popular election or by vows not mandated by the Word and the Constitution.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by number). Grounds rest on WCF 1.6, BCO Preface I, BCO 3-1 and 3-2, BCO Preliminary Principle 7, and WCF 20.2.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2009-25 / 2009-26 — Brown v. Northern California Presbytery; Session of Grace PC v. Northern California Presbytery](../cases/ga39_2011__2009-25_2009-26.md)** (M39GA/2011, sustained 20-0) — Directly on point: presbytery had adopted an abstract resolution permitting six diaconal "views/practices" (including unordained "deaconesses" and the "nobody ordained" view); the SJC annulled it, and the concurrence set the GUMP/Kniseley standard for when unordained diaconal practice crosses into a de facto office — the exact line O52 seeks to codify. [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p548)
- **[2007-13 — Kniseley v. Rocky Mountain Presbytery](../cases/ga37_2009__2007-13.md)** (M37GA/2009) — The standard-setting case on commissioning unordained diaconal assistants; bears on what counts as impermissibly vesting officer-power in unordained persons. [minutes](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p555)
- **[2008-01 / 2008-10 — Crossroads Community Church Session & Grasso v. Philadelphia Presbytery](../cases/ga37_2009__2008-01_2008-10.md)** (M37GA/2009, denied) — Licensure/ordination of a man holding the "nobody ordained" diaconal view; part of the same diaconal-office line and shows the practical friction O52 addresses. [minutes](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p554)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CCB 38-34 II.A** (M38GA/2010, in conflict) — Overture to prohibit deaconesses found in conflict because "deaconess" need not denote an ordained office; bears on the line between unordained service and a created office. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci02.md)
- **CCB 38-34 II.D** (M38GA/2010, in conflict) — Overture prohibiting commissioned/installed assistants to deacons found in conflict on the same grounds; directly relevant to "commissioning" unordained helpers. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci03.md)
- **CCB 38-34 II.E** (M38GA/2010, in conflict) — Overture appointing unordained persons to diaconal ministry found in conflict, in part because it implied an unordained office contrary to BCO 17-1 — the precise hazard O52 names. [page](../inquiries/ga38_2010__ci04.md)
- **CCB App. O II.H** (M46GA/2018, in conflict) — Grace Presbytery's deaconess/women-officer overture found in conflict; CCB held the session (not the congregation) is the appointing body requiring vows, invoking Preliminary Principle 7 — the same authorities and the popular-election/vows concern O52 raises. [page](../inquiries/ga46_2018__ci04.md)
- **CCB II.Q** (M47GA/2019, not in conflict) — Overture letting local sessions decide whether women may serve as deacons was found not in conflict; a counterpoint on how far courts may go in shaping unordained service. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci17.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA50 O26](../overtures/ga50_2023__o26.md)** (2023, Approved & ratified 2024) — Amend BCO 7-3 to prohibit ecclesiastical titles for unordained people; closest companion — the immediately prior, successful effort to fence the unordained/office boundary in ch. 7. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1028)
- **[GA46 O9](../overtures/ga46_2018__o9.md)** (2018, Approved → presbyteries; ratification not located) — Amend BCO 9-7 / add BCO 24-11 re women serving as deaconesses; a prior attempt to regulate the unordained-diaconal boundary. [page](../markdown/ga46_2018.md#ga46-p684)
- **[GA45 O8](../overtures/ga45_2017__o8.md)** (2017, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 7 to prohibit simultaneous service in both elder and deacon offices; bears on shaping office structure via ch. 7. [page](../markdown/ga45_2017.md#ga45-p656)
- **[GA38 O2](../overtures/ga38_2010__o2.md)** (2010) — Amend BCO 9-7 to prohibit deaconesses; the legislative companion to CCB 38-34 above, same office-creation question. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p386)
- **[GA38 O16](../overtures/ga38_2010__o16.md)** (2010) — Affirm the permissibility of unordained deaconesses in the PCA; the opposing prior overture on the same question. [page](../markdown/ga38_2010.md#ga38-p390)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 9-3 (deaconess commissioning)** — Recurring exceptions for diaconates including women "commissioned contrary to BCO 9-3" ([Northern California](../rpr/northern-california.md), 35th/2007 through 40th/2012; [Philadelphia](../rpr/exc/philadelphia__028.md), 35th/2007) — genuine real-world friction over courts creating/commissioning an unordained office, exactly what O52 targets. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 7-2 (women in an unrecognized office) — Korean Southern, a 30-year unresolved thread.** First cited as the office of "[Kwansa (translated 'eldress') not recognized by BCO 7-2](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__006.md)" (raised 23rd/1995, found unsatisfactory 24th/1996); the presbytery filed no response and the GA directed it forward to the 25th, leaving it **unsatisfactory/outstanding**. The same concern recurred — recast as "ordination of women as deaconesses not provided for in the Constitution (BCO 9-3; 7-2)" — at the [30th/2002](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__042.md), [31st/2003](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__054.md), [32nd/2004](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__064.md), and [34th/2006](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__084.md), each left unsatisfactory/outstanding for nearly a decade. It was first resolved satisfactorily at the [40th→41st (2012–13)](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__103.md) ("men and women appointed as deacons") and again at the [51st→52nd (2024–25)](../rpr/exc/korean-southern__176.md) ("church appoints women officers, no presbytery response"). That long arc — a court tolerating an office the Constitution does not provide — is precisely the hazard O52 targets. [full Korean Southern record](../rpr/korean-southern.md) · [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
The deterministic spine returned provisions=[BCO 7-4] with zero cases/inquiries/RPR and only two prior overtures — both PRUNED as incidental: GA23 O15 ("confine doctrinal requirements") and GA50 O9 (sexuality disqualification) cite the EXISTING BCO 7 / current 7-4 (officer qualifications), a different question from O52's office-creation prohibition. O52 inserts a NEW 7-4, so no past action cites this provision text; all bearing material is therefore TOPICAL — the diaconal-office / unordained-service line (cases, CCB advice, deaconess overtures, RPR). Also pruned: SJC 2023-22 (Suh — jurisdiction/membership, not office creation) and inquiry 12-53/ci09 (about a candidate's view on women deacons, not court-created office). No renumbering applies (7-4 is genuinely new). Companion GA53 overtures touching ch. 7 (titling/commissioning of unordained ministry) may cross-reference; O52's grounds are constitutional-principle based rather than case-based.

---

## O53 — Amend RAO 16 to Prohibit Members of RPR from Participating in GA Debate on the RPR Report
**Targets:** RAO 16 (new 16-12) · **Source:** Great Lakes Presbytery (to CCB, OC) · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-53_GreatLakes_RAO16.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-53_GreatLakes_RAO16.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a new RAO 16-12 barring a member of the Committee on Review of Presbytery Records (RPR) from participating in floor debate when the RPR report is presented, unless he is the chairman's designee for a particular recommendation or is presenting a minority report; the restriction may be lifted for a given member on a particular recommendation by a non-debatable majority-vote motion.

**Cites in its own grounds:** RAO 16-7 (RPR minority-report right) and RAO 15-8.f (the parallel debate restriction already imposed on Overtures Committee members). No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (The spine is provision-empty — RAO 16 is not a BCO provision, so the join returned no cases. Topical search of CASES.md found only the administrative citation series re: review of Gulfstream/Korean Central records, which concerns record-review discipline, not GA floor procedure — incidental, pruned. No SJC case construes a committee member's right to floor debate.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **29-28 III.7** (GA29/2001, advice given) — CCB advised that the CRPR may make any recommendation within its RAO 16 purview to the GA; bears on the scope of the RPR's role in presenting to the Assembly, which O53 would procedurally constrain on the floor. [page](../inquiries/ga29_2001__ci07.md)
- **52 Second Supplemental II.A** (GA52/2025, not in conflict, 6-0-0) — CCB found CRPR Recommendation 9 adding a new RAO 16-11 not in constitutional conflict; bears directly as the most recent CCB review of a new section being added to RAO 16 — the same structural move O53 makes (adding 16-12). ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci36.md)
- **52 II.W (23)** (GA52/2025, in conflict, 8-0-0) — CCB found an overture amending RAO 16 (statistical reporting) to conflict with the BCO; bears as a recent precedent that RAO 16 amendments are screened for BCO conflict — relevant to how CCB will treat O53. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci23.md)
- **52 III.A (29)** (GA52/2025, adopted 8-0-0) — CCB ruled all RAO amendments require CCB review (RAO 8-2.b.3); bears on the procedural track for O53 (referred to CCB, OC). ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci29.md)
- **49 Supplemental II.B** (GA49/2022, not in conflict) — CCB found RPR's proposed change to RAO 16-4c not in conflict; bears as a recent RPR-driven RAO 16 amendment review. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci28.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA52 O34](../overtures/ga52_2025__o34.md)** (2025, Adopted final) — Amend RAO 16 to require reporting on session/diaconate membership; bears as the most recent overture amending the very rule O53 targets. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1270)
- **[GA51 O28](../overtures/ga51_2024__o28.md)** (2024) — Amend RAO 16-6.c.1 to eliminate conflict with BCO 40-5; bears as a recent presbytery overture amending RAO 16. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1180)
- **[GA48 O9](../overtures/ga48_2021__o9.md)** (2021, Adopted final) — Amend RAO 15-6.s on the number of members required to file an Overtures Committee minority report; bears closely because it tunes the same RAO 15 committee-report/minority-report machinery O53 invokes by analogy (RAO 15-8.f, minority-report carve-out). ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p965)
- **[GA48 O10](../overtures/ga48_2021__o10.md)** (2021, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 15-6.s to regulate the content of Overtures Committee minority reports; bears as a parallel (failed) attempt to constrain committee members' floor presentations. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p967)
- **[GA50 O22](../overtures/ga50_2023__o22.md)** (2023, Answered in the negative) — Amend RAO 8-4.h/17-1/19-2 to specify when minority reports are permitted; bears on when committee members may bring differences to the floor — the same tension O53 addresses for RPR. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1019)
- **[GA37 O2](../overtures/ga37_2009__o2.md)** (2009, Adopted final) — Amend RAO 19-4.d, 14-9.h, 15-8.g governing debate on minority reports; bears as the closest prior action directly regulating floor debate on committee reports and minority reports (incl. RAO 15-8, the model rule O53 copies). [page](../markdown/ga37_2009.md#ga37-p57)

### RPR exceptions
None found. (O53 governs GA floor procedure for the RPR committee, not presbytery-record compliance; the RPR-exceptions corpus catalogs exceptions issued by RPR under RAO 16-3.e.5 etc. — RPR's product, not real-world friction with O53's debate restriction.) [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Non-provision (RAO) overture: the deterministic spine returned provisions=[] and zero cases/inquiries/overtures, so every citation here comes from topical search of the index. Two strands bear: (1) prior amendments to RAO 16 itself (GA52 O34, GA51 O28; CCB advice 49 Supp II.B, 52 Second Supp II.A, 52 II.W, 29-28 III.7); and (2) the floor-debate / minority-report machinery O53 copies from the Overtures Committee (RAO 15-8.f), best illuminated by GA48 O9/O10, GA50 O22, and GA37 O2. **GA53 companions for the committee:** O7 (PNW, Amend RAO 16 re RPR reporting on presbytery records) and O33 (Westminster, Amend RAO 16-7.h re minority reports from RPR) — O33 is closely related since O53 expressly preserves the RAO 16-7 minority-report exception. O53 is the only one of the three targeting floor-debate participation (new 16-12) rather than reporting content or minority-report mechanics. The Gulfstream administrative-citation case was pruned as incidental; no SJC case bears, so Judicial cases is None found.

## O54 — Amend BCO 42-2 to Clarify that a Person Judged Contumacious has the Right of Complaint Not Appeal
**Targets:** BCO 42-2 · **Source:** Hills and Plains Presbytery · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-54_HP_42-2.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-54_HP_42-2.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a sentence to BCO 42-2 providing that "If the court has dealt with the party as contumacious, the party may not appeal but may complain against the court," so an appellate court cannot rehear an entire case where the trial court never reached judgment (BCO 32-15) because it found the accused contumacious.

**Cites in its own grounds:** No case numbers or overture numbers are named, but the rationale describes "a recent case" in which an SJC panel treated a BCO 43 complaint from a Session-found-contumacious accused as a BCO 42 appeal and reheard the case — this is **Gozé v. Hills and Plains Presbytery (2024-10)**, the overturing presbytery's own case. It also relies on BCO 42-1, 32-15, 32-6, and 34-3 for the definition of appeal/judgment/contumacy.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-10 — Gozé v. Hills and Plains Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-10.md)** (52nd/2025, dismissed) — The "recent case" the overture's rationale describes: the trial court found the appellant contumacious and suspended him from the sacraments; his later appeal was dismissed as untimely (BCO 42-4). The overture seeks to foreclose treating such a contumacy disposition as an appealable "judgment." ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1013)
- **[2019-10/2019-12 — Evans and Pitts et al. v. Arizona Presbytery](../cases/ga48_2021__2019-10_2019-12.md)** (48th/2021, sustained) — The SJC itself observed that "to avoid confusion in the future, perhaps BCO 38-1 and 42-2 could be amended," directly seeding the GA48 amendment lineage that this overture continues. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p788)
- **[2002-17 — Appeal of TE Sung K. Kim vs. Korean Capital Presbytery](../cases/ga32_2004__2002-17.md)** (32nd/2004, dismissed) — Held that Kim, found guilty of contumacy without submitting to a regular trial, was not "entitled to an Appeal" under BCO 42-2 — the very rule the overture codifies. [minutes](../markdown/ga32_2004.md#ga32-p105)
- **[1997-11 — Raymond Larsen vs. Pacific Presbytery (Appeal)](../cases/ga26_1998__1997-11.md)** (26th/1998, administratively out of order) — Held the appeal out of order because Larsen was deposed for contumacy (failure to appear for trial); cites BCO 42-2 that only those who submitted to a regular trial are entitled to appeal. Squarely on the appeal-entitlement question. [minutes](../markdown/ga26_1998.md#ga26-p146)
- **[1993-10 — Clark v. Southwest Presbytery](../cases/ga23_1995__1993-10.md)** (23rd/1995, not sustained) — Construes contumacy where there was no trial on the original indictment (the court conceded "there was no trial on the original indictment") — the exact procedural posture the overture targets. [minutes](../markdown/ga23_1995.md#ga23-p102)
- **[2015-11 — Thompson v. South Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga44_2016__2015-11.md)** (44th/2016, sustained) — Heavy treatment of contumacy and the complaint mechanism in a case without process (excommunication imposed, complaints routed through Session and Presbytery), bearing on the appeal-vs-complaint distinction. [minutes](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p541)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.L** (48th/2021, not in conflict; Adopted) — CCB advice on the overture amending BCO 38-1 and 42-2 to allow appeal of a censure in a case without process; directly construes the appeal-entitlement clause of 42-2 this overture edits. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci12.md)
- **II.X** (48th/2021, not in conflict; Adopted) — Companion CCB advice on the BCO 38-1/42-2 cluster (confession timing in cases without process); bears on the same without-process/appeal architecture. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci24.md)
- **Supplemental II.A** (49th/2022, not in conflict; Adopted by the CCB) — Held over the seven discipline/appeals overtures (incl. 2021-19) touching BCO 38-1 and 42-2 from GA48 to GA49; confirms the recency of the 42-2 appeal-rights revisions. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci27.md)
- **App. O II.E** (43rd/2015, in conflict) — Found a reporting-mandate overture in conflict because new BCO 34-10 language conflicted with BCO 42-2; touches 42-2 but on the divestiture/reporting question, not contumacy — peripheral. [page](../inquiries/ga43_2015__ci02.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA48 O19](../overtures/ga48_2021__o19.md)** (2021) — "Amend BCO 38-1 and 42-2 to Allow Appeal of Censure in a Case Without Process" (Pacific Northwest Presbytery) — the immediately prior amendment to the same sentence of 42-2; O54 adds the contumacy clause to the text O19 produced. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p991)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
The exact-provision spine returned 18 case hits on BCO 42-2; I pruned 12 as incidental — cases that cite 42-2 in passing or for a different clause. Notably **2011-13 (Spann)** quotes 42-2 for the appeal-routing rule ("An appeal cannot be made to any court other than the next higher"), unrelated to contumacy; and **1997-13, 2002-5, 2003-3, 2004-4, 2004-6, 2009-28 (Ruff), 2010-3, 2015-10**, the **GA35 p.90** stub, and the **1993-5** administrative clarification stub surfaced no contumacy/appeal-entitlement holding (several have a null case_page, minutes-only). The six retained cases all construe the contumacy → appeal-entitlement question or the appeal-vs-complaint distinction. No renumbering affects chapter 42 (checked bco_renumberings.jsonl). Companion lineage: GA48 O19 (and CCB II.L/II.X, held over per CI Supplemental II.A) last revised this sentence; O54 is the next iteration, prompted by the overturing presbytery's own SJC loss in Gozé (2024-10).

## O55 — Amend BCO 22-3 and 23-1 Concerning the Tenure of Assistant Pastors
**Targets:** BCO 22-3, 23-1 · **Source:** SW Florida · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-55_SWFlorida_22-1.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-55_SWFlorida_22-1.pdf)

**What it does:** Caps an assistant pastor's initial call at five years, after which the Session must put him forward to the congregation as an associate pastor or he is automatically released; extraordinary circumstances permit three-year renewals by 2/3 Presbytery vote. It amends BCO 23-1 to add a corresponding dissolution trigger requiring Presbytery to dissolve the call if an assistant is neither advanced nor granted an extension.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (relies on Preliminary Principle 6 and cross-references to BCO 12-4, 13-2, 20-1, 22-4; no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2024-5 — Bigelow v. North Florida Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-05.md)** (GA52/2025, granted) — only spine hit citing BOTH 22-3 and 23-1; bears directly on the assistant-pastor call/dissolution interface this overture rewires. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p983)
- **[1992-2 — Roberts v. New River Presbytery](../cases/ga20_1992__1992-02.md)** (GA21/1993, sustained) — construes BCO 23-1 dissolution-of-pastoral-relation procedure, the chapter the overture amends. [minutes](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p201)
- **[2002-2 / 2002-3 — Nichols & Couch v. James River Presbytery](../cases/ga30_2002__2002-02_2002-03.md)** (GA33/2005, sustained / sustained in part) — leading SJC construction of BCO 23-1 pastoral-relation dissolution. [minutes](../markdown/ga33_2005.md#ga33-p74)

(Pruned as incidental: Pre-SJC GA12 referrals (../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p290); 1991-2 Nickoley & Stephens (../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p144); 1992-5 (../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p212); 31-3 out-of-order (../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p229); 2001-34 (../markdown/ga33_2005.md#ga33-p79); 2015-12 Wills (../cases/ga44_2016__2015-12.md); 2022-20 Wilson (../cases/ga50_2023__2022-20.md); 2023-11 Psiaki (../cases/ga51_2024__2023-11.md); 2023-7 Evans (../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p815); 2024-1 Moehn (../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p951); 2024-2 Gleason (../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p971) — these cite 23-1 only for generic dissolution/jurisdiction procedure, not assistant-pastor tenure.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI #13** (GA14/1986, advice given) — call of an assistant pastor; touches BCO 22-3, 22-4, 23-1 — the cluster the overture restructures. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci16.md)
- **17-82 III,17** (GA17/1989, advice given) — Tennessee Valley asked how the then-new BCO 22-3/22-4 Assistant Pastor provisions applied; directly on assistant-pastor status. [page](../inquiries/ga17_1989__ci03.md)
- **33-29 II.C** (GA33/2005, in conflict) — CCB held an overture detailing how assistant pastors are called conflicted with BCO 3-2/12-2–12-4 because the assistant-to-congregation relationship is "best left to the session"; cautionary precedent for this overture's mandated advancement-or-release scheme. [page](../inquiries/ga33_2005__ci02.md)
- **II.D** (GA47/2019, not in conflict; Adopted by the CCB) — CCB found the overture amending BCO 23-1 on procedures for dissolving various pastoral relations not in conflict; establishes that 23-1 dissolution-procedure amendments can pass constitutional scrutiny — a counterpoint to the two "in conflict" findings below. [page](../inquiries/ga47_2019__ci04.md)
- **49 II.A** (GA49/2022, in conflict; adopted by CCB) — CCB found an overture amending BCO 22-3 (assistant pastor standing) in conflict with the BCO; recent CCB read of the same provision. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga49_2022__ci01.md)
- **51 II.Y** (GA51/2024, not in conflict; adopted 8-0-0) — CCB cleared an amendment to BCO 23-1 (exit interview before dissolution); recent CCB treatment of the dissolution provision being amended here. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci25.md)
- **52 II.S** (GA52/2025, in conflict and ambiguous; adopted 8-0-0) — CCB found amendments to BCO 23-1 (and others) on calling/dissolution of TE relations in conflict and ambiguous; most recent CCB scrutiny of 23-1 amendments. ⭐ [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci19.md)

(Pruned as incidental: 16-77 III,27 (../inquiries/ga16_1988__ci07.md) — non-PCA-church jurisdiction; 23-15 II,Ref.1 (../inquiries/ga23_1995__ci01.md) and 26-68 (../inquiries/ga26_1998__ci02.md) — congregational-vote/severance mechanics under 23-1, not assistant tenure.)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA49 O2](../overtures/ga49_2022__o2.md)** (2022) — Amend BCO 22-3 to Allow Assistant Pastors to File Complaints Against Sessions; prior attempt to amend the very provision (22-3), found in conflict by CCB (49 II.A). ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1286)
- **[GA51 O30](../overtures/ga51_2024__o30.md)** (2024, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 23-1 to Require Presbytery Exit Interview Before Dissolution of Call; recent failed attempt to amend 23-1's dissolution procedure. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1183)
- **[GA47 O5](../overtures/ga47_2019__o5.md)** (2019, Approved → sent to presbyteries) — Amend BCO 23-1 on Procedures for Dissolving Various Pastoral Relations; most recent GA-level amendment effort on 23-1. [page](../markdown/ga47_2019.md#ga47-p593)
- **[GA29 O4](../overtures/ga29_2001__o4.md)** (2001, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO to Change Procedure for Dissolving Pastoral Relationships; prior attempt to alter the 23-1 dissolution machinery. [page](../markdown/ga29_2001.md#ga29-p139)
- **[GA12 O4](../overtures/ga12_1984__o4.md)** (1985, Approved & ratified) — Amend BCO 23-1 to Allow Associate Pastor to Succeed Senior Pastor by Presbytery Exception — from SW Florida's predecessor (Southern Florida); enacted the 4/5-congregation / 3/4-Presbytery succession-exception language this overture preserves verbatim. [page](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p49)
- **[GA10 O16](../overtures/ga10_1982__o16.md)** (1983, Approved & ratified) — Amend BCO 23-1 to Require Presbytery Approval Before Minister Leaves Pastoral Field; original source of the "must not physically leave the field" clause retained in the amended text. [page](../markdown/ga10_1982.md#ga10-p47)
- **GA12 O29 / O49** (1984) — Delmarva and West Hopewell Session overtures on associate pastors succeeding senior pastors; companion attempts in the same cycle on 23-1 succession. [O29](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p54) · [O49](../markdown/ga12_1984.md#ga12-p62)

(Pruned as incidental: GA16 O3 (../markdown/ga16_1988.md#ga16-p76) — presbytery boundary expansion, a title/body false match; GA49 O6 (../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p1290) — BCO 31-10/33-4 suspensions, unrelated.)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 22-3** — 6 citations; e.g. [North Texas](../rpr/exc/north-texas__015.md) 32nd (2004) no record of receiving a call from a session / approval of a call from presbytery; [Georgia Foothills](../rpr/exc/georgia-foothills__053.md) 52nd (2025, open) TE appointed to assistant pastor without record of receiving a call; [Korean Capital](../rpr/exc/korean-capital__108.md) 52nd (2025, open) call changed from Assistant to Associate without record. Live friction on assistant-pastor call mechanics the overture would further regulate. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 23-1** — 308 citations spanning 19th (1991) through 52nd (2025), overwhelmingly "no record of congregational meeting / concurrence in dissolution of pastoral relation" (e.g. Pacific Northwest 1994; South Texas 2002; Nashville 2025, open). Documents chronic, denomination-wide difficulty following 23-1's existing dissolution procedure — the procedure this overture adds a new mandatory trigger to. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
Companion GA53 caveat: this overture pairs a substantive 22-3 tenure cap with a conforming 23-1 dissolution trigger; cross-check other GA53 overtures touching BCO 22 or 23. No chapter renumbering applies (BCO 22 and 23 retain their historic numbers). Pruning: the BCO 23-1 spine is extremely high-recall — 11 of 17 cases and 3 of 5 inquiries cite 23-1 only for generic pastoral-relation dissolution or congregational-vote mechanics, not the assistant-pastor tenure question this overture creates, so they are pruned above; kept actions construe assistant-pastor status (22-3 cluster) or the 23-1 dissolution/succession machinery the overture rewrites. Judgment call: 33-29 II.C and 49 II.A are the most pointed warnings — CCB has twice resisted GA-level micromanagement of the assistant-pastor/session relationship, precisely what an automatic five-year advance-or-release rule does.

---

## O56 — Amend BCO 32-19 to Limit Representation in Judicial Process to Officers
**Targets:** BCO 32-19 · **Source:** SW Florida · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-56_SWFlorida_32-19.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-56_SWFlorida_32-19.pdf)

**What it does:** Partially rolls back the 2025 amendment to BCO 32-19: a non-officer member may still represent an accused before a Session, but at every higher court (Presbytery, SJC, General Assembly) the representative must be a church officer in good standing, on the rationale that representatives function as officers of the court and should carry ordination's vetting.

**Cites in its own grounds:** The 2025 General Assembly amendment to BCO 32-19 (the change it seeks to refine) — i.e., GA51 O26 from Tennessee Valley Presbytery, approved and ratified in 2025. No prior judicial cases or inquiries are cited by name.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[1993-10 — Clark v. Southwest Presbytery](../cases/ga23_1995__1993-10.md)** (GA23/1995, not_sustained) — directly construes 32-19 on representation/counsel, holding that 32-19 does not require a Presbytery to appoint counsel for an accused; bears on how the representation right operates in practice. [minutes](../markdown/ga23_1995.md#ga23-p102)
- **[2021-13 — Dudt v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2021-13.md)** (GA49/2022, sustained) — turns in part on who may represent the accused at trial under 32-19; concrete real-world friction over the representation rule O56 would tighten. [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p909)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **GA51 II.U (CI21)** (GA51/2024, not in conflict; Adopted 8-0-0) — CCB advice on Tennessee Valley O26, the very 2025 amendment broadening representation that O56 now seeks to narrow; the single most directly bearing prior action. [page](../inquiries/ga51_2024__ci21.md)
- **GA50 II.G (CI07)** (GA50/2023, in conflict; Adopted 8-0-0) — CCB found Northern New England O10's 32-19 professional-counsel amendment in conflict with the BCO; bears on the chapter's representation/counsel scheme. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci07.md)
- **GA50 II.J (CI10)** (GA50/2023, in conflict; Adopted 8-0-0) — CCB found Northern California O14's 32-19 professional-counsel amendment in conflict; parallel attempt to adjust who may participate as counsel/representative. [page](../inquiries/ga50_2023__ci10.md)
- **GA48 II.S (CI19)** (GA48/2021, in conflict at multiple points; Adopted) — CCB advice on a discipline-procedure overture touching BCO 31-2 and 32-19; bears more loosely on the disciplinary-process framework. [page](../inquiries/ga48_2021__ci19.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA51 O26](../overtures/ga51_2024__o26.md)** (2025, Approved & ratified) — Tennessee Valley: "Amend BCO 32-19 to Expand Representation of Accused Before Church Courts" — the enacted amendment O56 explicitly seeks to refine/reverse. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1271)
- **[GA50 O10](../overtures/ga50_2023__o10.md)** (2023) — Northern New England: "Amend BCO 32-19 to Clarify Use of Professional Counsel in Cases of Process" — prior attempt to adjust 32-19 representation/counsel. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p984)
- **[GA50 O14](../overtures/ga50_2023__o14.md)** (2023) — Northern California: "Amend BCO 32-19 Regarding Use of Professional Counsel in Cases of Process" — companion 2023 attempt on the same provision. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1076)
- **[GA48 O35](../overtures/ga48_2021__o35.md)** (2021) — Pacific Northwest: "Amend BCO 38-1 to Guarantee Right to Counsel in Cases Without Process" — related right-to-counsel reform in the disciplinary chapters. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p1064)
- **[GA46 O3](../overtures/ga46_2018__o3.md)** (2018, Approved but not ratified) — South Florida: "Amend BCO 32-19 to Allow Counsel by Any Communing Member in All Courts" — earlier, broader version of the 2025 expansion; shows the long arc of this debate. [page](../markdown/ga46_2018.md#ga46-p673)
- **[GA28 O5](../overtures/ga28_2000__o5.md)** (2000, Answered in the negative) — Louisiana: "Amend BCO 32-19 to Clarify Use of Counsel in Cases of Process" — oldest attempt to amend this exact provision. [page](../markdown/ga28_2000.md#ga28-p295)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
O56 is a direct counter-move to **[GA51 O26](../overtures/ga51_2024__o26.md)** (ratified 2025) — read the two together; the spine's exact-provision join surfaces this cleanly. Pruned as incidental the following 32-19 case hits that lack a full case page and cite 32-19 only in passing (representation noted, not construed as the holding): 1993-5 (Clark clarification, administrative), 1999-6 (Shive), 2012-4 and 2013-1 (Dunn/Pesnell), 2007-2 (Malone), 2019-3 (Crouse), 2020-4 (Marusich), 2020-7 (Wilbourne), 2020-9 (Ozbalt) — mostly GA48–49 SJC dispositions where 32-19 appears in the procedural record rather than the reasoning. Also pruned prior-overture spine hits matched only by incidental body text on unrelated subjects: GA28 O4 (presbytery division), GA46 O23 (BCO 35-11 court members as witnesses), GA48 O28 (BCO 31-2 investigation sequence), GA50 O23 (BCO 8-2/9-3 chastity standards). No renumbering applies to BCO chapter 32. No RPR exception in the corpus cites 32-19.

---

## O57 — Amend BCO 12-7, 13-9, and 25-5 to Require Minutes of Congregational Meetings in Session Records
**Targets:** BCO 12-7, 13-9, 25-5 · **Source:** South Texas · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-57_SouthTexas_CongregationalMtgs.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-57_SouthTexas_CongregationalMtgs.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 12-7, 13-9.b, and 25-5 to make explicit that the minutes of congregational meetings are part of the records of the church Session — kept by the congregational clerk, sent to the Session, and submitted to Presbytery for annual review — codifying what the CCB has held to be true only "by implication."

**Cites in its own grounds:** SJC Case 2021-12 (Michelson v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery), M49GA 2022, 822–825 at 823 — quoted for the holding that a Presbytery "could take note of a Constitutional deficiency in a congregational meeting in their review of the records of the Session (note BCO 25-5, last sentence and BCO 13-9(b))"; and the CCB non-judicial reference that could only say congregational records "must be maintained" by implication (the GA52 2025 IV.B advice below). Grounds also cite BCO 25-11, 25, 20, 24.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2021-12 — Michelson v. Northwest Georgia Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2021-12.md)** (GA49/2022, dismissed) — The overture's own anchor case: holds a Presbytery may note a constitutional deficiency in a congregational meeting when reviewing Session records (BCO 25-5 last sentence + 13-9.b). Directly construes all three target provisions together. ⭐ [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p839)
- **[2004-7 — Session of First Presbyterian Augusta v. Savannah River Presbytery](../cases/ga33_2005__2004-07.md)** (GA33/2005, sustained) — Real-world friction over the conduct and minutes of a congregational meeting (Session adding docket items / recommending a course of action); the only spine case construing BCO 25-5 on congregational-meeting proceedings. [minutes](../markdown/ga33_2005.md#ga33-p140)
- **[2023-06/2023-08 — Baird et al. v. Grace Presbytery](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p796)** (GA51/2024, sustained) — Cites BCO 12-7 + 13-9 on the Presbytery's duty to review Session records and redress what is contrary to order. [minutes](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p796)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **IV.B** (GA52/2025) — The non-judicial reference (Platte Valley) the overture cites: CCB ruled congregational meeting minutes ARE part of Session records subject to Presbytery review and must be submitted if required (BCO 25-5, 40, 41-3) — but only by implication, which is the gap O57 closes. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci32.md)
- **34-34 IV.C** (GA34/2006) — CCB advice on what Session records a Presbytery may review and require (language/translation), under BCO 12-7, 13-9b, 40-2; bears on the content and scope of the annual records review. [page](../inquiries/ga34_2006__ci04.md)
- **CI #17** (GA14/1986) — CCB advised a Presbytery must review ALL previously unreviewed Session records (BCO 13-9, 40-1..40-4), reinforcing the mandatory, comprehensive review O57 expands. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci19.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA44 O38](../overtures/ga44_2016__o38.md)** (2016, Approved & ratified 2017) — Pacific Northwest Presbytery amended BCO 5-3 to require minute reporting for mission-church governments; the closest structural precedent for adding an explicit minute-keeping/reporting duty to the BCO. [page](../markdown/ga44_2016.md#ga44-p638)
- **[GA51 O10](../overtures/ga51_2024__o10.md)** (2024, Answered in the negative) — Metro Atlanta Presbytery's attempt to amend BCO 13-9 (add Presbytery TE care); a recent, failed effort to amend the same provision, useful as a drafting/disposition cautionary precedent. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p1270)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 12-7** — 13 citations; repeated exceptions for Presbyteries failing to review/record Session minutes within the year (e.g., [South Texas](../rpr/south-texas.md) 18th/1990; [Hills and Plains](../rpr/hills-and-plains.md) 50th/2023). Shows chronic real-world friction in the very review process O57 would extend to congregational minutes. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)
- **BCO 13-9** — 33 citations; the largest block is "no record of review of records of church Sessions" (e.g., [North Florida](../rpr/north-florida.md) 52nd/2025; [Korean Southwest](../rpr/korean-southwest.md) 52nd/2025), confirming ongoing difficulty completing and documenting Session-records review. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
BCO 12-7, 13-9, and 25-5 are not renumbered (no entries in bco_renumberings.jsonl), so old-number searching is unnecessary. The spine is high-recall on BCO 13-9 — a provision enumerating nearly all of a Presbytery's powers — so the great majority of its ~50 case hits (church dissolution/dismissal, TE care, original jurisdiction, commissions, Korean-presbytery governance disputes, the Wilkins/Federal Vision cases) merely cite 13-9 in passing and were PRUNED as incidental; only actions touching review of Session/congregational records or the conduct/minutes of congregational meetings are kept (Michelson, First Pres Augusta, Baird). Likewise the prior-overture hits matched by title/body keyword on 13-9 concern dissolving/dismissing churches and TE care, not records — pruned except GA44 O38 (analogous minute-reporting amendment) and GA51 O10 (recent failed 13-9 amendment). The CCB advice items on BCO 7 / 8-7 / 17 / 41 (ordination, chaplains, venue) were pruned as unrelated. O57 is essentially the legislative sequel to the GA52 IV.B Platte Valley reference and the Michelson holding it quotes; cross-check any GA53 overture also amending BCO 25 or the records-review duty for a companion link. Pruned as incidental: 2022-22 Turner v. South Florida Presbytery — BCO 12-7 appears only in the factual timeline (Clerk submitted minutes "as required by BCO 12-7"); BCO 13-9(e)/(f) cited as Presbytery's remedial powers in a case whose actual holding is that BCO 40-6 requires formal process before censuring a Session; neither provision is construed on the records-review mechanism O57 targets.

---

## O58 — Amend BCO 10-4 to Specify that Clerks Must Be Elders
**Targets:** BCO 10-4 · **Source:** Calvary · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-58_Calvary_10-4.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-58_Calvary_10-4.pdf)

**What it does:** Adds a sentence to BCO 10-4 — "The clerk shall be a Ruling or Teaching Elder within the Presbyterian Church in America" — so that all court clerks (Session, Presbytery, GA) must be ordained elders.

**Cites in its own grounds:** None. The grounds cite only BCO provisions (12-1, 13-1, 35-8, 8-9, 7-2), RAO 3-5.a (GA Stated Clerk must be a TE or RE), and the PCA *Handbook for Clerks of Session* — no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found. (See Note — all seven spine cases cite 10-4 only for the records / extracts-as-evidence function, not the elder-qualification of clerks; pruned as incidental.)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
None found. (See Note — both spine inquiries construe the stated clerk's records/dissemination *duties*, not who may serve as clerk; pruned as incidental.)

### Prior overtures
None found. (See Note — the one spine match, GA50 O20 on electronic records, does not bear on clerk eligibility.)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 10-4** — 2 citations, both records/election-keeping rather than eligibility: Heritage (28th, 2000) re a complaint referenced in minutes but missing from the appendix; Southern New England (33rd, 2005) re "no record of election of stated clerk" (self-rectified). Bears only weakly, in that it confirms presbyteries formally elect a stated clerk under 10-4; neither touches the elder-qualification question. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
BCO 10-4 packs two distinct subjects into one section: (a) the election and qualification of clerks — what O58 changes — and (b) the clerk's duty to preserve records and grant extracts that serve as evidence. The provision-exact join is high-recall but every action it returns construes subject (b), not (a). Pruned judicial cases: 2001-6 and 2002-1 (RE Kim v. Korean Eastern, [minutes](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p96) / [minutes](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p114)); 2010-18 and 2010-20 ([Review of Presbytery Records citations](../cases/ga39_2011__2010-18_2010-19_2010-20_2010-21_2010-22_2010-23.md), [minutes](../markdown/ga39_2011.md#ga39-p603)); 2011-7 (PCA v. Warrior, [minutes](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p563)); 2012-10 ([PCA v. Korean Capital](../cases/ga41_2013__2012-10.md), [minutes](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p618)); 2012-5 (Hedman v. Pacific Northwest, [minutes](../markdown/ga41_2013.md#ga41-p585)) — all about records, citations, or extract evidence. Pruned inquiries: 17-82 III ([certificate of dismissal must bear the stated clerk's signature](../inquiries/ga17_1989__ci01.md)) and App. O IV.B ([scope of the stated clerk's duty to disseminate information](../inquiries/ga44_2016__ci05.md)) — both on the clerk's duties, not eligibility. Pruned overture: GA50 O20 ([electronic records research](../markdown/ga50_2023.md#ga50-p1015)), unrelated. No bearing actions survive: the corpus contains no case, inquiry, or prior overture construing whether a court clerk must be an ordained elder. The overture rests on RAO 3-5.a (already requiring the GA Stated Clerk to be a TE/RE), which O58 would extend down to all courts. No renumbering affects BCO chapter 10 (10-4 has been stable). Topical search of clerk-related overtures surfaced only RAO / Stated-Clerk-of-GA term and commendation overtures, none bearing on the elder-eligibility of court clerks.

---

## O59 — Amend BCO 38-3.a to Recognize the Non-Punitive Removal of Individuals from Membership Roll
**Targets:** BCO 38-3.a · **Source:** Calvary Presbytery · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-59_Calvary_38-3.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-59_Calvary_38-3.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 38-3.a so a member or officer in good standing may withdraw non-punitively either by affiliating with another branch of the visible Church (BCO 2-2) **or by communicating his intent** to do so — recording the irregularity, acknowledging "his new membership or intentions," and removing his name from the roll. This closes the current gap whereby, unless the person names an actual new membership, the only available tools are the punitive/disciplinary routes of 38-3.b and 38-4. It retains the original-jurisdiction court's option to keep the name on the roll and conduct any pending investigation (BCO 31-2) or charges (BCO 32-3).

**Cites in its own grounds:** None (the grounds cite only BCO provisions — 2-2, 31-2, 32-3, 38-3, 38-4 — no prior cases, overtures, or inquiries).

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
- **[2019-6 — Presbyterian Church in America v. Presbytery of the Mississippi Valley](../cases/ga48_2021__2019-06.md)** (GA48/2021, sustained) — ⭐ Construes a presbytery's BCO 38-3 duties when a minister withdraws to another body; the General Assembly itself prosecuted the presbytery's handling of the withdrawal, directly framing the question O59 reaches. [minutes](../markdown/ga48_2021.md#ga48-p718)
- **[2020-12 — Speck v. Missouri Presbytery](../cases/ga49_2022__2020-12.md)** (GA49/2022, sustained) — ⭐ Turns on whether/how a court must record and dispose of a member's status under BCO 38-3 when withdrawal coincides with pending matters — the very "investigation in process / charges" branch O59 rewrites. [minutes](../markdown/ga49_2022.md#ga49-p747)
- **[2023-7 — Evans v. Arizona Presbytery](../cases/ga51_2024__2023-07.md)** (GA51/2024, granted) — ⭐ Construes BCO 38-3 procedure for removal from the roll; bears on the mechanics O59 amends. [minutes](../markdown/ga51_2024.md#ga51-p815)
- **[2024-1 — Moehn v. Westminster Presbytery](../cases/ga52_2025__2024-01.md)** (GA52/2025, sustained) — ⭐ Recent SJC construction of BCO 38-3 in a withdrawal/erasure context. [minutes](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p951)
- **[Morse v. Covenant Presbytery (1992-3)](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p156)** (GA20/1992, denied) — Early construction of BCO 38-3 as applied to a minister's withdrawal/erasure; shows the long-standing question of non-punitive removal the overture targets. [minutes](../markdown/ga20_1992.md#ga20-p156)

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **CI #3** (GA14/1986) — Declining case-specific questions, the CCB laid out the three BCO routes for removing members from the rolls (transfer, discipline, relocation) under BCO 38-3 et al.; O59 argues a fourth, non-punitive, intent-based route is missing. [page](../inquiries/ga14_1986__ci08.md)
- **15-83 III, 8** (GA15/1987) — Advised that releasing a minister to an independent church is handled by **erasure under BCO 38-3**, the precise non-punitive-vs-disciplinary tension O59 addresses. [page](../inquiries/ga15_1987__ci02.md)
- **25-22 IV, 1** (GA25/1997) — CCB drafted amended BCO 38-3 language for roll removal when a member joins another church, with options for retaining/removing names when charges are pending — a direct prior drafting effort on the same text and the same "charges pending" branch O59 rewrites. [page](../inquiries/ga25_1997__ci03.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA21 O14](../overtures/ga21_1993__o14.md)** (1993, Referred) — Amend BCO 38-3 to clarify discipline of members joining other churches (Potomac); a prior attempt on the same provision and same withdrawal scenario. [page](../markdown/ga21_1993.md#ga21-p126)
- **[GA24 O26](../overtures/ga24_1996__o26.md)** (1996, Referred) — Amend BCO 38-3 regarding **renouncing church membership** (Potomac); prior attempt at the withdrawal question. [page](../markdown/ga24_1996.md#ga24-p310)
- **[GA24 O27](../overtures/ga24_1996__o27.md)** (1996, Approved & ratified 1997) — Delete BCO 46-5 & amend BCO 38 and 46-2 (Potomac); a successful amendment to the BCO 38 roll-removal framework. [page](../markdown/ga24_1996.md#ga24-p296)
- **[GA25 O6](../overtures/ga25_1997__o6.md)** (1997, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 38-3 regarding **renunciation of communion** (Northeast); the closest prior attempt to recognize non-punitive withdrawal, defeated. [page](../markdown/ga25_1997.md#ga25-p129)
- **[GA36 O3](../overtures/ga36_2008__o3.md)** (2008, Answered by reference) — Amend BCO 38-3a, 46-5, 46-6, 57-5 re transfers of church membership (Southeast Alabama); prior attempt on 38-3.a itself. [page](../markdown/ga36_2008.md#ga36-p284)
- **[GA40 O33](../overtures/ga40_2012__o33.md)** (2012, Answered in the negative) — Amend BCO 38-3a, BCO 46, remove BCO 57-6 re church-membership administration (Southeast Alabama); prior attempt on the same subsection, defeated. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p733)

### RPR exceptions
- **BCO 38-3** — 22 RPR citations, heavily clustered at recent assemblies (GA48–52, 2021–2025), almost all of the form "no record that presbytery made the determinations required by BCO 38-3" when a minister withdrew to another denomination — e.g. [Covenant](../rpr/covenant.md) (51st/2024, unsatisfactory), [Korean Southwest Orange County](../rpr/korean-southwest-orange-county.md) (51st/2024, outstanding), [Northern California](../rpr/northern-california.md) (51st/2024, outstanding), [Wisconsin](../rpr/wisconsin.md) (50th–52nd), [Pee Dee](../rpr/pee-dee.md) and [South Florida](../rpr/south-florida.md) (52nd/2025). This recurring presbytery confusion over how to remove a withdrawing minister non-punitively is the strongest real-world evidence of the friction O59 seeks to cure. [by provision](../index/RPR-BY-PROVISION.md)

### Note
The spine is provision-exact on BCO 38-3 (no renumbering applies to 38-3; no companion GA53 overture targets this subsection). I pruned several incidental spine cases that cite BCO 38-3 only in passing or in unrelated disciplinary/appellate postures: the 1987 North Texas/North Dallas administrative report, JC 31-3 (out of order), the GA35 (2007) out-of-order decision, JC 2005-2 and 2007-8 (both dismissed), Doty v. Nashville (2016-8, dismissed), Gendy v. Central Florida (2019-13), Eagle (2020-10) and Eudaly/Light (2021-5, both administrative), and the BCO 34-1/Wilson petitions (2022-12, 2022-20, dismissed) — none construe the non-punitive-withdrawal mechanism O59 amends. I also pruned inquiries 27-43 III, 36-30 II.C, 37-29 IV.3, and App. O II.T, which touch BCO 38-3 only tangentially (appeal-vs-complaint wording, profession-of-faith subscription, BCO 2-2 investigative duty) rather than the roll-removal-on-withdrawal question. Note the repeated, defeated Potomac/Northeast/Southeast Alabama attempts (GA21–GA40) to amend exactly this text: O59 enters a long and previously unsuccessful line of overtures on non-punitive withdrawal, which the committee will likely weigh.

---

## O60 — Amend BCO 58-5 to Specify that Only Men Lawfully Ordained Shall Distribute the Elements
**Targets:** BCO 58-5 · **Source:** Calvary · **PDF:** [https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-60_Calvary_58-5.pdf](https://pcaga.org/wp-content/uploads/2026/02/Overture-60_Calvary_58-5.pdf)

**What it does:** Amends BCO 58-5 to add that "Only men lawfully ordained as elders or deacons (when there is not a sufficient number of elders present) shall assist the officiating minister in the distribution (or serving, as distinct from merely passing) of the elements," grounding the restriction in the keys of the kingdom given to ordained elders (Matt. 16:19; BCO 3-2; 12-5.a).

**Cites in its own grounds:** No prior cases, overtures, or inquiries cited by number. Grounds rest on WCF 29.3; WLC 169, 173, 176; WCF 30.1-4; the Scots Confession of 1560 (Ch. 22); Scripture; and BCO 30-3, 12-5.a, 57, 3-2, 58-5.

### Judicial cases (SJC/CJB)
None found.

### Constitutional inquiries / CCB advice
- **II.H** (52nd GA/2025) — "Restricting distribution of the Lord's Supper to ordained officers": the CCB found the proposed BCO 58-5 amendment limiting Lord's Supper distribution to officers **not in conflict** with the Constitution, adopted 8-0-0. This is the same substantive change O60 re-files; the CCB's prior clearance directly governs its constitutionality. [page](../inquiries/ga52_2025__ci08.md)

### Prior overtures
- **[GA52 O12](../overtures/ga52_2025__o12.md)** (2025, Approved but not ratified) — Providence Presbytery, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Restrict Distribution of Lord's Supper to Officers." The immediate prior attempt at the identical change: it passed the Assembly but failed presbytery ratification. O60 is effectively a re-filing. ⭐ [page](../markdown/ga52_2025.md#ga52-p1189)
- **[GA40 O30](../overtures/ga40_2012__o30.md)** (2012, Approved but not ratified) — Savannah River Presbytery, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Prohibit Intinction." Analogous attempt to restrict the *manner* of distributing the Supper via 58-5 that the Assembly approved but the presbyteries did not ratify — bears on the difficulty of amending this rubric's distribution practice. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p88)
- **[GA40 O29](../overtures/ga40_2012__o29.md)** (2012, Answered by reference) — Savannah River Presbytery, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Prohibit the Practice of Intinction," the companion overture answered by reference to O30. Part of the same prior effort to constrain 58-5 communion practice. [page](../markdown/ga40_2012.md#ga40-p88)
- **[GA31 O21](../overtures/ga31_2003__o21.md)** (2003, Approved & ratified 2004) — Ascension Presbytery, "Amend BCO 58-5 to Delete 'Broken' in Communion Liturgy." Bears as precedent that 58-5 has been successfully amended on the substance of how the Supper is served. [page](../markdown/ga31_2003.md#ga31-p65)

### RPR exceptions
None found.

### Note
O60 is substantively a re-filing of **[GA52 O12](../overtures/ga52_2025__o12.md)** (Providence), which the CCB cleared as not-in-conflict (GA52 II.H) and the Assembly approved but the presbyteries did not ratify — the central bearing context. **Pruned as incidental:** the exact-provision spine also returned three 58-5 amendments on unrelated content — GA7 O22 (Christ's eternal deity in membership vow 2), GA18 O14 ("wine" → "fruit of the vine"), GA29 O2 (leavened bread) — and Inquiry 6-111 III (reaffirmation of faith for membership, GA6/1978). These share the section number but do not construe *who may distribute the elements*, so they are dropped. The GA40 intinction overtures are retained as analogous "restrict communion practice via 58-5, approved-but-not-ratified" attempts. No SJC/CJB case and no RPR exception in the corpus cites BCO 58-5.
